# Progress Log — goal AST front-end rewrite

## Codebase Patterns
- Derive lowering has THREE engines that must move in lockstep on field-matching
  and output-var rules (found US-023): the backend emitter (emit.goal
  emitConversionBody/resolveField/deriveBody + lower.goal findSemaField), the sema
  checker (convert.goal checkOneConvert/convertOverrides/findConvField), and the
  goscript interpreter (interp/derive.goal overridden + findFieldFold). Change one,
  change all, or `goal check` passes while emit/interp diverge. The interp handles a
  `derive func` (evalDerive) but NOT the inline `...derive` composite-literal spread
  — behavioral derive doctests must use the `derive func` form to pass the interp
  gate. The derive output variable is gensym'd (`e.gensym("out")`) and deriveDecl
  seeds `e.taken = e.newScope()` so the func-mode gensyms see file identifiers.
- internal/fix has TWO parallel AST traversals that MUST stay in lockstep on
  statement coverage (found US-017): `walkReturns` (resultsig.goal) classifies
  every non-closure return, and `descendStmt`/`forEachBlock` (fix.goal) is what
  the propagation rewriter (`safeLocalPropagationCalls`/`fixPropagate`) uses to
  reach collapsible call sites. If one descends into a statement context the
  other does not, a conforming bare-propagation return there gets classified but
  never rewritten -> the signature converts to Result with an unreachable return
  -> non-compiling output. When adding statement coverage, extend BOTH. Prefer
  riding `ast.Walk(visitFn(...))` with a `*ast.FuncLit` cutoff (returns inside a
  closure belong to the closure) — the pattern `unsafeRefOffset` already uses —
  so all statement contexts (type switch, select/comm clause, labeled) are
  covered uniformly for free.
- The single-file transpile path has NO source filename: the corpus `Transpiler`
  interface is `Transpile(src string)` (runner.go), and `backend.Transpile` /
  `goBackend.Emit` carry no file name, so any feature that wants to embed the
  `.goal` source name (e.g. //line anchoring, doctest failure positions) can only
  do so in PACKAGE mode (`backend.TranspilePackage`), where `pkg.Files[i].Name` is
  the real path. Single-file must degrade gracefully (pass "" and omit the
  name-dependent output) — otherwise the golden-VERIFYING path (corpus
  `Transpile(src)`) and the golden-SEEDING path (`goalc -test file.goal`) would
  emit different sidecars and drift. Found US-014: package mode gets
  `file.goal:<line>:` doctest-failure prefixes; single-file stays byte-identical.
- `go build ./cmd/goal` (or ./cmd/goalc) drops a `goal`/`goalc` binary in the
  repo ROOT that is NOT gitignored (found US-012) — it silently shows up as an
  untracked file at commit time. For a quick compile check prefer
  `go build -o /dev/null ./cmd/goal` or `go vet ./cmd/goal`; if you did build to
  the default output, `rm` the binary before staging.
- A doctest fixture is verified by TWO oracles: the compiled Go sidecar (go test)
  AND the goscript INTERP gate. The interp models a `Result` as a single variant
  Value, so `v, err := resultFn()` (two-value binding) FAILS under the interp
  ("assignment has 2 targets but call returned 1 values") even though it compiles
  fine in the backend (which tuple-lowers `Result[T,error]` to `(T,error)`). In a
  doctest fixture, consume a `Result` via value-position `match`
  (`match r { Result.Ok(v) => v; Result.Err(e) => ... }`), which both oracles
  handle. `?` works in the interp. (found US-002)
- To make a testdata transpile pair ALSO index as a doctest case (bumping the
  doctest count), its `.go.expected` must be a doctest sidecar — isDoctestSidecar
  keys on the file containing `"testing"` + `func Test`. Seed it with
  `go run ./cmd/goalc -test file.goal > file.go.expected`, then regenerate via
  corpus-gen + `TestUpdateGoldens -update-goldens`. The corpus manifest read by
  tests is repo-root `corpus/manifest.json` (manifestPath "../../corpus/..."),
  where cmd/corpus-gen writes by default. (found US-002)
- To prove a generated artifact really behaves as documented, compile+run it in a
  throwaway `module goal` temp dir (os.MkdirTemp, write `go.mod` = `module goal\n\ngo
  1.26\n`, format.Source-validate each file, exec `go test`/`go build`, defer
  os.RemoveAll) — the same shape internal/selfhost uses. For a doctest sidecar
  (backend.Transpile res.Test, identical to `goalc -test`), write res.Go AND res.Test
  into ONE package dir (the test is `package <name>` calling res.Go's funcs) and
  `go test .`. A failing doctest exits `go test` NON-ZERO — that is the success path;
  runErr==nil means the doctest passed. Match a locked failure block against a
  NORMALIZED subset (the `doctest <fn>: got …, want …` message), never raw output:
  the `<file>:<line>:` prefix and `FAIL\t<pkg>\t<time>` footer are toolchain-brittle
  (US-005).
- cmd/build-playground error-feature verification (US-003) discriminates checker
  vs backend by the LOCKED-BLOCK FORMAT, not by "does the checker fire". A located
  checker block's first line begins with the feature's SourceName
  (`traffic.goal:10:9: error: [code] …`, the shape sema.Diagnostic.Render emits);
  a backend rejection begins with `backend:`. This matters because the checker NOW
  also flags the unsafe-default example (CheckUnsafeDefaults is in sema.Check), so a
  naive checker-first path would try to match its `backend:`-format locked block
  against the checker render and break `go run ./cmd/build-playground`. Checker path:
  sema.Analyze(source) -> first Error-severity diag -> d.Render(SourceName) must equal
  the locked block (trailing newline trimmed). To capture the exact live render for a
  test constant, drop a throwaway `probe_test.go` in the package (internal/* imports
  need to live IN the module), print d.Render("name.goal"), run `go test -run Probe`,
  then delete it. goal enum syntax is `enum Name { … }` and match arms are
  `Name.Variant => …` (NOT `Variant =>`).
- by-example ERROR features have TWO live-verifying consumers, not one:
  cmd/build-playground (US-003) AND cmd/goal's `ai` bootstrap guide
  (internal/guide, sourced from guide.goal). US-003 only fixed build-playground;
  the guide's lower() still lowered every "error" feature via backend.Transpile
  alone, so a checker-ONLY rejection (non-exhaustive match, dropped result —
  backend.Transpile succeeds) makes TestAICommandEmitsGuide/TestBootstrapGolden
  fail with "expected rejection, but transpile succeeded" (found in US-006). Fix:
  mirror build-playground's discriminator in guide.goal — when
  isCheckerDiagnostic(f.LockedExpected, f.SourceName) (locked block's first line
  begins with SourceName), render live via sema.Analyze + Diagnostic.Render;
  else keep the backend path. After editing guide.goal you MUST regenerate the
  AI-KNOWLEDGE-BOOTSTRAP.md golden: `go run ./cmd/goal ai > AI-KNOWLEDGE-BOOTSTRAP.md`.
- Two-value binding a Result-returning goal function IS a valid consumption form
  in goal source: `diags, err := sema.Analyze(src)` compiles and satisfies
  must-use (Result[T,error] lowers to native (T,error); precedent:
  guide.goal's `perFile, err := sema.AnalyzePackageInDir(...)`).
- Bootstrap-cycle gotcha when adding a NEW helper func to a *.goal that other
  code in the same file calls: `task generate` runs bin/goal, and bin/goal is
  built from the committed *.go. If you regenerate after adding the CALL but
  before the committed .go has the DEFINITION (e.g. you split the edits), the
  committed .go references an undefined symbol, `go build ./cmd/goal` fails, and
  bin/goal can no longer rebuild to regenerate — a deadlock. Escape by
  hand-adding the missing func to the committed .go just enough to compile (the
  //line markers will differ), then `task generate` overwrites it canonically
  and verify-generated passes. Cleanest avoidance: put the def + all its callers
  in ONE edit before regenerating.
- The Edit PostToolUse hook runs the FULL `task check` (go vet + entire suite) after
  every single Edit and BLOCKS on failure — so a multi-edit change is red between
  edits (e.g. unused import, arg-count mismatch). Sequence edits so the tree is
  buildable ASAP; the intermediate hook failures are expected and clear once the last
  edit lands. corpus tests make each hook run ~15s.
- A panic-safety / classification RULE the lexical checker (internal/sema) and the
  backend must agree on belongs in sema (found in US-001): backend imports sema, so
  sema cannot import backend — promote the function INTO sema (exported, e.g.
  sema.ZeroSafety) and call it from backend. No package-both-import shim needed when
  the rule reads facts off sema.Info (Enums/Sealed). Inside sema the backend helpers
  collapse: enumOf(info,n) -> info.Enums[n] != nil, isSealed(info,n) -> info.Sealed[n].
  sema has no base-type helper — reproduce backend's baseType (strip `*` + `pkg.`)
  locally rather than importing textedit.
- The committed generated .go is owned by `task generate`, NEVER by hand: for any
  import-path / identifier rename, edit the .goal source then run `task generate`
  to re-emit ALL .go. A direct sed of the committed .go does not re-sort the
  gofmt import block, so a rename that shifts a path's sort position drifts the
  .go from the regenerated emit and fails `task verify-generated` (found in
  US-020). The .goal import order is cosmetic — the backend sorts on emit.
- The drift gate diffs only the .goal-SOURCED packages, which now share internal/
  with Go-only infra (byexample/corpus/selfhost — no .goal, not emitted). Scope
  any verify diff to the emitted entries (`for entry in _bootstrap/verify/internal/*`),
  never a blanket `diff -r internal _bootstrap/...` (the infra dirs false-fail as
  "Only in internal"). The compiler `main` package is internal/ itself; the lib
  packages are internal/<pkg>; `goal build ./internal` / `go build ./internal`
  both target them correctly.
- Deleting a legacy package can orphan an on-disk TESTDATA FIXTURE that a
  surviving corpus case resolves by import path (found in US-019): the
  foreign-derive corpus case imported `goal/internal/pipeline/testdata/extpkg`,
  a fixture that lived under the deleted `internal/pipeline`. The corpus resolver
  maps a `goal/<path>` import to the on-disk dir `<path>` at transpile time, AND
  the package-mode build step re-copies that dir via the case's pkg.json `imports`
  map — so a deleted fixture fails first as a transpile error ("derive make:
  target field not sourced") then, once relocated, as a build-wiring error ("no
  .go files in <old path>") until the manifest is regenerated. Before deleting any
  `internal/<pkg>`, grep `testdata/extpkg|testdata/` references in testdata/*,
  corpus/manifest.json, and *.goal cases. Relocate the fixture to surviving infra
  the case owns (e.g. internal/corpus/testdata/extpkg), repoint the case's
  `.goal` import + `pkg.json`, then REGENERATE the manifest with
  `go run ./cmd/corpus-gen` (it indexes testdata into corpus/manifest.json — never
  hand-edit the manifest). Keep fixtures OUT of internal/compiler: `task
  verify-generated` diffs internal/compiler against a fresh emit, so any non-emitted
  file there fails the drift gate.
- A type/receiver-name map key must be produced by PEELING the AST, not by
  string-rendering the type: `receiverType` (sema/resolve.goal) records method
  receivers, and both the implements check (implements.goal) and the emitter
  (`methodCalleeSig`, emit.goal) look those methods up by the BARE type name. A
  generic receiver `*Box[T]` rendered to a string keys `Box[T]` and is never
  found. Fix at the single key-PRODUCING site (unwrap `*ast.StarExpr`, then
  `*ast.IndexExpr`/`*ast.IndexListExpr` to `.X`, mirroring `foreignRecvBase` in
  foreign.goal) — that one change repairs the checker AND the emitter at once;
  never patch the lookup strings (fragile, and leaves the other consumer broken).
  (found in the audit-remediation US-018 generic-receiver fix.)
- Foreign package enrichment (internal/sema/foreign.goal) reads facts from a
  dependency's directory with TWO producers that must be composed, not chosen
  (found US-020): the `.go` path (`foreignDecls`) reconstructs struct/func/method
  arities AND §8.1-heuristic enums from generated Go, while the `.goal` path
  (`goalForeignDecls`) runs the front end over the sibling's SOURCE and projects
  its enums + sealed implementor sets. Enum/sealed facts must PREFER `.goal` source
  (overlay it over the `.go`-derived enums, goal wins per key) so a cross-package
  match/exhaustiveness check is not fooled by a stale generated `.go`; struct/func/
  method facts must stay `.go`-derived (qualifyForeignType-vs-goTypeString type-
  string drift). Per-file parse/read failures propagate through a `warns []error`
  return that `EnrichForeign` folds into its `[]error` (the non-fatal `ferrs` from
  `AnalyzePackageInDirWith`) — never swallow them with a bare `continue`.
- Classify a rendered TYPE STRING by WHOLE TOKEN, never by raw `HasPrefix`
  (found US-019). `strings.HasPrefix(typ, "chan"/"func"/"interface")` matches
  user types named `channelSet`/`funcTable`/`interfaceish` and misfires. The
  shared classifier is `sema.TypeShape(typ) -> pointer/slice/array/map/chan/
  func/interface/named`: chan iff `=="chan"`|prefix `"chan "`/`"chan<-"`/
  `"<-chan"`; func iff `=="func"`|prefix `"func("`; interface iff
  `=="interface{}"`|prefix `"interface{"`/`"interface {"` (space form from
  foreign goTypeString). `map[`/`[]`/`[`/`*` already carry a non-ident char so
  their prefixes are safe. Both the panic-safety checker (ZeroSafety) and the
  backend zero-literal lowering (zeroLit) dispatch on this ONE sema helper so
  they can never drift — same promotion pattern as sema.ZeroSafety (backend
  imports sema, not vice versa).
- Any throwaway SUB-EMITTER must reproduce emitFileWith's full (text, usedOption,
  err) contract, not just copy the Builder (found US-024). emitter.exprText renders
  an expression through a fresh &emitter{...} for derive-override values, assert
  messages, and alias underlying types; it used to drop sub.err (unsupported nodes
  emitted truncated Go instead of a located `backend:` error) and sub.usedOptionHelper
  (an `Option.Some(...)` override lowered to a `goalSome(...)` call whose boxing
  prelude was never emitted -> undefined goalSome). Fix: share `taken` by reference
  (gensym set), OR usedOptionHelper back onto the parent, and adopt the sub's FIRST
  error (`if e.err == nil { e.err = sub.err }`). Inert for clean inputs (no golden
  churn, fixpoint holds). To probe the emitter's "unsupported expression %T" arm from
  a fixture that must still PARSE, use a postfix unwrap `x?` (*ast.UnwrapExpr, not
  handled by expr()) — a `match` value does not parse in that position.
- The pinned corpus counts in internal/corpus/generate_test.go (transpile / pkg /
  check / doctest) DRIFT upward as stories add testdata cases, so the PRD notes'
  absolute numbers (e.g. "check 53->55") go stale. Read the CURRENT `want N` from
  generate_test.go and the actual `TestGenerateCounts` failure ("check cases = N,
  want M") — bump to the observed N — rather than trusting the PRD's snapshot.
- Corpus + selfhost are the ONLY external Go consumers of the compiler packages
  once cmd/* is repointed (US-018): when flipping imports
  goal/internal/<pkg> -> goal/internal/compiler/<pkg>, repoint per-SPECIFIC-package
  path (not a blanket goal/internal/ -> goal/internal/compiler/) so sibling infra
  paths (goal/internal/corpus, /byexample, /selfhost) are untouched. The compiler
  twins are API-compatible with the legacy packages EXCEPT sealed-interface enums:
  the only drift hit in US-019 was sema.Severity (compare -> type assertion), same
  as US-018. The internal/selfhost harness LIBRARY (selfhost.go: BuildTranspiled/
  BuildAndTest/ReadPackage) stays Go and is repointed; its legacy-PARITY tests
  (port_test.go, the InScope smoke gate) are retired because their oracle is the
  deleted legacy source — the corpus behavioral tier + `task fixpoint` are the
  post-flip correctness gates.
- When scrubbing `./selfhost` references (US-021, recurs in US-022): the retired
  COMPILER directory is the bare `./selfhost` / `selfhost/` token. `internal/selfhost`
  is a DIFFERENT, surviving package — the Go TEST HARNESS (selfhost.go:
  BuildTranspiled/BuildAndTest/ReadPackage). Scrub only the bare compiler-dir token;
  PRESERVE every `internal/selfhost` reference. Verify with
  `grep -nE "\./selfhost|[^l]selfhost/| selfhost\b"` (excludes the harness) vs
  `grep -n "internal/selfhost"` (must remain). Also note the live bootstrap path is
  `./internal` (Taskfile bootstrap/fixpoint build `go build ./internal`), so any stale
  `goal build ... ./selfhost` snippet maps to `./internal`.
- Adding N testdata/check/*.goal fixtures raises the hardcoded check-case count in
  internal/corpus/generate_test.go by N (found US-001 playground prd: 2 fixtures =>
  51->53). Never guess the delta — regen the manifest (`go run ./cmd/corpus-gen`)
  then read the exact expected number from `go test ./internal/corpus -run
  TestGenerateCounts` and set the assertion to it.
- A construction-side enum/type check must guard on names declared IN THIS FILE
  (walk file.Decls for the decl node) — sema.Info also carries foreign/qualified
  entries whose membership sets may be incomplete, so judging them risks false
  rejections, and the local guard is also what stops ordinary selectors
  (`io.Writer`, `cfg.name`) from being mistaken for `Enum.Variant` constructions.
- The by-example playground pipeline is ordinary Go (internal/byexample +
  cmd/build-playground have NO `.goal` siblings — edit directly, no `task generate`).
  A locked output block's KIND flows through four points: the fenced-block label
  (```go```/```error```/```testfail```) -> byexample readOutputBlock blockKind ->
  byexample parseFeature OutputKind ("go"/"test"/"error"/"doctest-failure") ->
  build-playground expectedLabel pane label. Adding a new output kind means touching
  all four. parseFeature's `/// >>>` "test" promotion only fires when the block began
  as a ```go``` block, so a non-go fenced block can't be mis-promoted. The
  TestParseFindsEveryFeature suite parses the REAL docs/by-example.md and asserts
  each OutputKind is in an allow-list switch — extend it when adding a kind.
- Pure-docs stories touch no `.goal`/`.go`: `task generate` is NOT needed and the
  `task verify-generated` drift gate stays green on its own (it diffs committed `.go`
  against a fresh emit, which is unchanged). The full gate set is still
  `task check` + `task verify-generated` + `task fixpoint`.
- goal front-end gap (found in US-010): a `*ptr = ...` deref-assignment statement
  parses ONLY as the FIRST statement in its block. When it follows another
  statement the lexer inserts no semicolon before the leading `*`, so the parser
  reads `prevExprTail * ptr` as multiplication and fails with "expected
  expression, found =". Workaround when porting Go that uses pointer-to-slice
  out-params (`*p = append(*p, x)`): route every such site through a tiny helper
  whose body is the single deref-assignment (e.g. `func addX(p *[]T, x T) { *p =
  append(*p, x) }`). Behavior-preserving; the prefix swap `*p = append(*p, ` ->
  `addX(p, ` keeps paren balance so multi-line composite-literal tails are
  untouched. (A proper fix belongs in internal/lexer/parser ASI, a separate story.)
- macOS ships BSD sed: `\b` word boundaries are NOT supported and silently no-op
  (the substitution looks like it ran but changes nothing). When renaming a goal
  reserved word used as an identifier (e.g. `enum` -> `enumDecl`, found in US-012)
  you cannot do a blanket word-boundary replace anyway — the same word often
  appears inside error STRING literals ("unknown enum %s") that must stay intact.
  Anchor on the identifier's syntactic delimiters instead (`enum.` / `enum, ` /
  `enum *T` / `enum ==`), or use BSD's `[[:<:]]`/`[[:>:]]`. Grep the strings after.
- A ported dependency may have a DIFFERENT public API than its legacy twin when it
  was made idiomatic first: internal/compiler/sema models `Mode` as a sealed
  interface (`Mode_ModeNone`/`Mode_ModeResult`/`Mode_ModeOption`/...), NOT the
  legacy int enum (`ModeNone`/`ModeResult`/...). Porting a package that compared
  `sig.Mode == sema.ModeResult` must rewrite those to type assertions (goal
  supports `x.(T)` comma-ok and `switch x.(type)`). Add local predicates
  (`func isModeResult(m sema.Mode) bool { _, ok := m.(sema.Mode_ModeResult); return ok }`).
  Safe because the ported sema always populates Mode with a concrete variant
  (ModeNone default), so the interface is never nil. Check a dep's ACTUAL ported
  surface (grep internal/compiler/<dep>/*.go) before assuming verbatim API parity.
  The drift recurs across BOTH source ports AND their dep enums: US-013's interp
  port hit ast.FuncMod (FuncMod_FuncDerive) and sema.Severity (Severity_Error/
  Severity_Warning) the same way. Before building any ported file, grep it for
  `(==|!=)\s*(ast|sema)\.[A-Z]` to find constant comparisons against a now-sealed
  enum and convert each to an `is<Variant>` type-assertion predicate.
- Feeding LEGACY white-box *_test.go through internal/selfhost BuildAndTest as a
  parity oracle (US-013, will recur for the lsp port): the harness rewrites
  goal/internal/ -> goal/internal/compiler/ in the copied tests, but a test that
  CONSUMES a drifted enum's legacy comparable-const/iota API (e.g. a
  `switch d.Severity { case sema.Warning: }` or `x == ast.FuncDerive`) will NOT
  compile against the ported sealed-interface package. Grep the candidate test
  files for the drifted surface FIRST; SPLIT any offender (plus its toolchain-
  bound siblings — e.g. a `go list -deps goal/internal/<pkg>` dependency-envelope
  test pinned to the real module path) into a legacy-only <pkg>_dep_test.go that
  stays under `task check`, rather than rewriting the oracle. Feed the REMAINING
  whole suite to BuildAndTest as ONE set so cross-file white-box helpers
  (runProgram/evalProgram/runMainScope) resolve; only exclude a file when nothing
  else references its helpers (`grep -l 'helperName('`).
- Project skills live in `.morse-code/skills/<name>/` (SKILL.md + scripts/ +
  references/), NOT `.claude/skills/` — `.claude/` is ignored by the user's GLOBAL
  gitignore (~/.config/git/ignore) so anything under it is uncommittable. The repo
  only ignores `.morse-code/state.json` + `.morse-code/initiative.json`, so the
  rest of `.morse-code/` IS tracked. Verify with `git check-ignore -v <path>`
  before placing committable content. macOS ships bash 3.2 — no `mapfile`; use a
  `while IFS= read -r` loop in helper scripts.
- A new sema lexical check (found in US-002): add the `Check<Name>(file *ast.File,
  info *Info) []Diagnostic` function to a feature file in internal/sema, then WIRE it
  by appending `diags = append(diags, Check<Name>(file, info)...)` in the `Check`
  aggregator in internal/sema/check.goal — that is the single path `goal check`'s
  lexical stage runs. Emit `Diagnostic{Pos, Severity.Error|Warning, Feature, Code,
  Message}` (Severity lowers to a sealed interface `Severity(Severity_Error{})`). A
  new emitted `Code` MUST get a row in internal/guide/catalog.goal (diagDoc: Code,
  Feature, severity string "error"/"warning", Meaning) — the catalog is rendered into
  the `goal ai` guide, so after `task generate` you MUST also regenerate the golden:
  `go run ./cmd/goal ai > AI-KNOWLEDGE-BOOTSTRAP.md` (cmd/goal/ai_test.go
  TestBootstrapGoldenMatches asserts committed == live). Reuse fields.goal helpers
  (identName, litKeys, missingFieldNames) and the shared sema.ZeroSafety rule rather
  than re-deriving. To classify a `...defaults` field type through alias chains,
  rebuild the decls map (name -> "struct"/"interface"/typeString(alias)) locally the
  way backend buildTypeDecls does — sema owns typeString in resolve.goal.
- Behavioral check of a sema diagnostic without a corpus fixture (found in US-002):
  sema is an INTERNAL package, so a scratch `go run` file outside the module tree
  fails "use of internal package not allowed". Drop the throwaway main.go into a temp
  dir INSIDE the repo (e.g. ./_tmpverify/) so it is under module `goal`, run
  `go run ./_tmpverify`, then delete it. `sema.Analyze(src)` returns diagnostics with
  Pos.Line/Pos.Col already populated; filter by `d.Code`.
- goal reserves three words beyond Go's keywords: `match`, `enum`, `assert`
  (implements/sealed/from/derive are contextual keywords, NOT reserved). Go source
  that uses any of these EXACT words as an identifier is valid Go but rejected by
  the goal parser. Before feeding any package through the front-end, rename such
  identifiers (e.g. `enum` -> `enumDecl`). `enumOf`/`enumName`/`.Enum` are fine —
  only the bare word collides.
- Self-host smoke gate: internal/selfhost transpiles a set of packages through the
  goal front-end and `go build`s the output in a temp `module goal`. Use
  selfhost.BuildTranspiled(layout) keyed by module-relative dir ("internal/<pkg>")
  to verify any package's transpile compiles — `go build` is the real gate because
  the checker is silent on miscompiles. Reused by every later port story.
- Porting a NON-LEAF file that dispatches into handlers owned by a LATER story (found
  in US-016: lsp server.goal calls definition/hover/references/diagnostics handlers
  ported in US-017): Go won't compile the package until every referenced symbol is
  DEFINED, so a "port this subset AND it builds" AC fails for a subset that calls
  forward. Bridge with an inert stub file (exact legacy signatures, zero-value returns,
  e.g. us017_stubs.goal) that the later story DELETES when it lands the real handlers.
  Two corollaries: (1) adding source files to an already-ported package can flip it from
  leaf to non-leaf and BREAK a sibling self-host gate whose layout assumed a leaf — after
  any port re-run ALL of that package's gates (`go test ./internal/selfhost -run
  'TestPorted<Pkg>'`), not just the new one; (2) the enum-drift trap (below) surfaces at
  `go build`, NOT at `task generate` — the backend emits .go from any syntactically-valid
  .goal, so ALWAYS `go build ./internal/compiler/<pkg>/...` after generating.
- Zero-dependency project: tests use stdlib `testing` only (no testify).
- Verify with `task check` (go vet + full `go test ./...`) and `task build`.
  A PostToolUse hook runs `task check` after every Edit, so a multi-file refactor
  reports transient "undefined: X" / "imported and not used" failures until the
  LAST edit lands — expected; only the final green state matters.
- sema is the one live checker. sema.Diagnostic.Pos is a token.Pos carrying
  Line/Col, so there is no OffsetToPosition step for diagnostics — read
  d.Pos.Line / d.Pos.Col directly. For a raw byte offset (not a diagnostic) use
  token.OffsetToPosition(src, off). Single-file check: sema.Analyze(src); package:
  sema.AnalyzePackageInDir(srcs, dir) / ...InDirWith(srcs, dir, resolve).
- Diagnostic severity unifies on sema.Severity (sema.Error / sema.Warning).
  A package that already imports `go/token` as `token` cannot also alias
  goal/internal/token — keep a tiny local offset->line/col helper instead.
- When the diagnostic-code set changes, two goldens must follow: the guide catalog
  (internal/guide/catalog.go, asserted against scanned source by guide_test
  TestDiagnosticCatalogMatchesSource) and AI-KNOWLEDGE-BOOTSTRAP.md (regenerate
  with `go run ./cmd/goal ai > AI-KNOWLEDGE-BOOTSTRAP.md`).
- internal/textedit is the home for lexer-independent text/type utilities
  (Replacement, Splice, BaseType, IsIdent, IsLineStart, NextNewline, LeadIdent,
  SplitAssign, IsStmtKeyword, ZeroLit). It imports only sort/strings/unicode —
  never the lexer.
- The lexer crutch is GONE: internal/analyze and internal/scan (the text/scanner
  lexer: Lex, Token, Match*, ScanFuncs, CalleeKey, FirstBodyBrace, ParamsClose,
  TopLevelComma, IsBareQuestionStmt, ...) were deleted in US-010. The AST front
  end (internal/parser -> internal/sema) is the only fact source on the live path;
  text/scanner now survives only under attic/ and features/_cut/. sema re-exports
  DirResolver/DefaultResolver (foreign.go) and ResolvePackage/EnrichForeign —
  use those, not analyze. The foreign-package test fixture lives at
  internal/sema/testdata/extpkg.
- Self-host port verification has TWO halves in internal/selfhost, both reused by
  every US-005+ port: selfhost.BuildTranspiled(layout) is the COMPILE gate
  (transpile + `go build` in a temp `module goal`); selfhost.BuildAndTest(relDir,
  pkg, testFiles, deps) is the BEHAVIORAL gate (transpile + copy the EXISTING
  internal/<pkg> white-box test files beside the generated Go + `go test`). Port a
  package by copying internal/<pkg>/*.go to selfhost/<pkg>/*.goal (Go superset =
  valid goal; grep for bare match/enum/assert first), then add a port_test that
  Discovers selfhost/<pkg> and runs both gates against ../<pkg>/<pkg>_test.go.
  When the ported package has an in-module dependency (e.g. lexer imports token),
  pass its ported deps as BuildAndTest's `deps map[string]*project.Package`
  (keyed by module-relative dir like "internal/token") so they are transpiled
  into the same temp module; pass nil for a leaf like token. BuildTranspiled
  already takes a multi-entry layout — list every dep package there too.
- Porting a package whose tests live in ONE monolithic *_test.go that mixes
  self-contained tests with corpus/fixture-dependent ones (e.g. internal/backend):
  PHYSICALLY SPLIT the fixture-free subset into its own real *_test.go in the same
  package (move, never copy — same external test package means duplicate function
  names would clash under `task check`). The split file becomes BuildAndTest's
  behavioral-gate input; the fixture tests stay behind and run under `task check`
  where the real ../../features/testdata + corpus exist. Compute each side's Go
  imports by string-stripping the file first — these test files embed goal source
  in string literals (`os.ReadFile`, `func add(...)`), which produce false-positive
  import/func detections otherwise. Also: a behavioral test file may import a ported
  package beyond the package's own deps (backend_selfhost_test.go imports project),
  which must then be in BuildAndTest's deps map.
- Adding a package under selfhost/ is automatically covered by `task fixpoint`:
  project.Discover walks the whole selfhost tree, so both bootstrap stages emit
  the new package and the diff stays byte-identical — no harness change per port.
  selfhost/ is .goal-only (invisible to the Go toolchain), so it never collides
  with the Go package internal/selfhost despite the shared name.
- The selfhost tree is self-contained (US-003): every selfhost/*.goal imports
  goal/selfhost/* (NOT goal/internal/*), so goal-c-1/goal-c-2 are built purely
  from goal source and `task fixpoint` is a GENUINE differential self-host proof.
  The bootstrap emits ./selfhost to _bootstrap/sN, writes a nested go.mod
  (`module goal`) there, and builds with `go build -C _bootstrap/sN -o
  ../../bin/goal-c-N ./selfhost`. The self-host port gate (internal/selfhost
  port_test.go) keys packages at "selfhost/<pkg>" and BuildAndTest rewrites
  goal/internal/ -> goal/selfhost/ in the copied internal test files. Keep the
  fixpoint green at every later (idiomatic) step — it is the oracle.
- US-002 RELOCATED the goal compiler source: ./selfhost is GONE; the goal-written
  compiler now lives under ./internal/compiler/<pkg> and self-imports
  goal/internal/compiler/<pkg> (was goal/selfhost/<pkg>). The bootstrap+fixpoint
  Taskfile targets emit/build ./internal/compiler. The Go port harness
  (internal/selfhost/) is unchanged in package/import (still goal/internal/selfhost)
  but its port_test.go now Discovers ../../internal/compiler/<pkg> and keys
  layout/deps/relDir at "internal/compiler/<pkg>", and selfhost.go rewrites copied
  white-box tests goal/internal/ -> goal/internal/compiler/. NOTE: selfhost_test.go
  (the InScope smoke gate) is SEPARATE — it transpiles the LEGACY internal/<pkg>/*.go
  via ReadPackage("../"+name) and was untouched. Any earlier "selfhost/" path in
  these notes now means "internal/compiler/".
- Phase-2 TOOLING ports (goalfmt onward) reuse the IDENTICAL internal/compiler
  port harness as the compiler ports — no harness change. Recipe: copy
  internal/<pkg>/*.go -> internal/compiler/<pkg>/*.goal (grep bare
  match/enum/assert first; repoint goal/internal/* -> goal/internal/compiler/*),
  run `task generate` to emit the colocated .go BEFORE any `task check` (the
  verify-generated hook fails on a .goal with no fresh .go), then add a
  TestPorted<Pkg>Package to internal/selfhost/port_test.go using discoverPorted +
  BuildTranspiled (compile gate) + BuildAndTest (behavioral gate). `task generate`
  and `task fixpoint` need NO edit: both tree-walk internal/compiler, so a new
  package is emitted/diffed automatically. When the legacy test file mixes a
  corpus/fixture-dependent suite with self-contained ones, MOVE (not copy) the
  self-contained subset into a new <pkg>_selfhost_test.go (same external test
  package) and feed THAT to BuildAndTest; the fixture suite stays behind under
  `task check`. A test pinning a byte-identical `want` doubles as the output-parity
  oracle when run against the transpiled package.
- LEAF tooling port (package imports only stdlib, no goal/internal deps): simplest
  Phase-2 shape — cp internal/<pkg>/*.go -> internal/compiler/<pkg>/*.goal VERBATIM
  (no import repoint), `task generate`, then a port test with a SINGLE-package
  layout and nil BuildAndTest deps. If the legacy package has NO test file, WRITE a
  self-contained stdlib-only <pkg>_selfhost_test.go in the LEGACY dir with pinned
  byte-identical `want` values — one file then proves parity on BOTH the legacy
  package (`task check`) and the transpiled one (BuildAndTest). cp via Bash does NOT
  trip the verify-generated PostToolUse hook (only Edit/Write do). If the legacy
  package ALREADY ships a self-contained, stdlib-`testing`-only test that builds
  its inputs inline (e.g. internal/cap/cap_test.go), reuse it DIRECTLY as
  BuildAndTest's behavioral input (`../<pkg>/<pkg>_test.go`) — no new
  *_selfhost_test.go needed. A zero-import leaf (cap imports nothing at all) is the
  minimal port: verbatim cp, `task generate`, single-package layout, nil deps.
- The lexer strips newlines/implicit semicolons, so the parser reconstructs
  spec/decl boundaries structurally. Where Go relies on the newline=semicolon
  rule (e.g. a bare const continuation vs a Name+Type spec), use token line
  numbers: p.onNewLine() (parser.go) compares cur().Pos.Line to the previous
  token's line. Every token carries token.Pos{Offset,Line,Col} from the lexer.
- `goal fix` is PER-FILE (cmd/goal cmdFix calls fix.File on each file
  independently — no cross-file/cross-package coordination). Therefore the
  result-sig rule (internal/fix/resultsig.go) only converts a `(T,error)`
  function to Result[T,error] when it can PROVE every call site stays valid:
  it refuses EXPORTED functions (callers may be in another file/package fix never
  sees) and refuses any function referenced anywhere but a collapsible
  `v,err:=f(); if err!=nil{...}` propagation site (a tail `return f(...)`, an
  unguarded call, or a value/argument use would break, since Result is a single
  value not a 2-tuple). Net effect on the selfhost compiler: ~zero safe
  auto-conversions — almost every fallible function bottoms out at an exported
  cross-package API (Discover/Analyze/ParseFile/Transpile/...). Converting those
  Result/? is the per-package audit work (US-005..US-012), which CAN edit the
  cross-file callers; the autofixer deliberately leaves them and reports a
  result-sig Skip naming each one.
- Idiomatic-audit pattern (US-005+): a goal `enum` lowers to a sealed interface +
  per-variant struct + marker (DECISIONS.md §01-enums / §8.1) — it is NOT an
  ordered integer. So a `go/token`-style iota `const` block whose values are used
  as ARRAY INDICES (kindNames[k]), in RANGE PREDICATES (beg < k && k < end), or
  iterated with a numeric `for` does NOT fit `enum`; keep it as `type X int` +
  iota and record the refusal in DECISIONS.md (AC's escape hatch). `enum` fits
  closed, UNORDERED, payload-or-not variant sets matched with `match`. Also: a
  comma-ok helper `f() (T, bool)` is NOT a `goal fix` site and must stay comma-ok
  if the reused US-003 oracle test pins its signature — do not "upgrade" it to
  Option. Audit verification per package: `goal fix <pkg>/*.goal` must produce no
  diff and no stderr report; the self-host port gate + `task fixpoint` confirm the
  behavior-preserving oracle stays byte-identical.
- §9 switch-coexistence is the dominant blocker for SEALING a type during a
  single-package audit (US-007+): a plain `switch`/type-switch on a closed
  enum/sealed value is a sema COMPILE ERROR. So a type whose values are consumed
  by plain switches in OTHER packages (e.g. ast's Node/Decl/Stmt/Expr and the
  FuncMod/ChanDir modifiers are switched on in selfhost/{sema,backend,parser})
  CANNOT be converted to enum/sealed-interface without a coordinated tree-wide
  switch->match in packages the per-package story may not edit. Refuse and record
  it; cross-package conversions, if ever wanted, belong to the whole-tree US-013
  sweep. go/ast-style ordered iota ints used as modifiers/directions are the same
  "keep as iota" case as token.Kind even without array-index/range uses, because
  ==/plain-switch consumption + the `int` representation make a boxed enum a
  behavior break.
- `match` arm patterns are three distinct AST nodes: VariantPattern (enum
  `Enum.Variant`, lead token IDENT), RestPattern (`_`), and TypePattern (sealed-
  interface type pattern `*T`/`*T(x)`, lead token `*`). The backend routes by
  pattern SHAPE, not scrutinee type: isSealedMatch(m) (any TypePattern arm) selects
  the sealedMatch lowering (a Go type-switch with `case *T:` labels), else
  matchQualifier picks Result/Option/enum — keeping dispatch position-independent
  across matchStmt/returnStmt/tryVarMatch/tryAssignMatch/matchValue. Sealedness
  (sema.Info.Sealed bool) and the implementor registry (sema.Info.SealedImpls,
  iface→`*T` set from `implements` clauses) are SEPARATE maps: `implements` also
  binds ordinary interfaces (feature-07 CheckImplements short-circuits sealed ones),
  so a single presence-keyed map would skip that check. Implementors stored as `*T`
  so the registry value == the case-label render == the type-pattern string.
- Value-position `match` arm bodies introduce a grammar ambiguity ONLY for patterns
  whose lead token is also a binary operator (`*`,`-`,`+`,`&`,`<-`): `body \n *T`
  parses as `body * T`. Fix = Go ASI (a binary operator never begins a continuation
  line), applied targeted via a parser `armBody` flag that stops parseBinary when
  `armBody && onNewLine()`. Set it around the value-position arm-body parseExpr only,
  to keep the fixpoint safe.
- A recursive-descent parser written in the error-ACCUMULATOR style (a
  `parser.errs []error` field appended by an `errorf` recorder; internal helpers
  return a bare AST node / nil and never `error`; the exported entry point joins
  the slice at the end) has ZERO intra-package Result/? surface — there is no
  `if err!=nil` propagation site to idiomatize, and the lone `(T,error)` function
  is the exported, oracle-pinned entry point that `goal fix` correctly result-sig
  SKIPs. Before planning a "parser -> Result/?" audit, grep `func .*error`: if the
  only hits are the public ParseFile + a void errorf recorder, the headline idiom
  does not apply and the audit is a documented refusal (US-008). Recovery-by-
  accumulation is behavior-load-bearing (it emits ALL errors + a partial AST), so
  manufacturing (T,error) returns just to apply `?` would NOT be behavior-preserving.
- Converting a (T,error) function to `Result[T, error]` (open-E) + `?` is
  BYTE-IDENTICAL at the emit boundary: open-E Result lowers to native `(T, error)`,
  and `f()?` lowers to `v, err := f(); if err != nil { return zero, err }`, and
  `return Result.Ok(x)` lowers to `return x, nil`. So such a conversion is safe on
  an EXPORTED selfhost function PROVIDED the function has no in-tree callers and no
  oracle test pins it (grep `Func(` across selfhost/** + the copied internal/<pkg>/
  *_test.go) — the emitted Go signature is unchanged, the fixpoint stays
  byte-identical, and no cross-package edit is needed. This is how US-009 converted
  sema.Analyze (its only fitting site). Construction syntax is `Result.Ok(x)` /
  `Result.Err(e)`; propagation is postfix `f(x)?`.
- comma-ok `(T, bool)` helpers whose inner `err != nil` is SWALLOWED to a
  control-flow bool (two distinct failures -> one bool the caller branches on) are
  NOT Result/Option/`?` sites: `?` has nothing to propagate and Option changes the
  (T,bool) contract. `goal fix` emits an advisory `suggestion: [call-site]` for
  these but produces NO source diff, so AC-2 ("no remaining auto-convertible
  propagation sites") still holds with the suggestion present — a `suggestion` is
  not an auto-conversion, only a `skipped`/no-diff matters for the machine check.
- The BACKEND EMITTER gates `?` more tightly than sema: sema accepts `?` in any
  function whose return is "a Result, a `func(…) error`, or a tuple ending in
  error" (sema.goal:39), but emit.goal REJECTS `?` outside a Result/Option-
  returning host (`backend: \`?\` outside a Result- or Option-returning function`).
  So to `?` a pure-propagation site you MUST convert the ENCLOSING function to
  `Result` — a plain `(T,error)` host cannot host `?` even though sema allows it.
  This matches `goal fix`'s own `suggestion` wording ("…not Result-returning;
  convert its signature to use `?`"). Practical consequence for an audit: a `?`
  conversion is never purely local — it forces the host to `Result`, which forces
  every caller of that host to consume a `Result` (via `?` if it also propagates
  purely, or `match` if it WRAPS / is void).
- Error-WRAPPING propagation (`if err != nil { return …, fmt.Errorf("ctx: %w",
  err) }`) is NOT a `?` site: `?` propagates the error UNCHANGED, so `?` would drop
  the context = behavior change. Such a consumer of a `Result` callee uses
  statement-position `match { Result.Ok(v) => {…} Result.Err(e) => { return
  Result.Err(fmt.Errorf("ctx: %w", e)) } }` (lowers via emit.goal resultMatch to
  `v, err := f(); if err != nil { <Err arm> } else { <Ok arm> }` — behavior-
  identical). Backends/compilers tend to wrap pervasively (good Go practice), so
  in such packages the genuine `?` surface is a SUBSET of the fallible functions —
  only the cluster whose internal propagation is pure. Convert that cluster
  (US-011 did the backend derive/`from`-conversion cluster: resolveField +
  deriveBody -> Result, elemConv stays (T,error) callee, the 5 pure sites -> `?`,
  the 2 wrapping/void consumers -> `match`) and refuse the wrapping/oracle/
  interface-pinned rest with reason.
- match arm bodies accept a block `{ … }`, a statement, or an expression (parser
  parseMatchArm / emit.goal armBody). Wrap a multi-statement or assignment arm
  body in a block `{ … }` to be safe (a bare `x = y` assignment is not an
  expression). `match` over an open-E Result needs BOTH `Result.Ok` and
  `Result.Err` arms (emit.goal:2142). It is the §8.3 Result idiom, NOT a
  switch->enum conversion — do not count it toward AC-1's "switch-over-in-file-
  enum -> match" (backend has no in-file enum; that part stays a refusal).
- Foreign enrichment (sema.EnrichForeign -> foreignDecls) has TWO source paths now
  (SEAM-CAP-2): when the resolved import dir holds non-test .go, it reconstructs foreign
  enums from the generated §8.1 marker-interface encoding (reconstructForeignEnums); when
  it holds ONLY .goal SOURCE (the real per-package `goal build ./selfhost` topology), it
  runs the goal front end (parser.ParseFile + ResolvePackage) over those .goal files and
  projects EXPORTED enums into info.Enums keyed `alias.Enum` AND (SEAM-CAP-3c) EXPORTED
  sealed-interface implementor sets into info.Sealed + info.SealedImpls keyed `alias.Iface`
  (implementors requalified `*alias.T` via qualifyForeignType), as a new 6th `sealed
  map[string][]string` return of foreignDecls/goalForeignDecls (the .go path returns nil
  sealed). The .go path wins when both exist. Only ENUMS + SEALED-INTERFACE implementor sets
  are projected from .goal; struct/func/method foreign facts from .goal source are deferred.
  The sealed projection is what makes a cross-package type-pattern `match` resolve +
  exhaustiveness-check; the backend sealedMatch lowering is pattern-SHAPE dispatch
  (isSealedMatch) and needs no foreign fact. Cross-package bare variant construction
  (`pkg.Enum.Variant`) lowers via enumRef (the construction-side counterpart of
  matchQualifier) in backend selectorExpr/variantLit/armBodyType -> `pkg.Enum(pkg.Enum_Variant{})`.
  Mirror any such pipeline change in BOTH internal/ and selfhost/ or fixpoint breaks.
- Converting an iota type to a goal `enum` (SEAM-002 pattern): (1) The enum ZERO
  VALUE is nil, NOT the first variant — iota gave a meaningful zero, an enum does
  not, so set the field explicitly at EVERY constructor (`grep '&ast.<Type>{'`) or a
  later `match` faults on nil at run time. (2) Every ==/!=/plain-switch consumer
  becomes `match`; for a `!=`/`==` inside a boolean guard, bind a bool via
  value-position `match` and split any `!ok` type-assert check out FIRST (hoisting
  the match above `!ok` nil-derefs the failed assertion). (3) A control switch with a
  no-op/grouped arm is cleanest as `isX := match {…}` + `if isX`, avoiding an empty
  `{}` match arm. (4) KEEP a member as iota only for genuine NUMERIC IDENTITY (array
  index, range predicate, contiguous numbering — e.g. token.Kind); a boxed enum would
  be a behavior change there (AC escape hatch). (5) internal/ast (bootstrap Go AST)
  stays Go-iota and is NOT in the fixpoint diff, so a selfhost-only iota->enum
  conversion moves NO corpus/snapshot goldens (those test internal/). The only
  conflict is a SHARED port-gated internal test referencing the iota constants: it
  cannot compile against the enum-transpiled selfhost pkg, so relocate those
  assertions to a NEW internal-only `_test.go` kept OUT of
  internal/selfhost/port_test.go's BuildAndTest slice (and re-create any
  function-local closure helpers — they are not package-level).
- Enum gotchas refined in SEAM-003: (a) A goal `enum` CANNOT carry a method — it
  lowers to a sealed interface and Go forbids a method on an interface type
  (`invalid receiver type X`). Convert `(x X) String()` etc. to a FREE function
  `XLabel(x X)` and update `%s`/Stringer call sites to call it. (b) Value-position
  `match` lowers only as `:=` / `var name T = match` / `return match`, NEVER as a
  bare `field = match` assignment (`unsupported expression *ast.MatchExpr`); and
  `:=` type-inference fires only when EVERY arm is one enum/string/bool LITERAL, so
  an arm returning a variable forces `var name T = match`. Bind to a temp, then
  assign. (c) When a value may be the enum ZERO (nil) — a `csig`/`sig` paired with
  `!ok`/`!known`, or a map miss — match with an explicit `_` rest-arm (lowers to a
  real Go `default`, nil-safe) and keep the `!ok` short-circuit in the surrounding
  `if`; full enumeration lowers to a panicking default and faults on nil. (d) The
  shared-port-gate test conflict has TWO fixes by whether the type has a production
  string form: a type WITH one (Severity→SeverityLabel) — mirror the free function
  in BOTH internal and selfhost and rewrite shared comparisons to call it (no
  relocation, full coverage); a type WITHOUT one (Mode) — relocate its assertions to
  an internal-only `_test.go` out of the port-gate slice.
- Self-host FLIP invariants (adopted in US-001, binding on all flip stories): the
  layout is COLOCATED — `<file>.goal` canonical source + committed generated
  `<file>.go` in the SAME package dir (one import path; go build reads .go, the goal
  front-end reads .goal). The bootstrap is B-commit (committed generated Go, drift-
  gated), NOT a prebuilt binary or emit-on-every-build. Once the hand-written
  reference Go transpiler is deleted, the corpus behavioral tier is the PRIMARY
  correctness gate (the Go differential oracle is gone); `task fixpoint` byte-identity
  still holds. "Self-hosted" = the shipped goal+goalc library closure (incl. goalfmt/
  textedit/cap/guide/fix/interp/lsp); corpus, byexample, internal/selfhost,
  cmd/corpus-gen, cmd/build-playground deliberately stay Go.
- CAPABILITY GAP — the goal backend DROPS `//go:embed` directives (US-009 probe:
  a `.goal` with `//go:embed x` + `var v string` emits Go that KEEPS the `_ "embed"`
  blank import but EMITS NO directive, so the var is empty; a `//line` directive is
  also injected between import and var, which would break embed even if emitted).
  Porting any package that uses `//go:embed` requires inlining the embedded bytes as
  a `const` raw-string literal (exact bytes, incl. trailing newline) and dropping the
  `_ "embed"` import. Raw-string content is one lexer token, so embedded `enum`/
  `match`/`=>`/keywords are safe. Distinct from `goal.Docs.ReadFile(...)` (a METHOD
  call on the root `goal` package's embed.FS) which ports unchanged.
- NON-COMPILER tooling port whose deps include the root `goal` package and/or Go-only
  dev infra (byexample, corpus): the internal/selfhost BuildTranspiled/BuildAndTest
  throwaway `module goal` harness CANNOT verify it (those deps are absent from the
  isolated temp module, so the transpiled package won't build there). Instead rely on
  the REAL module: AC "generates .go that builds" = `task generate` +
  `go build ./internal/compiler/<pkg>/...` + the verify-generated drift gate; AC
  "output matches legacy" = an IN-REPO parity test (`package <pkg>_test`) placed in
  the LEGACY internal/<pkg>/ dir (NOT internal/compiler/<pkg>/ — verify-generated
  diffs that tree vs a fresh emit excluding only *.goal, so a hand-written _test.go
  there is flagged as drift) that imports BOTH legacy `goal/internal/<pkg>` and ported
  `goal/internal/compiler/<pkg>` (aliased; same package name) and asserts byte-identical
  output over a fixture set. The port-gate test in port_test.go then only asserts the
  port SHAPE (discoverPorted: one package, right name). This is also a strong end-to-end
  check: the ported package transitively uses the ported backend/sema, so any
  legacy-vs-ported divergence surfaces.
- PORTING A CALLER OF A TYPE THE SEMA PORT TURNED INTO AN ENUM: sema.Severity is a goal
  `enum` (sealed interface) in the ported sema, so it has NO `String()` method (an enum
  can't) — `%s`/Stringer renders the empty variant struct as `{}`. The ported sema
  exposes a free func `sema.SeverityLabel(s)` (its own analyze.goal uses it); legacy
  sema keeps BOTH `(Severity).String()` and `SeverityLabel`. So a ported consumer that
  formatted `d.Severity` with `%s` (relying on the legacy Stringer) must switch to
  `sema.SeverityLabel(d.Severity)` to stay byte-identical (US-009 guide hit exactly
  this on the live feedback-sample diagnostics). General rule: when a ported package
  formats a value of a type the sema/ast port boxed into an enum/sealed interface,
  grep the ported package for that type's String/Format-via-`%s` uses and route them
  through the port's replacement free function.
- Editing a `.goal` file's package-doc or inline COMMENTS produces NO committed `.go`
  delta (found in US-022): the backend drops comments on emit, so `task generate` is a
  no-op for comment-only `.goal` edits and the `task verify-generated` drift gate stays
  green without a `.go` change. Still run `task generate` after ANY `.goal` edit to
  confirm — only string-literal/identifier/structural edits move the emitted `.go`.
- To scrub a path token while PRESERVING a longer token that contains it (e.g. strip
  `selfhost/<pkg>` and `./selfhost` but keep `internal/selfhost`, found in US-022), use
  a protect-restore sed — BSD sed has no lookbehind: `s|internal/selfhost|@@SENTINEL@@|g`
  first, then the scrub (`s|\./selfhost|./internal|g; s|selfhost/|internal/|g`), then
  `s|@@SENTINEL@@|internal/selfhost|g`. Verify after: the scrubbed token returns empty
  and the protected token's count is unchanged, and grep for `internal/internal` to catch
  any accidental double-prefix. Conceptual prose ("the selfhost tree", "selfhost packages")
  and the compiler's own program name are NOT directory tokens — leave them.
- The goscript INTERP (internal/interp) evaluates doctests as a SECOND oracle and
  cannot run every construct (e.g. it has no *ast.FuncLit case; it resolves a
  function's ?-propagation signature by NAME via sigFor). When a new doctest
  fixture uses an interp-unsupported construct, record its case ID in the
  honest-deferral registry internal/corpus/interp_gate_test.go `interpGateSkips`
  (map[caseID]reason, blank reasons are rejected) — do NOT drop it silently. BOTH
  TestInterpWholeCorpusBehavioralGate and TestInterpRunner consult that registry.
  The compiled Go sidecar oracle (TestDoctestRunner) still proves behavior.
- `Result.Ok(...)`/`Result.Err(...)` inside a MATCH ARM (value/return position) is
  a PRE-EXISTING lowering gap: emitted unlowered even without closures. A bare tail
  `return Result.Ok(x)` lowers fine. Design Result-returning fixtures to keep match
  arms yielding plain values and reconstruct the Result in tail position. A
  value-position `x := match ...` with plain-typed arms needs `var x T = match ...`.

- Bootstrap ordering trap (found US-022): `task generate` first runs `go build -o
  bin/goal ./cmd/goal`, then uses that binary to transpile `./internal`. So if a
  `.goal` edit changes a type/signature that `cmd/goal` or `cmd/goalc` itself
  consumes (e.g. a new field on `pipeline.Output`/`PackageOutput`), the build of
  bin/goal fails against the STALE generated `.go`, and generate can never run to
  refresh it — a deadlock. Break it by hand-patching just enough of the stale
  generated `internal/.../*.go` (the struct/signature the drivers reference) so
  bin/goal compiles; then `task generate` regenerates every mirror correctly and
  overwrites the manual patch. The emitter's runtime logic being stale does not
  matter for this step — transpiling source only emits structure as written.

## [2026-06-29T12:30:00Z] - US-011 (self-host idiomatic PRD)
- Step 3 of 3 (idiomatic audit), seventh and LARGEST package: selfhost/backend
  (~3,447 LOC). Unlike the leaf refusals (token/lexer/ast/parser, US-005..US-008)
  and the project/pipeline double-refusal (US-010), this is a GENUINE conversion
  of the derive/`from`-conversion subsystem to idiomatic Result/`?`/`match`, plus
  documented refusals for the wrapping + oracle/interface-pinned rest. Second
  package after sema (US-009) with executable Result/`?`, and the FIRST to use
  `match` in executable selfhost source.
- CONVERTED (emit.goal + lower.goal): `resolveField` ([]string,error) ->
  Result[[]string,error] and `deriveBody` ([]string,error) -> Result[[]string,
  error]. resolveField owns no internal wrap, so its 4 `elemConv(...)` sites + 1
  `e.deriveBody(...)` site became `?` and its other returns became Result.Ok/Err.
  `elemConv` stays (func(string)string, error) — it is the leaf CALLEE; the `?`
  requirement is on the host, not the callee, so no signature change (also avoids a
  func-typed Result.Ok payload). The two WRAPPING/void consumers of resolveField
  became `match`: deriveBody's nested-field-wrap site and genConversion's
  void/e.fail site.
- REFUSED (recorded in DECISIONS.md "US-011 (backend)"): Transpile (exported +
  oracle + wraps parse:/generated-Go:), Backend.Emit/goBackend.Emit (interface-
  pinned + wraps doctests:), TranspilePackage (exported + oracle + wraps format:),
  GoFormatter.Format (foreign tail-return), emitFile/emitFileWith/emitDoctests
  (3-value accumulator shape, non-propagating), and switch->match (NO in-file enum;
  every switch is over ast category interfaces [unsealable per US-007 §9],
  token.Kind, rune, or bool).
- Machine check (AC-2): `goal fix -inplace selfhost/backend/*.goal` -> NO source
  diff (verified against a pre-fix backup). The former genConversion/resolveField/
  deriveBody `suggestion`s are gone; remaining stderr is only `skipped` (Transpile/
  emitFile/elemConv/TranspilePackage non-propagating returns) + advisory
  `suggestion`s on the documented refusals — neither is an auto-conversion, so AC-2
  holds.
- Files: selfhost/backend/emit.goal (resolveField/deriveBody -> Result, `?`x5,
  `match`x2 in deriveBody+genConversion); DECISIONS.md (US-011 section); prd.json
  (US-011 passes:true); progress.txt. Initiative artifacts under
  history/20260629-refactor-us-011-idiomatic-audit-backend/. lower.goal unchanged
  (elemConv kept (T,error)).
- Verify: go test ./internal/selfhost -run TestPortedBackendPackage green (the
  converted backend transpiles to compiling Go and passes the copied internal/
  backend behavioral suite); task check green (incl. the port gate + internal/
  backend + the corpus transpile/behavioral tiers); task build green; task
  fixpoint FIXPOINT OK (selfhost/backend/*.go byte-identical goal-c-1/goal-c-2).
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - See the three new Codebase Patterns bullets (emitter gates `?` to a Result/
    Option host; wrapping propagation is a `match` site not a `?` site; match arm
    bodies + Result-match shape). The net audit rule for a wrapping-heavy package:
    convert the cluster whose internal propagation is PURE; consume its Result at
    wrapping/void boundaries with `match`; refuse the oracle/interface-pinned and
    wrapping-only functions.
  - Only US-012 (typecheck) and US-013 (final whole-tree sweep) remain.

## [2026-06-28T23:25:00Z] - US-008 (checker-onto-ast PRD)
- Migrated internal/project and internal/pipeline/sourcemap off the internal/scan
  token lexer (and confirmed neither touches internal/analyze). Package-name
  detection and the //line source map are now derived from the goal AST.
- project.PackageClause: scan.Lex loop -> parser.ParseFile + file.Name.Name. The
  goal parser's expect() synthesizes a name token even when `package` is absent
  (so `func main(){}` would falsely yield "main"); guard by checking src at
  file.Package.Offset literally begins with "package". Reading the name even on
  later body parse errors preserves the old lexer's tolerance.
- pipeline.sourcemap: declSites now parses with parser.ParseFile and walks
  file.Decls, taking decl.Pos().Offset as the line-start keyword offset. declName
  rewritten to switch on ast.Decl (FuncDecl/EnumDecl/SealedInterfaceDecl ->
  Name.Name; GenDecl -> single-spec const/var/type name, "" for import/grouped).
  Removed token-based declName + isDeclKeyword.
- Files: internal/project/project.go, internal/pipeline/sourcemap.go, prd.json,
  progress.txt. Initiative artifacts under
  history/20260628-refactor-us-008-migrate-project-and-sourcemap-off-scan/.
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - The goal parser is a Go superset, so parser.ParseFile reads BOTH goal source
    AND generated Go (internal/fix already relies on this) — no separate go/parser
    needed for the source map's two sides.
  - parser.ParseFile ALWAYS returns a non-nil *ast.File (partial on error) and
    ALWAYS sets file.Name via expect(), so a missing package clause is detected by
    inspecting src at file.Package.Offset, not by a nil name.
  - FuncDecl.Pos() resolves to FuncType.Func, which the parser sets to the `func`
    keyword even for methods (parser.go:350) — so it is the line-start offset a
    //line directive must precede, methods included.
  - Minor (documented) divergence from the legacy lexer: sealed interfaces and
    from/derive funcs are now mapped to their source lines too (legacy skipped
    them since their leading token isn't a decl keyword). Strictly more correct
    for error reporting; no golden asserts //line text and conformance is
    behavioral. Remaining live analyze/scan consumer after this story:
    backend/package (US-009); then US-010 deletes analyze + the scanner.

## [2026-06-28T22:01:00Z] - US-003 (checker-onto-ast PRD)
- Proved US-003 "Add differential checker parity gate": a new test runs BOTH the
  AST checker (corpus.SemaCheck) and the legacy lexical checker (check.Analyze)
  over every KindCheck case under testdata/check/** and compares findings by
  (file, line, feature, code, severity) — the safety proof that deleting
  internal/check (US-005) loses no guarantee the AST checker doesn't already
  provide. The gate subtracts a DECISIONS.md-backed allowlist of 4 known
  divergences and fails on (a) an empty check corpus, (b) any undocumented
  divergence, and (c) any stale allowlist entry that no longer reproduces.
- The 4 divergences (the COMPLETE set over the corpus, discovered empirically):
  - 3x 12-derive-convert (fallible_in_total:24, unbridged_field:19,
    unsourced_field:18): AST fires a real Error (fallible-in-total-derive /
    unbridged-field / unsourced-field) where legacy defers with
    unresolved-derive-type (Warning). Legacy reads the derive target type NAME
    lexically and swallows the trailing `// want` comment into the name, so it
    never resolves the in-file struct; the AST checker resolves it and proves the
    incompleteness. Documented as improvements; the existing `// want` markers
    already contain the sema Error substrings (no fixture edit needed).
  - 1x 06-error-e/defer_err_value:16: AST surfaces a located
    unresolved-err-value Warning (closedness deferred for Result.Err on a bound
    var); legacy is silent. Both non-rejecting; documented.
- Files: internal/corpus/parity_test.go (new gate + knownDivergences allowlist),
  DECISIONS.md (new "US-003 — differential checker parity gate" section). prd.json
  US-003 -> passes:true. Initiative artifacts under
  history/20260628-feature-us-003-differential-checker-parity-gate/.
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Parity is judged by (file, line, feature, code, severity), NOT message text:
    the lexical checker quotes raw source spans while the AST checker reports
    resolved type/field names, so message equality would be pure noise. Compare
    WHICH guarantee fires WHERE at WHAT severity.
  - Both check.Analyze and corpus.SemaCheck return []check.Diagnostic with Pos as
    a byte offset; line = check.OffsetToPosition(src, d.Pos).Line for both, so the
    two streams are directly comparable with no sema/check severity translation
    (SemaCheck already maps sema.Severity -> check.Severity).
  - The gate is self-policing against allowlist rot: a documented divergence that
    stops reproducing FAILS the gate (stale entry), forcing the allowlist +
    DECISIONS.md to stay honest as the AST checker evolves.
  - To discover divergences over the whole corpus, drop a throwaway _test.go in
    internal/corpus that diffs the two checkers' finding sets per manifest
    KindCheck case — fast and exhaustive; delete it once the real gate is written.

## [2026-06-28T21:10:00Z] - US-002 (checker-onto-ast PRD)
- Proved US-002 "Add sema package-check driver": internal/sema now has a
  package-level entry point that checks a whole multi-file goal package and
  returns per-file diagnostics from merged, foreign-enriched facts — the AST
  analogue of internal/check.AnalyzePackageInDir, so US-004 (rewire cmd/goal) is
  a near drop-in swap. New `sema.AnalyzePackageInDir(srcs []string, dir string)
  ([][]Diagnostic, error)` + `AnalyzePackageInDirWith(srcs, dir, resolve
  DirResolver) ([][]Diagnostic, []error, error)`: parse each src
  (parser.ParseFile), ResolvePackage over all files, aggregate every file's
  ast.File.Imports, EnrichForeign once over the shared Info (US-001), then Check
  per file in input order. Parse error is fatal; foreign-resolution errors are
  non-fatal (the plain entry point discards them).
- Files: internal/sema/package.go (new driver),
  internal/sema/package_test.go (new): cross-file exhaustiveness (enum in file A,
  non-exhaustive match in file B -> Error only in file B; proves merge + input
  order), foreign-enriched derive finding (a `derive func make(o *ext.Outer)
  Target` where Target.Extra is unsourced -> unsourced-field Error ONLY when the
  fake resolver loads the shared ../analyze/testdata/extpkg fixture; the control
  run with a failing resolver defers to the unresolved-derive-type Warning,
  proving the Error depends on US-001 enrichment), and a parse-error test. All
  verifyCommands green (task check, task build).
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - sema may import internal/parser with no cycle (parser deps = token/ast/lexer
    only); the package driver is the first production sema->parser edge (corpus
    and backend already do parser.ParseFile + sema.* externally).
  - The foreign-enrichment-dependent finding is a CheckConvert derive whose
    SOURCE is a foreign struct: without EnrichForeign loading the imported
    package, info.Structs lacks `alias.Type` so CheckConvert defers
    (unresolved-derive-type Warning); with it, an unsourced target field becomes
    a real unsourced-field Error. Contrast Warning-vs-Error across two driver
    runs (good resolver vs failing resolver) to PROVE a finding depends on
    enrichment rather than just asserting the enriched outcome.
  - Imports are aggregated across ALL package files before one EnrichForeign call
    (it dedupes by import path); the merged Info is shared by every per-file
    Check — mirrors check.AnalyzePackageInDirWith threading one analyze.Tables.
  - sema.Diagnostic.Pos is a token.Pos carrying Line/Col, so the driver returns
    diagnostics ready to render with no OffsetToPosition mapping (US-004 note).

## [2026-06-28T20:30:00Z] - US-001 (checker-onto-ast PRD)
- Proved US-001 "Add foreign enrichment to sema.Info": sema can now resolve
  out-of-package struct fields and method signatures into sema.Info WITHOUT
  analyze.Tables and WITHOUT re-lexing. New `sema.EnrichForeign(info,
  imports []*ast.ImportSpec, dir string, resolve DirResolver) []error` reads
  the imported Go packages (stdlib go/parser) driven by the parsed goal file's
  import specs (ast.File.Imports), folding exported foreign structs into
  info.Structs (keyed `alias.Type`, fields qualified by alias), exported methods
  into the NEW info.ForeignMethods (keyed `alias.Recv.Method`), and exported
  receiver-less funcs into info.FuncSignatures (keyed `alias.Func`). A foreign
  entry carries only the `?`-relevant facts (Arity, EndsInError; Mode=ModeNone),
  mirroring analyze.Tables.
- Mechanism: ported the Go-toolchain reader from internal/analyze/foreign.go
  (foreignDecls, goTypeString qualify-by-alias, foreignRecvBase, endsInErrorAST,
  arity, DefaultResolver + moduleResolve/goListResolve), but the import list now
  comes from the AST, not scan.Lex/analyze.ParseImports — so the lexer is off
  this path. The rendering matches analyze byte-for-byte, which the parity test
  pins.
- Files: internal/sema/sema.go (Info.ForeignMethods field),
  internal/sema/resolve.go (init + Merge ForeignMethods),
  internal/sema/foreign.go (new: DirResolver, DefaultResolver, EnrichForeign +
  reader helpers), internal/sema/foreign_test.go (new: parity vs
  analyze.EnrichForeign over the shared ../analyze/testdata/extpkg fixture, plus
  resolve-error-non-fatal and nil-resolver-default tests).
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - sema/foreign.go aliases stdlib go/ast as `goast`/go/parser as `goparser`
    because the package already imports goal's internal/ast as `ast`; foreign
    reader helpers are renamed (goResultArity, foreignFields, goExprText) to
    avoid colliding with resolve.go's resultArity/typeString.
  - Foreign struct fields MUST be rendered with the qualify-by-alias renderer
    (goTypeString), NOT sema.typeString (which does not qualify a package-local
    name), or the foreign Structs entries diverge from analyze and the registry
    lookups by string miss. The parity test (compare info.Structs +
    info.ForeignMethods against analyze.Build+EnrichForeign for the same src)
    is the gate against future drift.
  - The shared foreign fixture lives at internal/analyze/testdata/extpkg
    (Outer/Inner structs + Inner.Close method + Mkdir/Open/Triple funcs); reuse
    it from sema via the relative path ../analyze/testdata/extpkg.
  - This is the shared unit for US-009 (backend onto sema enrichment): the
    backend can drop analyze.BuildPackage+analyze.EnrichForeign in favor of
    sema.ResolvePackage + sema.EnrichForeign(info, file.Imports, dir, nil).
---

## [2026-06-28T19:10:00Z] - US-003
- Proved US-003 "Allow `?` on method calls returning Result": `?` now works on a
  method call whose method returns a Result (or a trailing error), for both a
  concrete-struct receiver and an interface- / sealed-interface-typed receiver —
  no need to wrap interface calls in a plain helper func first (the
  environment-manager workaround). `goal check` accepts `v := recv.M()?` (M
  returns Result[T,error]) with no question-callee-no-error; transpiling binds the
  value + propagates the error; a bare `recv.M()?` on an error-only method lowers
  to the single-variable `if err := recv.M(); err != nil` form (not a 2-value
  over-destructure); a `?` on a non-error-ending method is still rejected.
- Mechanism: a `recv.M()?` callee was mis-resolved in all three `?` layers because
  a method's resolved signature dropped its Result/Option MODE (it kept only a raw
  syntactic arity/ends-in-error). Fix carries the method's full FuncSig through
  each layer:
  - internal/analyze: new `methodResultSig` applies the same Result/Option
    normalization analyzeSig uses, stored as `analyze.Method.Return`;
    `methodFrom` (shared by concrete `analyzeMethods` AND interface
    `parseInterfaceBody`) fills it. `ResolveCallee` returns `m.Return` and now
    also resolves interface-typed receivers via `Tables.Interfaces`. A
    `sealed interface` body is parsed into `Tables.Interfaces` too (Build loop).
  - internal/sema: added `sema.Method.Return` (the resolved FuncSig), populated in
    `resolveMethod` and `resolveInterface` via the existing `funcSig` helper;
    extracted `resolveInterfaceMethods(name, *ast.FieldList)` so a
    `*ast.SealedInterfaceDecl`'s method set is resolved into `Info.Interfaces`,
    not just flagged in `Info.Sealed`.
  - internal/backend: emitter gained a per-function `recvTypes` map (receiver +
    params -> base type), built in `funcDecl` (save/restore); `calleeSig`'s
    selector case first tries `methodCalleeSig` (info.Methods then
    info.Interfaces) before the package-qualifier path, so the `?` destructure
    arity matches the method's real lowered shape.
- Files: internal/analyze/analyze.go (Method.Return, methodResultSig, methodFrom,
  sealed-interface body parse), internal/analyze/methods.go (ResolveCallee
  concrete+interface), internal/sema/sema.go (Method.Return),
  internal/sema/resolve.go (resolveMethod/resolveInterface/resolveInterfaceMethods,
  SealedInterfaceDecl), internal/backend/emit.go (recvTypes, buildRecvTypes,
  recvBaseType, methodCalleeSig, calleeSig), internal/check/question_test.go
  (accept Result method `?`, reject non-error method `?`),
  internal/backend/backend_test.go (TestASTEngineUnwrapsMethodCallResult). All
  verifyCommands green (build, vet, full test suite).
- Learnings: see the new Codebase Patterns entry (method-callee `?` resolution
  threads the method's full FuncSig through analyze/sema/backend; sealed-interface
  method sets must be resolved, not just flagged).

## [2026-06-28T18:20:00Z] - US-002
- Proved US-002 "Lower value-position match over Result and Option": a `match`
  over a Result or Option used as a VALUE — returned directly (`return match …`)
  or bound as an assignment RHS (`x := match …` / `var x T = match …`) — now
  lowers. Previously only enum value-position match lowered; a value-position
  Result/Option match reached the generic expr path and failed with
  `unsupported expression *ast.MatchExpr`.
- Mechanism: generalized the existing statement-position lowering
  (resultMatch/closedResultMatch/optionMatch) to take `(m, pos matchPos, name
  string)` and emit each arm body through armWrap (the same wrapper enumMatch
  already uses): bare in posStmt, `return <body>` in posReturn, `name = <body>`
  in posVar. Renamed arms (Ok/Err payload bindings) flow through a new
  armBodyRenamedWrap. Value-position dispatch wired into the SAME three seams the
  enum path uses: returnStmt (posReturn), tryVarMatch (posVar, explicit `var name
  T`), tryAssignMatch (posVar, type via inferMatchType — non-inferable arms keep
  the located deferral). matchStmt calls the emitters with posStmt, so the
  statement path (features/03-result, features/04-option) is byte-for-byte
  unchanged.
- Files: internal/backend/emit.go (matchStmt, resultMatch, closedResultMatch,
  optionMatch signatures + armWrap calls; new armBodyRenamedWrap; returnStmt,
  tryVarMatch, tryAssignMatch dispatch; new matchValue dispatch helper),
  internal/backend/backend_test.go (TestASTEngineValueMatchBehavioralTier +
  TestASTEngineValueMatchEncoding), internal/backend/testdata/
  match_value_result.goal + match_value_option.goal (Result/Option × return/assign
  fixtures). All verifyCommands green (build, vet, full test suite).
- Learnings: see the new Codebase Patterns entry (one position-parameterized set
  of match emitters + three dispatch seams; no separate value path).

## [2026-06-28T18:05:00Z] - US-001
- Proved US-001 "Lower Option construction in value positions": Option.Some/None
  now lowers to its *T pointer encoding wherever an Option value is PRODUCED — a
  var/assign RHS (`x := Option.Some(v)` -> `x := &v`), a call argument, a
  struct-literal field, and slice/map-literal elements — not only at a direct
  return or as a Result.Ok payload. Previously these reached the generic expr path
  and emitted `Option.Some/None` verbatim, leaving `Option` undefined in the Go.
- Mechanism: a single interception at the TOP of emitter.expr (the one
  value-emission seam all value positions route through). optionConstruction
  (lower.go) classifies an Option construction as "none" (-> nil), "some-addr"
  (single Ident arg -> &arg), or "some-box" (any other single arg -> goalSome(arg)).
  A non-addressable Some cannot be address-taken as a pure expression and the
  single-pass emitter cannot hoist a temp there, so it boxes through a generic
  helper `func goalSome[T any](v T) *T { return &v }` (optionPrelude), appended at
  end-of-file (Go decls are order-independent) gated by the runtime
  emitter.usedOptionHelper flag — emitted only when actually used. Package mode
  surfaces the flag out of emitFileWith and emits one shared goal_options.go.
- Files: internal/backend/lower.go (optionConstruction, optionPrelude),
  internal/backend/emit.go (usedOptionHelper field, tryOptionValue, expr()
  interception, file() end-append, emitFileWith returns usedOption),
  internal/backend/package.go (shared goal_options.go), internal/backend/backend_test.go
  (TestASTEngineLowersOptionInValuePositions). Existing
  TestASTEngineLowersNestedOptionInResult + whole corpus/pipeline tier stay green
  (the return/Result.Ok optionValueExpr path is untouched).
- Learnings: see the new Codebase Patterns entries (single expr() seam, runtime-flag
  end-of-file helper vs over-counting static scan, helper-comment Option. gotcha).

## [2026-06-28T09:00:00Z] - US-025
- Proved US-025 "Add corpus interpreter runner": the implementation-independent
  behavioral conformance tier now judges the goscript INTERPRETER on the same
  yardstick as the Go backend. internal/corpus.RunInterp loads a doctest corpus
  case, runs it through internal/interp.RunDoctests, and asserts each `///  >>>`
  example's evaluated runtime result matches its documented expected value — the
  interpreter analogue of RunDoctestExec (which transpiles + runs `go test`), but
  in-process with NO Go toolchain. A wrong result, a parse/eval failure, a
  wrong-kind case, or a doctest case with zero examples is a LOUD, case-identified
  error, never a silent pass.

  []DoctestFailure, ran int, err error). Parses + sema.Resolve + New, then for each
  FuncDecl.Doc.Doctests evaluates the input expression via ip.evalExpr(expr, ip.root)
  and compares Value.String() to the trimmed joined Expected. DoctestFailure{Func,
  Input,Expected,Got}. parseDoctestExpr wraps the input in
  `func __doctest__(){ __dt := <input> }`, parses it (parser exposes only ParseFile,
  no ParseExpr), and lifts the AssignStmt.Rhs[0] expr node. A value mismatch is a
  returned failure; a structural/eval problem is a returned error.

  no failures), TestRunDoctestsReportsMismatch (mutated `/// 5`->`/// 6` -> one

- history/20260627-feature-us-025-corpus-interpreter-runner/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - The interpreter has NO ParseExpr — parser exposes only ParseFile. To evaluate a
    bare goal EXPRESSION (a doctest `>>>` line, or any future "run this snippet"
    need), wrap it in `func __x(){ __dt := <expr> }`, ParseFile it, and lift
    AssignStmt.Rhs[0]; then ip.evalExpr(expr, ip.root) against an interp built from
    the real program (funcs/enums/methods already registered by New).
  - Value.String() IS the doctest behavioral oracle: it already renders int->`5`,
    string->`"abab"` (strconv.Quote), bool->`true` — exactly the Go-literal spelling
    the doctest goldens paste as the `want :=` literal. So a result that passes the
    Go doctest tier passes RunInterp and vice versa, with no separate renderer.

    parser/sema/ast/cap/token, never corpus). The RunInterp corpus test stays in

    RunInterp; US-026 (CLI interp engine) is separate.

    seams (interp.New/evalExpr/Value.String, corpus.Case/Load/manifest). The interp
    doctest eval does NOT run main or the sema gate; it evaluates expressions
