## [2026-06-28T08:10:00Z] - US-024
- Proved US-024 "Enforce capability denial": the goscript interpreter's
  capability gate now REFUSES a denied effect loudly instead of silently
  skipping it. Running under a cap.CapabilitySet that does not grant cap.Stdout
  makes the standard-output effect (fmt.Println via emitStdout) fail with a
  LOCATED, NAMED CapabilityError — nothing reaches the sink — turning the US-023
  placeholder (not-granted -> return nil) into a real sandbox refusal. The
  granted path is unchanged.
- internal/interp/interp.go: added `type CapabilityError{Cap cap.Capability;
  Pos token.Pos}` with `Error() -> "interp: <line:col>: capability denied: <Cap>
  not granted"` (named via cap.Capability.String(), located via token.Pos.String()).
  emitStdout's signature gained the effect's source position
  (`emitStdout(pos token.Pos, write func(io.Writer) error) error`); the
  not-granted branch now returns `CapabilityError{Cap: cap.Stdout, Pos: pos}`
  WITHOUT calling write (FR-4 nothing written). cap + token + fmt were already
  imported — no new dependency, US-022 gate holds.
- internal/interp/host.go: evalHostCall's fmt.Println interception passes
  `sel.Pos()` into emitStdout so the refusal is located at the call.
- internal/interp/cap_io_test.go: the existing direct emitStdout call (US-023's
  TestEmitStdoutRoutesThroughConfiguredSink) now passes `token.Pos{}` for the new
  position arg (added the token import).
- internal/interp/cap_deny_test.go (new): TestPrintlnUnderDeniedStdoutIsRefused
  (DenyAll -> Run returns a CapabilityError naming Stdout, located, buf empty),
  TestEmitStdoutDeniedReturnsLocatedNamedErrorAndSkipsWrite (gate drives directly:
  the write func is NOT invoked under denial; error located at the supplied 7:2),
  TestPrintlnUnderGrantedStdoutStillPrints (FR-5 regression: GrantAll still prints
  "hello 42\n", nil error). stdlib testing, no testify.
- prd.json (US-024 passes:true), progress.txt
- history/20260627-feature-us-024-enforce-capability-denial/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - A denied capability is a RETURNED typed error (CapabilityError), NOT a
    panicSignal: it is a host-policy refusal of an effect, matchable via
    errors.As, distinct from a program panic. Future effect sites (time/env/file/
    net) reuse this: gate the effect on caps.Has(cap.X) and, when not granted,
    return CapabilityError{Cap: cap.X, Pos: <effect pos>} BEFORE performing it.
  - emitStdout now REQUIRES the effect's source position so the refusal is
    located; the only caller (host.go fmt.Println) supplies sel.Pos(). Any new
    stdout effect routed through emitStdout must thread a real position (a test
    calling it directly can pass token.Pos{} or a synthetic token.Pos{Line,Col}).
  - token.Pos is a STRUCT ({Offset,Line,Col}), not an int — you cannot pass 0;
    use token.Pos{} (or a literal with Line/Col) when a position is unavailable.

## [2026-06-28T07:30:00Z] - US-023
- Proved US-023 "Route runtime IO through cap": the goscript interpreter's host
  effects now flow through a cap.CapabilitySet instead of touching the OS
  directly. The default Run path runs with FULL authority (cap.GrantAll), and
  the standard-output effect targets a CONFIGURABLE sink (defaulting to
  os.Stdout) so a host — or a test — can capture what a program prints. The one
  existing effect site (fmt.Println) is routed through the new gate; the future
  time/env reads reuse the same seam. Denial-to-error is the NEXT story (US-024):
  here the not-granted branch performs no write and returns nil.
- internal/interp/interp.go: Interp gained `caps cap.CapabilitySet` + `stdout
  io.Writer`. New is now `New(file, info, opts ...Option)` — it defaults
  caps=cap.GrantAll() and stdout=os.Stdout, then applies options (existing 2-arg
  call sites are unaffected by the variadic). Added `type Option func(*Interp)`
  with `WithCapabilities` / `WithStdout`, and the capability gate
  `emitStdout(write func(io.Writer) error) error` — writes through ip.stdout only
  when caps.Has(cap.Stdout) (nil-sink falls back to os.Stdout). Imports gained
  io, os, goal/internal/cap.
- internal/interp/host.go: removed the effectful "fmt.Println" entry from the
  pure package-level hostFuncs registry (a pure func can't reach the interpreter
  sink/caps) and intercepted it in evalHostCall, routing it through
  ip.emitStdout(func(w io.Writer){ fmt.Fprintln(w, goArgs(args)...) }). Swapped
  the os import for io. The pure shims (Sprintf/Sprint/Errorf/errors.New) stay in
  the registry; the unresolved-symbol refusal path is unchanged.

    (and its future siblings emitTime/emitEnv): consult ip.caps.Has(cap.X) and,
    when granted, perform the effect through the interpreter-held sink. US-024
    (deny -> located, named error) only needs to turn the not-granted branch

## [2026-06-28T06:45:00Z] - US-022
- Proved US-022 "Gate interp on native sema only": the goscript interpreter's
  Run() now validates the program through the NATIVE sema checks BEFORE any
  evaluation. A static-guarantee violation (canonically a non-exhaustive
  `match`) is a LOUD, LOCATED refusal before `func main` is found or run;
  Warning-severity diagnostics (located deferrals like an unresolved-enum
  match) do NOT block. The gate reads ONLY internal/sema — the interpreter
  never reaches for go/types or internal/typecheck, so goscript runs in a host
  with no Go toolchain (REWRITE-ARCHITECTURE.md §3.2: types checked statically,
  erased at runtime).
- internal/interp/interp.go: Run() now calls the new `gate()` as its first
  statement (before findMain). `gate()` iterates `sema.Check(ip.file, ip.info)`
  and returns `interp: refused before run: <line:col>: [<code>] <message>` for
  the FIRST sema.Error (skipping sema.Warning), nil otherwise. Uses only the
  already-imported goal/internal/sema — NO new dependency.
- internal/interp/gate_test.go (new): TestRunRefusesNonExhaustiveMatch (refusal
  names the code + is located), TestRunAllowsExhaustiveMatch (no false refusal),
  TestRunDoesNotBlockOnWarning (unresolved-enum warning is not refused),
  TestInterpHasNoGoTypesOrTypecheckDep (`go list -deps goal/internal/interp`
  contains neither go/types nor goal/internal/typecheck). stdlib testing, no
  testify.
- prd.json (US-022 passes:true), progress.txt
- history/20260627-feature-us-022-gate-interp-on-native-sema-only/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - sema.Check(file, info) is the ONE native validation aggregate (exhaustive,
    fields, must-use, implements, question, closed, assert, convert). Any later
    interp story needing a pre-run static guard reuses Run()'s gate() — it is
    the native-only validation seam. Refuse on Severity==Error; let Warning
    through (it is a deferral, not a violated guarantee).
  - PARSER GOTCHA (cost a test rerun): the parser does NOT insert a semicolon
    after a BARE `return` before a newline, so a `=> return` match arm followed
    by ANOTHER arm swallows the next arm's pattern as the return expression
    ("expected IDENT, found =>"). In a multi-arm test fixture use a block-body
    arm (`=> {}`) or `return <value>`; a bare-return arm only parses as the
    LAST arm before `}`.

## [2026-06-28T06:10:00Z] - US-021
- Proved US-021 "Eval derive and from": the goscript interpreter now evaluates
  `derive func` conversions field-by-field over the resolved sema facts. Each
  target field is sourced from its same-named source field: identity (sf==tf)
  copies the value through; a differing type is bridged through its registered
  `from func` (sema.Info.FromRegistry); nested in-file structs and slice/array/
  map containers recurse over a TOTAL element conversion. A fallible `(T, error)`
  derive threads a conversion's error as its second result; an unsourced or
  unconvertible target field is a LOUD, located refusal, never a silent zero.
  This is the runtime analogue of the Go backend's genConversion/resolveField,
  but it builds a runtime Value and selects each strategy from the resolved sema
  TYPE STRINGS (the interp erases static types).
- internal/interp/interp.go: added `derives map[string]*ast.FuncDecl` to Interp
  (init in New). registerFuncs now routes a `fn.Mod == ast.FuncDerive` decl into
  `derives` (even when bodyless) instead of binding it as an ordinary callable —
  a derive is NOT runnable as a body (`_` skips + `...derive(src)` fill). A
  `from func` keeps its ordinary registration (it has a real body) and is invoked
  by name as the bridge conversion.
- internal/interp/derive.go (new): evalDerive (intercepted call -> [target] for a
  total derive, [target, errVal] for a fallible one), deriveConvert (build the
  target struct map: overrides first, then same-named-field fill, then zero-fill a
  `_`-skipped field; nil pointer source -> zero target; unsourced field ->
  located refusal), convertFieldValue (identity / registry total / registry
  fallible / slice / array / map / nested-struct recursion; pointer/Option and
  anything else -> loud "no conversion"). A fallible leaf error rides the new
  `deriveErrVal` signal so the enclosing derive returns it. callNamedConv invokes
  a registered `from func` by root-scope lookup + callFunc (mirrors
  callConversion). Local type-string splitters (deriveTargetType, deriveOverridesOf,
  findFieldFold, derefTypeName, sliceElem, arrayElem, mapKeyVal, typeName) mirror
  backend/lower.go so interp imports NO internal/backend (US-022 envelope).
- internal/interp/eval.go: evalExpr's Ident case now resolves the predeclared
  `nil` to NilVal (so a `from func ... (T, error)` can `return T{}, nil` /
  `return v, nil`). evalCallMulti intercepts an Ident-callee call whose name is a
  registered derive (not shadowed) -> evalDerive, before the generic call path.
- internal/interp/derive_test.go (new): TestDeriveTotalNestedStructAndRegistryBridge
  (the features/12 derive_nested_struct shape: identity Name, nested Addr->AddrV2,
  Zip string->Code bridge), TestDeriveFallibleSucceedsAndReturnsNilError,
  TestDeriveFalliblePropagatesConversionError (errors.New "empty id" value),
  TestDeriveUnsourcedFieldIsRefused ("not sourced" + names field B). stdlib
  testing, no testify.
- prd.json (US-021 passes:true), progress.txt
- history/20260627-feature-us-021-eval-derive-and-from/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - A `derive func` is bodyless (or carries a `_`/`...derive(src)` body the
    ordinary evaluator cannot run), so it is NOT an ordinary callable. Register it
    in a dedicated `ip.derives` map and intercept the call in evalCallMulti. A
    `from func` is the opposite — it has a real body, registers normally, and is
    the bridge conversion invoked by name (callNamedConv, like callConversion).
  - Conversion strategy is chosen from the sema TYPE STRINGS (Field.Type,
    FromRegistry keys), exactly like the backend — but the interp produces a
    Value. The backend's string splitters port verbatim; keep them LOCAL to interp
    so the US-022 envelope (no internal/backend) holds (go list -deps confirms).
  - The predeclared `nil` identifier was previously unhandled (it fell through to
    scope.Lookup and 404'd); evalExpr now maps it to NilVal. A fallible `from func`
    success path (`return v, nil`) and any future nil-returning host shim depend
    on this.
  - A fallible field conversion error is threaded via the `deriveErrVal` sentinel
    (errors.As) so a `(T, error)` derive surfaces it as its second result; a
    container element conversion must be TOTAL (a fallible element conv is
    refused), matching the backend's elemConv contract.
  - Pointer/Option field recursion is a deliberate loud refusal (the interp models
    no address-of); the file-mode features/12 fixtures don't need it and
    cross-package derives stay on the package-mode corpus runner.
---

## [2026-06-28T05:20:00Z] - US-020
- Proved US-020 "Eval defaults expansion": the goscript interpreter now expands
  a `...defaults` spread in a STRUCT composite literal at construction. Every
  declared field the literal did NOT set explicitly is filled with that field's
  safe runtime zero value; every explicitly set field is preserved. The fill is
  position-INDEPENDENT (runs after all explicit elements are collected), so
  `...defaults` before or after an explicit field never overwrites it.
- internal/interp/eval.go:
  - evalCompositeLit's `case *ast.Ident:` (struct) branch now accepts a
    `*ast.SpreadElement`: `X` == Ident "defaults" sets a wantDefaults flag; any
    OTHER spread (`...derive`) is a LOCATED refusal ("only ...defaults is
    supported") — US-021's job, refused loud not silent. After the element loop,
    wantDefaults calls fillDefaults.
  - fillDefaults(typeName, fields, pos): reads the declared fields from
    ip.info.Structs (via structFields, base-name keyed) — an UNKNOWN struct type
    is a located "unknown struct type" refusal, never a silent empty fill — and
    fills each absent field with ip.zeroValue(f.Type, 0).
  - zeroValue(typ, depth): the runtime analogue of backend zeroLit, derived from
    the SEMA TYPE STRING (the interp erases static types): ""/false/0 for
    string/bool/int+float kinds; NilVal for *T/map/chan/func/non-empty-iface/
    any/error; an EMPTY SliceVal for []T (so range/len stay valid); a RECURSIVELY
    zero-filled StructVal for a named in-file struct (depth-guarded); NilVal for
    an unresolvable named type. Reads ONLY sema.Info — no internal/backend.
  - baseTypeName(t): strips leading `*` and `pkg.` qualifier (mirrors
    scan.BaseType locally so interp imports neither scan nor backend). Added the
    `strings` import.
- internal/interp/defaults_test.go (new): TestDefaultsFillsOmittedPrimitivesAndPreservesSet
  (name/logins preserved, email""/active false defaulted),
  TestDefaultsDoesNotOverwriteExplicitFieldBeforeOrAfter (spread BEFORE an
  explicit field), TestDefaultsFillsNestedStructAndSlice (omitted Addr -> zeroed
  Addr{}, omitted []string -> empty slice; explicit Addr preserved),
  TestNonDefaultsSpreadIsRefused (hand-built `...derive` -> error),
  TestDefaultsUnknownStructIsRefused. Modeled on features/08-no-zero-value
  defaults_primitives + defaults_refs. stdlib testing, no testify.
- prd.json (US-020 passes:true), progress.txt
- history/20260627-feature-us-020-eval-defaults-expansion/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - `...defaults` parses to *ast.SpreadElement{X: *ast.Ident "defaults"} inside a
    *ast.CompositeLit — intercept it in evalCompositeLit's struct branch, NOT in
    evalExpr. A bare `...derive(s)` would be the same node with a different X
    (US-021). The declared-field source is sema.Info.Structs (Name+Type strings);
    the interp has no Go types, so zeros are computed from the type STRING.
  - The interp evaluates NO top-level `const`/iota: a test program cannot
    reference an enum/const value like `RoleMember` (undefined at runtime). Set
    explicitly-preserved fields to plain literals, or default them. Likewise a
    DEFINED type over a primitive (`type Role int`) has no alias table in
    sema.Info, so zeroValue("Role") currently yields NilVal, not IntVal(0) — the
    feature-08 fixtures set such fields explicitly so it is unexercised; if a
    future story needs it, resolve defined-type underlyings from ip.file's
    TypeSpecs (as backend buildTypeDecls does).
  - A defaulted slice is an EMPTY SliceVal (not NilVal) so len/range/append stay
    valid — the one intentional divergence from backend zeroLit's literal "nil"
    (behaviorally identical for a Go nil slice).
  - interp deps stay clean for the US-022 gate (go list -deps ./internal/interp:
    no go/types, internal/backend, internal/typecheck).

## [2026-06-28T04:40:00Z] - US-019
- Proved US-019 "Eval assert at runtime": the goscript interpreter now evaluates
  goal's `assert` statement — a true condition is a no-op (evaluation continues),
  a false condition raises a LOUD, located panic carrying the assertion message
  ("erase the guarantee, panic-not-silent"). Both the bare form
  (`assert amount > 0`) and the printf-message form
  (`assert age >= 0, "...", age`) are handled.
- internal/interp/assert.go (new): `execAssert(s, scope)` evaluates s.Cond,
  refuses a non-bool condition descriptively (`interp: assert condition must be
  bool, got <kind>`, mirroring execIf), returns nil on true, and on false raises
  `panicSignal{StrVal("<pos>: assertion failed: <cond>[: <fmt msg>]")}`. The
  panicSignal reuses the established unrecovered control signal (no call/loop/
  switch boundary catches it — surfaces to Run/host exactly like the `panic`
  builtin and the unreachable-match default). The message form evaluates s.Msg
  (must be string) + s.Args and appends `fmt.Sprintf(format, goArgs(args)...)`,
  matching the Go backend's assertStmt lowering. exprText (also in assert.go) is a
  self-contained AST->text renderer for the condition (Ident/BasicLit/Paren/Unary/
  Star/Binary/Selector/Index/Call; operators via token.Kind.String(); unknown ->
  "<expr>") — the interp holds NO source bytes (US-022 native-only envelope), so
  the condition text is rendered from the AST, NOT sliced from source and NOT via
  internal/backend.
- internal/interp/interp.go: execStmt's type switch gains
  `case *ast.AssertStmt: return ip.execAssert(s, scope)`.
- internal/interp/assert_test.go (new): TestAssertTrueIsNoOp (goodWithdraw=90),
  TestAssertFalseBarePanicsLocated (panicSignal contains "assertion failed" +
  "amount > 0" + a located prefix), TestAssertFalseMessageFormFormatsMessage
  (formatted "age must be non-negative, got -3"), TestAssertMessageFormTrueIsNoOp,
  TestAssertNonBoolConditionIsRefused (hand-built AssertStmt with an int cond ->
  descriptive "must be bool" error, NOT a panic). Modeled on
  features/10-assert/examples/{bank,message}.goal. stdlib testing, no testify.
- prd.json (US-019 passes:true), progress.txt
- history/20260627-feature-us-019-eval-assert-at-runtime/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - `assert` is just another loud panic on the existing panicSignal channel —
    no new boundary handling. Detect it in a test via errors.As(err, &panicSignal).
    A failing assert in a function body propagates OUT of evalExpr(call(...)) as
    an error (callFunc does NOT recover panicSignal), so evalFnErr observes it.
  - The interp has NO source-text renderer of its own and MUST NOT import
    internal/backend (US-022). When a runtime message needs source-ish text (here
    the asserted condition), render it from the AST with a small local printer —
    the same pattern any future "quote the source expression" runtime message
    should reuse. Operators render via token.Kind.String() (no token import
    needed: Op is already a token.Kind field on the node).
  - The printf-message form reuses host.go's goArgs bridge + fmt.Sprintf, so the
    interpreter's assert message text matches the Go backend's lowered output.
  - interp deps stay clean for the US-022 gate (go list -deps ./internal/interp:
    no go/types, internal/backend, internal/typecheck).

## [2026-06-28T04:00:00Z] - US-018
- Proved US-018 "Eval implements dispatch": the goscript interpreter honors
  `implements` — a struct satisfying a sealed/ordinary interface is dispatched
  through the interface, calling the correct concrete method at runtime. NO
  production change was needed: interface method dispatch already rides entirely
  on the US-010 method registry (registerMethods -> ip.methods, tryMethodCall,
  callMethod). Because the interpreter ERASES static types at runtime
  (REWRITE-ARCHITECTURE §3.2), an interface-typed binding simply HOLDS the
  concrete struct value, and tryMethodCall dispatches structurally on
  recv.Struct.TypeID — so differently-typed values, value receivers, pointer
  receivers, and values read out of a heterogeneous interface-element slice all
  dispatch to the right concrete method with no interface-boxing wrapper.
- internal/interp/implements_test.go (new): TestImplementsValueReceiverDifferentTypes
  (Stringer{Describe() string} over Point/Label through a `render(s Stringer)`
  param), TestImplementsPointerReceiverThroughInterface (Resetter{Reset()} with a
  pointer-receiver Counter.Reset called through a `use(r Resetter)` param — the
  mutation is observed back through the caller's value, NO `&` needed),
  TestImplementsHeterogeneousSliceDispatch ([]Shape{Square,Rect} ranged+summed =
  17), TestImplementsMissingMethodIsLoud (a Plain with no Describe -> a loud
  error, not a silent zero). stdlib testing, no testify.
- prd.json (US-018 passes:true), progress.txt
- history/20260627-feature-us-018-eval-implements-dispatch/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Interface dispatch is FREE on top of US-010: there is no interface value at
    runtime, only the concrete struct, so calling `iface.M()` is just
    tryMethodCall on the concrete TypeID. US-018 added ONLY a conformance test —
    confirming the US-010 prediction ("an interface value dispatched to a
    concrete method reuses callMethod").
  - Pointer-receiver dispatch through an interface works WITHOUT `&`: the
    interpreter has NO address-of operator (evalUnary refuses `&` with
    "unsupported unary operator &"), but a goal value shares its underlying
    *StructValue, so a pointer-receiver method (recvIsPointer -> callMethod skips
    the copyStructValue) mutates the caller's value. General first-class pointers
    / `&` remain unimplemented and out of scope for the current stories.
  - PARSER LIMITATION (pre-existing, not US-018's concern): a VOID interface
    method followed by another method fails to parse (`type R interface { A();
    B() int }` -> "expected IDENT, found ("). A single void method (`Reset()`)
    or all-returning methods parse fine. Any interp test that needs a multi-
    method interface must give every method a return type, or use single-method
    interfaces — which is what implements_test.go does.
  - interp deps stay clean for the US-022 gate (go list -deps ./internal/interp:
    no go/types, internal/backend, internal/typecheck).

## [2026-06-27T00:00:00Z] - US-017
- Added postfix `?` (ast.UnwrapExpr) to the goscript interpreter as NON-LOCAL
  early return — the second of the two genuinely non-Go runtime mechanics. On
  Result.Ok / Option.Some it yields the unwrapped payload and continues; on
  Result.Err / Option.None it unwinds to the enclosing function's own
  Result.Err(...) / Option.None; closed-E `from` conversions are applied to the
  error during propagation.
- internal/interp/interp.go: added `fnStack []sema.FuncSig` to Interp — the stack
  of currently-executing function signatures (innermost last). callFunc pushes
  `sigFor(fn.Name)` and callMethod pushes a zero (none-shaped) sig; BOTH pop via
  `defer` so any unwind (returnSignal/panicSignal/error) keeps the stack balanced.
  New nil-safe helpers `sigFor(name)` (reads info.FuncSignatures) and `curSig()`
  (top of stack, ok=false when empty).
- internal/interp/eval.go: evalExpr gained `case *ast.UnwrapExpr` -> evalUnwrap.
  evalUnwrap evaluates the operand, then dispatches on Variant.TypeID: a Result
  operand REQUIRES a Result-returning enclosing function (ModeResult/
  ModeResultClosed) checked UP FRONT so the erased static guarantee fails loudly
  on BOTH the Ok and Err paths; Ok -> payloadValue (unwrapped), Err ->
  propagateErr. An Option operand requires ModeOption; Some -> payloadValue, None
  -> propagateNone. A non-variant operand (or a non-Result/Option variant) is a
  located refusal. propagateErr raises returnSignal{[Result.Err(out)]} — recovered
  by callFunc exactly like an explicit `return Result.Err(...)`; for
  ModeResultClosed when calleeErrType(u.X) != caller E it applies the FromRegistry
  conversion (callConversion looks the `from func` up in the ROOT scope — it is an
  ordinary callable registered by registerFuncs — and calls it via callFunc).
  calleeErrType resolves the callee E only for a direct `f(...)?` call.
- internal/interp/question_test.go (new): TestQuestionResultOkContinues/
  ...ErrEarlyReturns (post-? statement proven NOT to run), OptionSome/None,
  ClosedEAppliesFromConversion (ParseError->AppError via `from func toApp`),
  ClosedEOkContinues, ClosedESameENoConversion (Err payload unchanged),
  OutsidePropagatingFunctionRefused, OnNonVariantRefused. Programs are MODELED ON
  the 05/06 fixtures but adapted so the Err/None/conversion branches actually fire
  (the fixtures return Ok/None unconditionally). stdlib testing, no testify.
- prd.json (US-017 passes:true), progress.txt
- history/20260627-feature-us-017-eval-question-mark-unwinding/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - The CURRENT-FUNCTION signature stack (Interp.fnStack, pushed in callFunc/
    callMethod, popped via defer) is the seam any future construct needing the
    enclosing function's shape should reuse. At a `?` site, curSig() correctly
    reflects the ENCLOSING function because the inner operand call already
    pushed+popped its own sig before evalUnwrap inspects the result.
  - `?` early-return is just a returnSignal carrying the enclosing function's own
    Err/None variant — NO new boundary handling: callFunc/callMethod already
    recover returnSignal. The propagated value is identical in shape to an
    explicit `return Result.Err(...)`/`return Option.None`.
  - The closed-E `from` conversion func is an ordinary root-scope callable
    (registerFuncs binds every FuncDecl incl. `from func`), invoked via callFunc;
    its src->tgt mapping is sema.FromRegistry[[2]string{calleeE, callerE}].
  - FR-5 loudness: validate the enclosing function shape UP FRONT (before
    unwrapping), keyed on the operand's TypeID, so a misplaced `?` refuses on the
    success path too, not only on Err/None.
  - interp deps stay clean for the US-022 gate (go list -deps ./internal/interp:
    no go/types, internal/backend, internal/typecheck).

## Codebase Patterns
- A `?` site is validated/lowered in THREE parallel layers that must agree:
  internal/analyze (lexical, what `goal check` runs via internal/check),
  internal/sema (the native check the interp gate runs), and internal/backend
  (the `?` destructure lowering). A `recv.M()?` callee resolves through the
  RECEIVER's type method set, not by name: analyze reads the receiver var's
  declared type lexically (analyze/methods.go scopeVarType) and the backend reads
  it from a per-function recvTypes map (built in funcDecl from d.Recv + params).
  The method's resolved signature MUST carry its Result/Option MODE (stored as
  `Method.Return FuncSig` in both analyze and sema), or a `Result[T,error]`
  method `?` mis-resolves as a non-error callee. Both concrete (`Methods`) and
  interface (`Interfaces`) method sets are consulted.
- A `sealed interface X {…}` is a distinct decl node: `*ast.SealedInterfaceDecl`
  in sema (NOT a `type X interface`), and a `sealed interface` token sequence in
  analyze (NOT caught by the `type`-keyed analyzeTypeDecls). Its method set must
  be resolved into Info.Interfaces / Tables.Interfaces explicitly — sema only
  flagged it in Info.Sealed and analyze only set Tables.Sealed before US-003, so
  anything keyed off the interface's METHODS (a `?` on a sealed-iface method, and
  potentially implements/hover) needs the body parsed, not just the name flagged.
- Value-position match lowering (enum AND Result/Option) reuses ONE set of
  position-parameterized emitters keyed by matchPos: enumMatch(m,pos,name),
  resultMatch/closedResultMatch/optionMatch(m,pos,name). Each wraps its arm bodies
  through armWrap (posStmt=bare, posReturn=`return <body>`, posVar=`name = <body>`)
  — renamed arms via armBodyRenamedWrap. The value-position DISPATCH lives in
  exactly three seams: returnStmt (posReturn), tryVarMatch (posVar, explicit `var
  name T`), tryAssignMatch (posVar, type via inferMatchType). A statement match
  goes through matchStmt with posStmt. To add value-position support for any new
  match subject kind, generalize its statement-position emitter to (m,pos,name) +
  armWrap and add a qualifier branch in those three dispatch sites — do NOT add a
  separate value-path. inferMatchType only resolves string/bool/enum arm bodies, so
  a `:=` (untyped) assignment whose arms aren't inferable keeps a located deferral;
  richer arm bodies need `var x T = match` or `return match`.
- AST-backend value-position lowering of Option construction rides on a SINGLE
  seam: the top of emitter.expr (emit.go). Every value position — a var/assign
  RHS, a call argument, a struct-literal field, and slice/map-literal elements —
  routes through expr(), so intercepting there (e.tryOptionValue) lowers
  Option.None->nil / Option.Some(ident)->&ident / Option.Some(other)->goalSome(other)
  everywhere at once. optionConstruction (lower.go) is the SINGLE classifier
  ("none"/"some-addr"/"some-box"); do not duplicate the Option-shape match. The
  pre-existing return/Result.Ok path (optionValueExpr/emitOptionReturn) handles the
  construction itself and never reaches expr(), so there is no double-lowering —
  leave it untouched.
- A backend helper func needed only in SOME outputs (e.g. the goalSome Option box)
  is emitted at the END of the file gated by a RUNTIME flag set when it is actually
  used (emitter.usedOptionHelper), NOT a static AST pre-scan. Go package-level
  decls are order-independent, so end-of-file placement is valid, and a runtime
  flag avoids the over-counting a static scan suffers (a scan cannot tell a
  value-position Some that boxes via goalSome from a return-position Some that the
  hoisted-temp path lowers, so it would inject an unused helper and break goldens).
  For package mode, surface the flag out of emitFileWith and emit ONE shared
  goal_options.go (mirrors the goal_prelude.go result-sum sharing).
- When asserting "no `Option.` token survived" in a backend test, beware the
  emitted helper's OWN doc comment: keep generated-helper comments free of the
  literal `Option.<Ident>` sequence or the substring check false-positives.
- The goscript interpreter validates input through the NATIVE sema aggregate
  only: Run()'s gate() runs sema.Check(file, info) before evaluating main and
  refuses on the FIRST sema.Error (Warnings are deferrals that do NOT block).
  sema.Check is the one native validation seam (exhaustive/fields/must-use/
  implements/question/closed/assert/convert) — any pre-run static guard reuses
  it. internal/interp must NEVER depend on go/types or internal/typecheck
  (TestInterpHasNoGoTypesOrTypecheckDep pins this via `go list -deps`).
- The goscript interpreter's host effects are CAPABILITY-MEDIATED (US-023):
  Interp carries `caps cap.CapabilitySet` + a configurable `stdout io.Writer`,
  constructed via `New(file, info, opts ...Option)` (defaults cap.GrantAll() +
  os.Stdout; WithCapabilities/WithStdout override). Every stdout effect flows
  through `emitStdout(pos token.Pos, write func(io.Writer) error)` — it writes
  through ip.stdout only when caps.Has(cap.Stdout). An EFFECTFUL stdlib shim
  (fmt.Println) cannot live in the pure package-level hostFuncs map — it is
  intercepted by key in evalHostCall and routed through the gate (passing
  sel.Pos()); pure value shims stay in the registry. US-024 made denial REAL: the
  not-granted branch returns a LOCATED, NAMED CapabilityError{Cap,Pos} (a returned
  typed error, errors.As-matchable — NOT a panicSignal) and performs no write.
  Future effects (time/env/file/net) reuse the same emit-gate pattern: gate on
  caps.Has(cap.X), else return CapabilityError{Cap: cap.X, Pos: effectPos}. cap is
  dependency-free, so it does not breach the US-022 dependency gate. NOTE token.Pos
  is a struct ({Offset,Line,Col}), not an int — use token.Pos{} when unavailable.
- PARSER: no semicolon is inserted after a BARE `return` before a newline, so a
  `=> return` match arm followed by another arm swallows the next arm's pattern
  ("expected IDENT, found =>"). In a multi-arm fixture use a block-body arm
  (`=> {}`) or `return <value>`; a bare-return arm only parses as the LAST arm.
- The goscript interpreter (internal/interp) evaluates NO top-level `const`/iota
  bindings yet, and sema.Info carries no defined-type/alias table — so an interp
  test program cannot reference an enum const (e.g. `RoleMember` is "undefined"
  at runtime), and a runtime zero of a defined type over a primitive
  (`type Role int`) resolves through interp.zeroValue to NilVal, not IntVal(0).
  When writing interp test fixtures, set such fields with plain literals or
  default them; if a story ever needs defined-type underlyings, resolve them
  from ip.file's TypeSpecs the way internal/backend buildTypeDecls does.
- The goscript-runtime PRD (US-001..US-028) builds the tree-walking interpreter
  (planned internal/interp) + capability model (internal/cap) over the shared
  AST+sema front-end. internal/cap (US-001) is the authority seam: a Capability
  iota enum + CapabilitySet{bits uint64} bitset with Has (value recv) / Grant
  (ptr recv) + GrantAll()/DenyAll() constructors + package-private
  allCapabilities() (single source of truth for "every capability", mirrored to
  the enum — the exhaustive test and GrantAll both iterate it). v1 grants
  everything by default; deny is host opt-in, enforcement deferred to later
  stories. Doc: docs/goscript/restriction-diff.md.
- Zero-dependency: stdlib only. Tests use stdlib `testing` (NO testify), even
  though the injected go.md rule mentions testify — the project constraint wins.
- LSP go-to-definition (US-048) introduces the AST SYMBOL GRAPH the later editor
  stories (US-049 hover, US-050 references/rename) build on. internal/lsp/
  definition.go resolveDefinition parses (parser.ParseFile), builds a name-keyed
  declIndex (funcs/types/variants[enum][tag] -> declaration Range) over
  file.Decls BEFORE walking references (so a forward call resolves), then
  collectRefs (refVisitor, keyed by structural parent exactly like
  semantictokens roleVisitor) records each reference identifier's byte span ->
  target declaration Range. The handler maps the 0-based cursor to a byte offset
  with offsetForPosition (the inverse of check.OffsetToPosition — none existed in
  the tree) and returns the ref whose [start,end) covers it. Nil *Location
  marshals to JSON null, the best-effort contract shared with documentSymbol /
  semanticTokens (unknown URI / no symbol / unparseable -> null, never an error).
  Variants are keyed UNDER their enum because a variant tag is ALSO its own
  declaration ident; tests must locate the reference occurrence, not the first
  (declaration) occurrence. Resolution is single-document — locals, params,
  qualified imports, and cross-file are out of scope for this milestone.
- New packages live under `internal/`; fixtures go in a sibling `testdata/` dir
  (see internal/{analyze,check,pipeline,corpus}/testdata).
- Verify gates (prd.json verifyCommands): `go build ./...`, `go vet ./...`,
  `go test ./... -count=1`. All must be green before committing.
- AST-driven tools that must PRESERVE source formatting (internal/fix, and the
  coming goal fmt / LSP edits) compute byte ranges from node Pos()/End() offsets
  and emit minimal scan.Replacement edits via scan.Splice (pure string utils, not
  lexing) — never print the AST (it reflows). The parser DROPS // and /* comments,
  so any "don't drop a comment" guard must scan the raw source byte range
  (spanHasComment over token.Pos.Offset), not the AST.
- Follow REWRITE-ARCHITECTURE.md phasing; §10 details Phases 0–2 (the approved
  scope). Phase 0 = corpus hardening (US-001..US-010).
- Each story runs through the morse-code `feature` workflow in --automode on the
  current branch (no new branch); human-review gates are passed via
  `morse-code workflow resume`.
- The golden corpus is indexed by `corpus/manifest.json` (repo root). Regenerate
  after adding/removing golden files: `go generate ./internal/corpus` (or
  `go run ./cmd/corpus-gen -root .`). Paths are repo-root-relative, slash-form.
- `internal/corpus` imports `internal/pipeline` and `internal/check`. Any test
  that delegates to a corpus runner must therefore live in an EXTERNAL `_test`
  package (`package pipeline_test` / `check_test`) to avoid an import cycle; an
  internal-package test importing corpus will not compile. Internal and external
  test packages coexist fine in one directory. From `internal/<pkg>`, repo root is
  `../..` and the manifest is `../../corpus/manifest.json` (same depth as corpus).
- Corpus cases share Kind across modes: package-mode cases are also
  Kind=transpile. Any loop selecting transpile cases for a FILE-mode runner
  (one that reads Case.Input as a single file) MUST also guard
  `c.Mode == ModeFile`, or it will misread a package fixture's directory Input.
  Package cases run through corpus.RunPackage (Mode=package) only.
- internal/parser's newParser strips ONLY token.COMMENT; token.DOC_COMMENT (`///`)
  is RETAINED in the token stream and collected before each top-level decl
  (collectDoc) to attach as ast.FuncDecl.Doc. Any new parser loop that scans
  tokens must skip a stray DOC_COMMENT (parseBlock already does) — they otherwise
  only appear at top level before a declaration.
- parser.parseIndexSuffix is the SINGLE index entry point for BOTH type position
  (typeNameFrom) and expression position (parsePostfix); it parses a comma list →
  ast.IndexExpr (1 elt) or ast.IndexListExpr (>1). parseOperand also accepts
  type-literal starts (LBRACK/MAP/STRUCT) so parseExpr can parse type args like
  []byte and so `[]byte(p)` conversions / `map[K]V{}` composites parse; compositeOK
  must list every type form (ArrayType/MapType/StructType/IndexListExpr) that may
  precede a `{`. Enum payload-field colon is OPTIONAL (`name Type` or `name: Type`).
- ast.MatchArm.Body is a generic ast.Node: parseMatchArm dispatches `{`→block,
  statement-keyword→parseStmt (e.g. `=> return true`), else→parseExpr (value-pos
  arm `=> 1`). Don't force arm bodies to Expr.
- corpus may import internal/parser (nothing in corpus's deps — pipeline/check/
  project — imports parser), so the parse gate lives in package corpus
  (parse_runner.go: Parser/ParserFunc/RunParse + CaseInputs; TestParseGate). The
  corpus runner pattern is uniform: define an interface + Func adapter, drive the
  whole manifest, t.Fatalf on zero cases.
- ast.Sexpr (internal/ast/dump.go) renders any AST node to a deterministic,
  POSITION-FREE s-expression via reflection over exported fields (skips
  token.Pos, names token.Kind/FuncMod/ChanDir, elides zero/empty fields). It
  auto-covers new node types — adding an ast node needs NO dumper change. Keep
  node fields EXPORTED or they vanish from the dump. Parser structure is pinned
  by internal/parser TestASTSnapshots against testdata/snapshots/*.sexpr; after
  an INTENTIONAL grammar/AST change regenerate with
  `go test ./internal/parser -run TestASTSnapshots -update-snapshots` and review
  the diff before committing.
- The AST engine seam (Phase 2): internal/backend defines Backend{Emit(*ast.File,
  *sema.Info)(pipeline.Output,error)} + Formatter{Format([]byte)([]byte,error)} +
  GoFormatter (go/format) + the Transpile entry (parse->sema->Emit->format) that
  satisfies corpus.Transpiler. The Go emitter is the position-FREE, format-once
  model: emit.go writes only syntactically valid, token-correct Go (spaces between
  tokens, balanced braces) and lets GoFormatter normalize layout — so emit code
  need not pretty-print, only parse. Operators/keywords render via token.Kind's
  String() (e.g. d.Tok.String(), x.Op.String()), no token import needed in emit.go.
  Unsupported nodes (every goal-specific node, plus any not-yet-wired Go form)
  return a descriptive `backend: unsupported <kind> %T` error — later stories
  (US-032+) fill them in. internal/backend's test is EXTERNAL (package
  backend_test) so it can import internal/corpus (corpus does not import backend).
- backend/emit.go field separators are CONTEXT-sensitive: param/result/receiver
  lists are comma-joined (fieldList), but STRUCT FIELDS and INTERFACE METHODS must
  be newline/semicolon-separated (structType/interfaceType) — a comma there is a
  Go SYNTAX error that the format-once GoFormatter pass reports as "generated Go
  did not parse", not a layout nit. Interface methods render `Name(params)
  results` (funcSig without the `func` keyword); embedded interfaces emit the bare
  type. goal's parser has NO func-literal-as-expression (IIFE) and NO trailing
  variadic call spread (`f(xs...)`), so neither belongs in a plain-Go fixture.
- After changing cmd/goal subcommand/flag docs (guideCommands), regenerate the
  checked-in golden: `go run ./cmd/goal ai > AI-KNOWLEDGE-BOOTSTRAP.md`
  (TestBootstrapGoldenMatches fails otherwise). No CLI flag-drift test exists; the
  guide drift test only covers diagnostic codes.
- AST-backend goal-construct LOWERING is folded into internal/backend (no separate
  `lower` package — REWRITE-ARCHITECTURE marks lower/ir OPTIONAL, and emit.go does
  direct AST->Go-text). Per-construct encoders live in internal/backend/lower.go,
  mirrored VERBATIM from the legacy internal/pass/*.go (known-good build+vet-clean
  encodings) but read off sema facts instead of token scans. backend.Transpile
  MUST call sema.Resolve(file) (NOT sema.New(), which is empty) so the emitter has
  Enums/Sealed/Methods; the emitter stores `info *sema.Info` (nil-safe accessors
  enumOf/isSealed) + a local `pointerRecv` set (sema.Methods is star-stripped, so
  pointer-vs-value receiver is recomputed by walking File.Decls). US-034+ add more
  constructs the same way: encoder in lower.go, dispatch case in emit.go decl/expr.
- The three meanings of `Enum.Variant(x)` are distinct AST nodes, so emit-time
  lowering needs NO pass-ordering hack: a payload construction is *ast.VariantLit
  (parser builds it only for >=1 labeled arg), a DATA-LESS construction
  (`Status.Pending`) stays an *ast.SelectorExpr (lower it in the SelectorExpr case,
  GUARDED by info.Enums membership + VSet so io.Writer / receiver selectors are
  untouched), and a destructuring is *ast.VariantPattern (never emitted as a value).
  Recursive e.expr over VariantLit args lowers nested constructions for free.
- Function-scoped backend lowering rides on emitter.fnKind (set+restored around
  the body in funcDecl from resultOptionKind off the result type): a `return
  Ctor(...)` is only lowered when fnKind matches, the AST analogue of the splice
  passes' sigAt/funcSpans scoping. A statement-position match parses to ExprStmt{X:
  *MatchExpr} and is intercepted in stmt()'s ExprStmt case (NOT expr()); value-
  position match stays in expr() and still errors until US-036. Match-arm binding
  renames use emitter.renames (consulted in the Ident case, set per-arm via
  armBodyRenamed+defer delete); a generic ast.Node arm Body is dispatched by
  armBody() (ast.Stmt->stmt, ast.Expr->expr-statement). US-035/036/037 extend this
  same seam (encoder in lower.go + dispatch case in emit.go).
- A struct `implements` clause (StructType.Implements) lowers to a SEPARATE
  top-level decl emitted AFTER the type decl (implementsMarkers, called from decl()
  after genDecl) — never inside the struct. structType drops the clause and emits
  plain Go. Sealed iface -> marker METHOD `func (T) isI() {}`; ordinary iface ->
  `var _ I = T{}` (or `(*T)(nil)` when T has any pointer-receiver method). A
  qualified iface (io.Writer) is never sealed (sealed are in-file) so it routes to
  the var-assertion branch; render the iface name via typeExprName (Ident/Selector).
- The AST backend uses a SCOPE-AWARE gensym, not a magic `__goal_` prefix (US-035).
  emitFile seeds emitter.fileIdents = fileIdentSet(f) (every identifier in the file,
  lower.go). funcDecl opens a per-function scope: e.taken = e.newScope() (a fresh
  COPY of fileIdents) and, for an open-E Result function, mints the named returns
  `e.okName = e.gensym("ok")` / `e.errName = e.gensym("err")` BEFORE funcSig so the
  signature and body reference identical names; all of fnKind/okName/errName/taken
  are saved+restored (defer) so siblings start clean. e.gensym(want) returns want,
  or want+N for the least N avoiding any in-scope name. CONSEQUENCE: a function whose
  source already binds `err` (e.g. result_int's strconv.Atoi) gets a non-colliding
  `err1` named return — the scope-aware win. Function-scoped names (Result returns)
  live on the emitter; LOCAL temps (statement-position match `v`/`err`/`o`, Option
  box `some`, Option `?` pointer `o`) are minted at point of use — a match may sit in
  a NON-Result function (e.g. `handle`), so its destructure names must be locals, not
  the enclosing function's returns. funcSig falls back to plain "ok"/"err" when
  e.okName=="" (a bodyless Result-returning interface method / func-type expr).
- Postfix `?` (ast.UnwrapExpr) is lowered at STATEMENT position only, intercepted in
  stmt(): AssignStmt with a single UnwrapExpr RHS (`name := expr?` / `_ := expr?`) and
  ExprStmt with an UnwrapExpr X (bare `expr?`). A Result `?` destructures the callee's
  LOWERED arity (e.calleeSig reads sema.Info.FuncSignatures[name]: a plain
  `func()error` callee -> 1 value -> `if err := f(); err != nil`, a Result callee ->
  2 -> `if _, err := f(); err != nil`) and on failure returns the function's own
  (okName, errName). An Option `?` mints a fresh pointer temp per site and returns
  nil. A `?` in a roNone function hits the descriptive "`?` outside Result/Option"
  error. A closed-E Result function (E != error) is its OWN roKind (roResultClosed),
  set in funcDecl from sema.FuncSig[name].Mode==ModeResultClosed (NOT resultOptionKind,
  which returns roNone for closed-E so funcSig emits the `Result[T,E]` type verbatim).
  closedT/closedE ride on the emitter (saved/restored like okName/errName) and feed the
  Ok/Err sum constructors + closed `?` propagation.
- Closed-E Result (feature 06) lowers to the §8.1 GENERIC SUM, not a native tuple:
  the `resultPrelude` (Result[T,E] iface + Ok/Err carriers + marker methods, in
  lower.go) is emitted ONCE per file by file(), after import decls (isImportDecl
  guard) and before the first other decl, gated by needsResultPrelude(info) (any
  func is ModeResultClosed). `Result.Ok/Err(X)` -> `Ok/Err[T,E]{Value: X}`; a closed
  `match` and closed `?` are type-switches over `Ok[T,E]`/`Err[T,E]` with a panicking
  §8.2 default. Closed-E match is dispatched on the SCRUTINEE CALLEE's mode
  (calleeMode==ModeResultClosed), NOT the enclosing function — the matching function
  may be void (e.g. `handle`). Closed `?` returns the enclosing function's own
  Err[closedT,closedE], applying the `from func` conversion
  (FromRegistry[[2]string{callee.E, caller.E}].Name) when the error types differ.
- A `from func` (ast.FuncFrom) emits as an ORDINARY Go function (the modifier is
  stripped): its src->tgt registration already lives in sema.FromRegistry (sema.Resolve
  routes from/derive to the registry, NOT FuncSignatures), so the emitted func is just
  a callable conversion. funcDecl's modifier guard allows FuncPlain+FuncFrom; FuncDerive
  still fails (US-039).
- `...defaults` (feature 08, §8.5) and `assert` (feature 10) lower in internal/backend
  the same encoder-in-lower.go + dispatch-in-emit.go way. `...defaults` is parsed as
  *ast.SpreadElement{X: Ident "defaults"} inside a *ast.CompositeLit, so route ALL
  composite literals through emitter.compositeLit (not the inline exprList): it expands
  a `...defaults` element via defaultEntries (one `name: zeroLit(type)` per omitted
  declared field; an unsafe zero — nil pointer/map/chan/func, sum type, method-iface —
  is a located e.fail). A non-`defaults` spread (`...derive`) is US-039. zeroLit/
  zeroSafety/baseType are mirrored VERBATIM from analyze.ZeroLit/internal/pass.zeroSafety
  into lower.go, but read a `typeDecls map[string]string` (emitter.buildTypeDecls walks
  File TypeSpecs: struct->"struct", interface->"interface", alias->exprText(underlying))
  + sema enum/sealed sets — the AST-native replacement for analyze.Tables.TypeDecls.
- emitter.exprText(x) renders an expr to text WITHOUT touching the main output: it uses
  a FRESH sub-emitter (sharing info/renames/typeDecls), NOT a swap of e.b. Swapping a
  used strings.Builder by value panics ("illegal use of non-zero Builder copied by
  value") via copyCheck — never `saved := e.b`. exprText powers the assert panic-message
  text and an alias's underlying-type text.
- `assert` (*ast.AssertStmt) lowers in stmt()'s new AssertStmt case (assertStmt):
  `if !(cond) { panic("assertion failed: "+condtext[ +": "+fmt.Sprintf(msg,args...)]) }`,
  condtext = exprText(Cond), the real cond re-emitted via e.expr. The printf-message form
  needs fmt: file() injects `import "fmt"` ONCE right after the package clause when
  needsFmtImport(f) (Walk finds any AssertStmt with Msg!=nil) && !importsPkg(f,"fmt").
  Imports must precede other decls, so inject before the closed-E prelude / first decl.
- `derive func` (feature 12, §12) lowers in internal/backend the same encoder-in-lower.go
  + dispatch-in-emit.go way; `from func` is ALREADY a plain func (funcDecl's FuncFrom case,
  US-037). funcDecl's d.Mod switch routes ast.FuncDerive -> deriveDecl, which OWNS the whole
  declaration (a derive has no ordinary body to emit) and returns BEFORE the Result/Option
  gensym-scope setup. deriveDecl reads the source name+type (first param) and the target
  type+fallibility from deriveTarget(d.Type.Results) (one result => total; (T,error) => the
  derive returns (T,error) and threads the error). A BODIED derive's overrides come from
  deriveOverrides: walk Body->ReturnStmt->CompositeLit.Elts; a *ast.KeyValueExpr{Key:Ident}
  is an override (value *ast.Ident "_" => SKIP, field left at its `var out` zero); the
  `...derive(src)` *ast.SpreadElement is the implicit fill marker (ignored — the unoverridden
  fields ARE the fill). genConversion emits `func name(src S) <ret> { var out T; <overrides>;
  <resolved fields>; return out[, nil] }`. resolveField is mirrored VERBATIM from
  internal/pass.resolveField but reads sema.Info.Structs (case-insensitive findSemaField) +
  sema.Info.FromRegistry: identity (sf==tf) `out.F=src.F`; registry total `out.F=conv(src.F)`;
  registry fallible `v,err:=conv(src.F); if err!=nil {return out,err}; out.F=v`; ptr/Option
  `*A->*B` nil-guarded re-address; slice `[]A->[]B` make+indexed loop; array `[N]A->[N]B`
  in-place; map `map[K]A->map[K]B`; nested in-file struct via deriveBody. An unsourced or
  unconvertible field is a LOCATED e.fail, never a silent zero (the footgun §12 kills).
  Override VALUES emit via e.exprText (AST expr, not string parse — FR-6). Temp names are
  scope-aware gensyms (one shared `err` per fallible derive; `v`/`p`/`i`/`k`/`s` per site),
  NOT `__goal_v0`. typeExprString (lower.go) renders a source/target type expr to the
  sema-canonical key string (matching Structs/FromRegistry keys). The string-level splitters
  (derefType/ptrInner/arrElem/mapKV/elemConv) port verbatim — they operate on already-resolved
  sema type strings. NOTE the foreign-package derive fixture (US-009) still runs through the
  SPLICE engine via corpus.RunPackage; this AST lowering covers only the file-mode features/12
  cases.
- The AST engine is now the DEFAULT (US-042). cmd/goal parseFlags defaults engine=engineAST;
  the default package path routes through backend.TranspilePackage (cross-file merge + ONE
  shared prelude), NOT a per-file loop. The exact-tier corpus tests (TestTranspileRunner,
  TestDoctestRunner, TestCorpusTranspile, TestCorpusDoctest) run backend.Transpile and compare
  against goldens regenerated FROM the backend; splice keeps only behavioral-tier coverage
  (RunCompile/RunDoctestExec/RunPackage via pipeline.Transpile) + the --engine=splice flag.
- Regenerate the .go.expected goldens with the off-by-default flag:
  `go test ./internal/corpus -run TestUpdateGoldens -update-goldens` (internal/corpus/
  update_goldens_test.go, mirrors parser's -update-snapshots). It writes gofmt(backend Output.Go),
  or gofmt(Output.Test) when the existing golden is a doctest sidecar (isDoctestSidecar). Goldens
  are produced ONLY from real backend output — never hand-edit them. The exact tier uses
  single-file backend.Transpile (no //line directives), so regen output matches by construction.
- Source-position mapping is engine-agnostic: pipeline.AddLineDirectives (exported) inserts
  name-anchored `//line` directives. Any new package-mode emit path must apply it or `goal build`
  errors stop mapping back to .goal source (TestBuildErrorMapsToGoalSource guards this).
- THE SPLICE ENGINE IS GONE (US-043). internal/pass is deleted; internal/pipeline now holds ONLY
  the engine-independent Output/GoFile/PackageOutput types + sourcemap (AddLineDirectives) — there
  is no pipeline.Transpile/TranspilePackage anymore. backend.Transpile / backend.TranspilePackage
  is the ONE front-end; every transpile call site (cmd/goalc, cmd/build-playground, cmd/goal-wasm,
  internal/guide, internal/typecheck, corpus behavioral runners) uses it. The --engine flag is
  removed; parseFlags returns (emit, emitDir, root, err). Add transpile consumers via backend.*,
  never pipeline.*.
- internal/typecheck (the go/types depth checker, on the DEFAULT `goal build/check` path) transpiles
  internally — it now uses backend.TranspilePackage. The AST backend therefore must faithfully emit
  whatever real goal programs feed the depth checker, including constructs ABSENT from the corpus:
  generic type-parameter DECLARATIONS (`type Box[T any]`) and type ALIASES (`type T = U`). The splice
  engine masked these by passing them through verbatim; the AST parser/emitter must handle them.
- Generic type-parameter DECLARATIONS are parsed in parser.parseTypeSpec via atTypeParams()
  (disambiguates `type T[P any]` from `[]T`/`[N]T`/`[3]T` arrays using kindAt(2): typeparams iff
  `[` then IDENT then COMMA-or-type-start) + parseTypeParams() (shared-constraint name lists like
  `[T, U any]`). They live on ast.TypeSpec.TypeParams *FieldList and emit via fieldList(fl,"[","]").
  Generic INSTANTIATION (`Box[int]`) already parsed via parseIndexSuffix (IndexExpr/IndexListExpr).
  kindAt(n) is the new n-token lookahead helper (peekKind == kindAt(1)).
- Type ALIASES carry on ast.TypeSpec.Assign token.Pos (zero == defined type). parser records the
  `=` position; emit.go's TypeSpec case emits `= ` when Assign is non-zero. Sexpr SKIPS token.Pos so
  AST snapshots are unaffected; but the BACKEND OUTPUT changed (`type T int64` -> `type T = int64`),
  so any corpus golden with an alias must be regenerated (-update-goldens). Aliases vs defined types
  have DIFFERENT go/types identity — emitting the alias faithfully is what makes the depth checker's
  signature-equivalence checks pass (TestImplementsAliasEqualSignatureIsNotAMismatch).
- scan.Splice/Replacement and the analyze fact tables are STILL LIVE (consumed by check/fix/lsp/
  typecheck/project). Nothing in scan/analyze was used SOLELY by the deleted splice passes, so the
  "dead scanning" can only be removed once US-044 (fix->AST) and US-046 (lsp->AST) migrate those
  consumers off the token scanner. Don't try to delete scan/analyze symbols until then.
- `goal fmt` (internal/goalfmt.Source) is a position-driven REINDENTER, NOT an AST
  pretty-printer: it parses with parser.ParseFile only as a validity gate, then rewrites
  RAW SOURCE LINES (normalizing leading indent = one tab per delimiter-nesting depth from
  lexer.Tokens, trailing whitespace, and blank-line runs) — never printing the bare AST
  (which would drop // and /* comments). Because only whitespace the lexer skips changes,
  the token stream/AST/meaning is invariant and it is idempotent by construction. Any
  future fmt enhancement (struct-field alignment, switch-case dedent) must keep that
  raw-source, position-driven discipline — do NOT switch to AST printing.
- The LSP document model is AST-derived (US-046). internal/lsp/symbols.go
  collectSymbols PARSES (parser.ParseFile) and walks ast.File.Decls — there is no
  more token scan (scanDecls is gone). Outline ranges come straight off node
  Pos()/End() offsets via rangeOf, so a bodyless decl never overruns the next
  (End() stops at its own last token). internal/lsp no longer imports internal/scan:
  diagnostics.go tokenEnds tokenizes via lexer.Tokens (token end = Pos.Offset +
  len(Lit)). BUT diagnostic FINDINGS still come from check.Analyze /
  AnalyzePackageInDirWith — the checker itself is still analyze/scan-based (its
  package path needs analyze.EnrichForeign), so don't expect sema there yet.
  rangeOf still uses check.OffsetToPosition, so symbols.go keeps the internal/check
  import even though the scan import is gone.
- LSP semantic tokens (US-047) are computed by overlaying an AST role map on the
  lexer token STREAM, not by walking the AST alone: lexer.Tokens gives ordered
  positions + lengths + the lexer-confident classes (keywords incl. match/enum,
  comments, string/char, int/float/imag, and the goal operators QUESTION/FAT_ARROW/
  ELLIPSIS), and astRoles (parser.ParseFile + ast.Walk roleVisitor) supplies the
  identifier ROLE keyed by Ident byte offset. roleVisitor fixes a name's role by its
  STRUCTURAL parent (handled at the EnumDecl/TypeSpec/FuncDecl/VariantLit/
  VariantPattern/CallExpr node, NOT at the bare Ident) and always returns itself so
  Walk still descends into bodies. An IDENT with no recorded role is NOT emitted —
  builtins like int stay grammar-coloured rather than mislabelled. The wire form is
  the LSP delta-encoded 5-tuple [dLine,dStartChar,length,type,modifiers], 0-based via
  check.OffsetToPosition; tokenLen falls back to len(Kind.String()) for empty-Lit
  operators. The legend ordering is one source of truth: the sem* index constants
  index semanticTokenTypes, shared by the advertised SemanticTokensProvider and the
  encoder, so wire indices can't drift. GOTCHA: a `?` inside a string ("?") lexes as
  STRING, not QUESTION — a test locating the postfix `?` by substring must avoid a
  stray `?` string in its sample.
- LSP hover (US-049) reuses the US-048 symbol graph: parse the open buffer, build
  a name-keyed index over file.Decls, walk references keyed by structural parent
  (hoverVisitor mirrors definition.go's refVisitor), and map the cursor to a byte
  offset with offsetForPosition. The ONE difference from go-to-definition: the
  index value is a rendered hoverInfo{signature,doc} instead of a declaration
  Range, and declaration-name idents are seeded as spans too (so hovering the
  declaration itself resolves, not just references). A func/method signature is
  the RAW SOURCE slice src[FuncDecl.Pos().Offset:FuncDecl.Type.End().Offset]
  whitespace-collapsed — Pos() already starts at the from/derive modifier or the
  func keyword, and Type.End() stops before the body, so the result type
  (Result[...]/Option[...]) shows verbatim without rendering the AST. Only
  FuncDecl carries Doc in the AST, so doc text is function-only; enum/type/variant
  hovers render a header string. Nil *Hover marshals to JSON null (best-effort
  contract). GOTCHA: a word inside a /// doc line is NOT an indexable identifier,
  so a hover test that locates a function-name occurrence by substring must word
  the doc comment to avoid the symbol name.
- LSP references + rename (US-050) INVERT the US-048 symbol graph: where
  go-to-definition maps a reference -> its declaration Range, references/rename
  map a symbol -> ALL its occurrences. internal/lsp/references.go reuses
  definition.go's buildDeclIndex + offsetForPosition + rangeOf, then
  collectOccurrences records EVERY occurrence of EVERY top-level symbol as
  occurrence{start,end,key symKey,isDecl}: declaration names seeded first
  (isDecl=true, like hover.go's span seeding) then references via occVisitor whose
  structural keying is IDENTICAL to refVisitor — so reference coverage equals
  go-to-definition coverage BY CONSTRUCTION (change one visitor, change both; they
  are deliberately parallel, not shared). symKey{kind(func|type|variant),enum,name}
  is the symbol identity; variants are keyed UNDER their enum (the enum field) so a
  tag shared by two enums stays distinct and a variant query never leaks into the
  enum type or a sibling variant. resolveOccurrences finds the occurrence covering
  the cursor offset and returns all SAME-KEY occurrences. references() -> []Location
  drops isDecl ones when !context.includeDeclaration; rename() validates the new
  name via isIdent (letter/_ then letter/digit/_) and returns a *WorkspaceEdit with
  one TextEdit per occurrence, version-pinned via s.buffer's version (as
  codeaction.go does). Nil slice / nil *WorkspaceEdit marshal to JSON null
  (best-effort contract). To assert a rename in a test WITHOUT a printer, apply the
  TextEdits by byte offset RIGHT-TO-LEFT (sort spans by descending start) so earlier
  edits don't shift later offsets. Still single-document (locals/params/qualified
  imports/cross-file out of scope, consistent with US-048/049).

## [2026-06-28T03:10:00Z] - US-016
- Added OPTION as a tagged union to the goscript interpreter: `Option.Some(x)` and
  `Option.None` now construct universal Variant values (TypeID "Option", Tag
  "Some"/"None") with NO *T optimization, and `match` dispatches+binds over them.
  A mechanical mirror of US-015 (Result); match dispatch needed ZERO changes.
- internal/interp/value.go: added const optionTypeID/optionSomeTag/optionNoneTag/
  optionSomeField("value") next to the Result constants. `payloadValue` already
  returns ok=false for None's zero fields (a None arm binds nothing) — no change.
- internal/interp/eval.go: added `evalOptionCtor` (mirrors evalResultCtor but only
  the `Some` ctor + default refusal, since None is data-less). evalCallMulti
  intercepts a SelectorExpr-call whose X is Ident "Option" (not shadowed) ->
  evalOptionCtor, right after the Result interception. evalSelector intercepts the
  DATA-LESS `Option.None` (X Ident "Option", Sel "None", not shadowed) ->
  VariantVal("Option","None",nil); Option is NOT in info.Enums so it needs its own
  guard distinct from the enum data-less path.
- internal/interp/interp.go: armScopeFor's payload-unwrap guard now fires for
  TypeID == optionTypeID too (was resultTypeID only) — so a `Some(v)` arm binds the
  UNWRAPPED inner value, a `None` arm binds nothing.

  - Result and Option are now BOTH unwrapped-on-bind in armScopeFor (keyed on

## [2026-06-28T02:30:00Z] - US-015
- Added RESULT as a tagged union to the goscript interpreter: `Result.Ok(x)` and
  `Result.Err(e)` now construct universal Variant values (TypeID "Result", Tag
  "Ok"/"Err"), uniformly for open-E (`Result[T, error]`) and closed-E
  (`Result[T, Enum]`) — NO (T,error) optimization — and `match` dispatches+binds
  over them. Reuses the US-012 VariantVal ctor and the US-013/014 selectMatchArm
  tag dispatch; the only new match concern was payload BINDING.
- internal/interp/value.go: added const resultTypeID/resultOkTag/resultErrTag/
  resultOkField("value")/resultErrField("error") + `payloadValue(*Variant)

  (so a data-less variant like Option.None reports no payload).
- internal/interp/eval.go: evalCallMulti intercepts a SelectorExpr-call whose X is
  Ident "Result" (not shadowed) BEFORE the host/method paths -> evalResultCtor.
  `Result.Ok(x)` -> VariantVal("Result","Ok",{value:x}); `Result.Err(e)` ->
  VariantVal("Result","Err",{error:e}); each requires exactly 1 arg; an unknown
  Result ctor or wrong arity is a LOCATED (call.Pos()) descriptive refusal.
- internal/interp/interp.go: armScopeFor (the ONE bind seam shared by statement-
  and value-position match) now UNWRAPS for a Result subject — when
  subj.Variant.TypeID == resultTypeID it binds payloadValue(...) (the inner
  value/error), matching surface semantics (`Result.Ok(cfg) => cfg.Raw`,
  `Result.Err(e) => ...e`). A named-field ENUM variant still binds the WHOLE

## [2026-06-28T01:50:00Z] - US-014
- Added VALUE-POSITION match to the goscript interpreter: a `match` used as an
  expression — `return match`, `x := match`, `var x = match` — now yields the
  selected arm's value as an expression result (one of the two non-Go runtime
  mechanics). Dispatch is uniform with statement-position match (US-013).
- internal/interp/interp.go: factored the arm-selection + arm-scope logic out of
  execMatch/execArm into two SHARED helpers so statement- and value-position
  match stay in lock-step (one place to change dispatch):
  - selectMatchArm(m, subj) (*ast.MatchArm, *ast.VariantPattern): the variant arm
    whose pattern tag == subj.Variant.Tag, else a `_` rest arm (nil vp), else
    (nil, nil) -> caller raises the loud default.
  - armScopeFor(vp, subj, scope) *Env: child scope binding vp.Binding (when named)
    to the whole variant value (payload read as `binding.field`).
  - unreachableMatch(subj) error: the shared panicSignal "unreachable: non-
    exhaustive match on <TypeID>" default. execMatch/execArm now call these.
- internal/interp/eval.go: evalExpr gained `case *ast.MatchExpr` -> evalMatch
  (value position; statement-position match is still intercepted earlier in
  execStmt and never reaches evalExpr, so no conflict). evalMatch mirrors
  execMatch but evaluates the selected arm body via evalArmValue and RETURNS its
  Value. evalArmValue evaluates the arm body as an ast.Expr (the parser's value-
  position `=> expr` arm); a non-expression body in value position is a
  descriptive refusal. All three value positions (return / := / var =) reach
  evalExpr through existing callers (execReturn non-call result, execAssign RHS,
  execDecl spec values) so NO caller changes were needed.
- internal/interp/value_match_test.go (new): TestValueMatchInReturn,
  TestValueMatchInShortVar, TestValueMatchInVarDecl (each over Point/Circle/Square
  with payload-computing arms), TestValueMatchRestArmSuppliesValue (`_` arm),
  TestValueMatchDefaultIsUnreachable (hand-built value-match over an uncovered tag
  -> panicSignal "unreachable"), TestValueMatchOnNonVariantIsRefused. Drives a
  02-match-shaped program through newInterp+evalFn. stdlib testing, no testify.
- prd.json (US-014 passes:true), progress.txt
- history/20260627-feature-us-014-eval-value-position-match/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Value- and statement-position match now share selectMatchArm + armScopeFor +
    unreachableMatch. US-015/US-016 (Result/Option as tagged unions) get
    value-position match over Ok/Err/Some/None for FREE once those construct
    VariantVals — the SAME tag dispatch applies, in both positions. Keep match
    tag-keyed, not enum-specific.
  - A value-position arm body is an ast.Expr (parser `=> expr`); a NESTED value-
    position match arm (`=> match {...}`) is covered for free because evalArmValue
    -> evalExpr dispatches *ast.MatchExpr recursively.
  - The non-exhaustive default is a panicSignal in BOTH positions (returned as an
    error from evalMatch; raised as an error from execMatch) — loud, not silent.
  - interp deps stay clean for the US-022 gate (go list -deps ./internal/interp:
    no go/types, internal/backend, internal/typecheck).

## [2026-06-28T01:05:00Z] - US-013
- Added STATEMENT-POSITION match to the goscript interpreter: a `match` in
  statement position dispatches on the scrutinee variant's tag, binds the matched
  payload into a child scope, runs the selected arm, and panics 'unreachable' on
  the defensive default of a proven-exhaustive match (loud, never silent).
- internal/interp/interp.go:
  - execStmt's ExprStmt case now intercepts `*ast.MatchExpr` and routes to
    execMatch BEFORE the CallExpr path (a statement-position match parses to
    ExprStmt{X: *ast.MatchExpr}). Value-position match stays out of scope (US-014).
  - execMatch evaluates m.Subject (must be KindVariant), walks the arms, runs the
    arm whose *ast.VariantPattern.Variant.Name == subj.Variant.Tag, else a
    *ast.RestPattern (`_`) arm; with neither it raises panicSignal carrying an
    "unreachable: non-exhaustive match on <TypeID> ..." message — the same
    loud-not-silent stance as the backend's panicking default.
  - execArm binds vp.Binding (when present) to the WHOLE variant value in a fresh
    scope.NewChild(); execArmBody dispatches the generic ast.Node arm body
    (ast.Stmt -> execStmt incl. block/return; *ast.CallExpr -> evalCallMulti for
    void calls; other ast.Expr -> evalExpr). A return/break/continue/panic raised
    by the body propagates up the established control-signal seam.
- internal/interp/eval.go: evalSelector now reads a payload field off a
  KindVariant receiver via Value.Field (so a match binding `a` reads `a.since`),
  in addition to the existing struct-field read; non-struct/non-variant stays a
  descriptive refusal. The data-less enum-construction guard at the top is
  unaffected (a binding name is not an enum name, and the shadow check protects).
- internal/interp/match_test.go (new): TestMatchDispatchesDataLessArm,
  TestMatchDispatchesPayloadArmAndBindsPayload, TestMatchRestArmRunsWhenNoVariantMatches,
  TestMatchDefaultArmIsUnreachable (hand-built match over an uncovered tag ->
  panicSignal mentioning "unreachable"), TestMatchOnNonVariantIsRefused. Drives a
  02-match-shaped program (Shape{Point, Circle{radius}, Square{side}}) through

- prd.json (US-013 passes:true), progress.txt
- history/20260627-feature-us-013-eval-statement-position-match/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Match dispatch is UNIFORM over the tagged union: execMatch keys on
    subj.Variant.Tag, so once US-015/US-016 construct Result.Ok/Err and
    Option.Some/None as VariantVals, the SAME execMatch dispatches them by tag
    (Ok/Err/Some/None) with NO match-specific code — only construction + `?` are
    new there. Keep match tag-keyed, not enum-specific.
  - A match arm body is a generic ast.Node: `=> return x` is an ast.Stmt (run via
    execStmt), `=> f()` is an *ast.CallExpr (run via evalCallMulti for void), a
    value-position arm `=> expr` is an ast.Expr. execArmBody is the one seam;

    discarding it, but reuse the same tag dispatch + payload binding.

## [2026-06-28T00:20:00Z] - US-012
- Added enum CONSTRUCTION to the goscript interpreter: data-less
  (`Status.Pending`) and payload-carrying (`Status.Active(since: now())`)
  variants now evaluate into the universal tagged-union Value, and their
  payload fields read back by name. No value-model change — value.go already
  carried Variant{TypeID,Tag,Fields} + VariantVal + Value.Field.
- internal/interp/eval.go:
  - evalExpr gained `case *ast.VariantLit` -> evalVariantLit (the PAYLOAD form;
    the parser builds a VariantLit only when the arg list has >=1 LABELED arg).
    evalVariantLit resolves the enum ref (*ast.Ident only — a qualified enum is
    a deferred refusal), validates the tag against enum.VSet, fills the Fields
    map from each *ast.LabeledArg (label->eval(value)) and binds a positional
    arg by declared field order (variantFields), then returns
    VariantVal(enumName, tag, fields). Unknown enum / unknown variant / too many
    positional args are LOCATED, descriptive refusals, never a silent value.
  - evalSelector now intercepts the DATA-LESS form at the TOP, BEFORE evaluating
    the receiver: `Enum.Variant` (no parens) parses to *ast.SelectorExpr, so when
    s.X is an *ast.Ident naming an enum in info.Enums, that name is NOT shadowed
    by a value binding (scope.Lookup fails), and s.Sel.Name is in enum.VSet, it
    returns VariantVal(enum.Name, tag, nil). Otherwise it falls through to the
    existing struct-field read — so io.Writer / receiver / struct-field selectors
    are untouched (mirrors the backend's SelectorExpr-lowering guard).
  - new enumByName(name) nil-safe lookup of ip.info.Enums (the single gate every
    enum-construction path consults) + variantFields(enum,tag) helper.
- internal/interp/enum_test.go (new): TestConstructDataLessVariant,
  TestConstructPayloadVariantSingleField, TestConstructPayloadVariantMultiField,
  TestConstructUnknownVariantIsRefused, TestConstructUnknownEnumIsRefused — drive
  a 01-enums-shaped program (Status{Pending, Active{since}, Cancelled{reason,at}})
  through newInterp+evalFn (call_test.go/composite_test.go helpers); error cases
  build the VariantLit AST by hand. stdlib testing, no testify.
- prd.json (US-012 passes:true), progress.txt
- history/20260627-feature-us-012-eval-enum-construction/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - The three meanings of `Enum.Variant(x)` are DISTINCT AST nodes (per ast/
    goal_expr.go), so no pass-ordering hack is needed at eval time: a PAYLOAD
    construction (labeled args) is *ast.VariantLit, a DATA-LESS construction is
    *ast.SelectorExpr (guard it in evalSelector by info.Enums+VSet+not-shadowed),
    and a destructuring is *ast.VariantPattern (US-013, never a value). A bare
    POSITIONAL `Enum.Variant(x)` (no label) parses to an ordinary *ast.CallExpr,
    NOT a VariantLit — Result.Ok(x)/Option.Some(x) land that way and are
    US-015/US-016, so they are out of scope here.

    v.Variant.Tag and bind v.Variant.Fields. The tagged-union the construction
    produces is the exact shape match reads — keep VariantVal as the one ctor.
  - reading a variant payload field is via the Value.Field(name) API (already in
    value.go); direct `a.since` selector access is NOT goal syntax (payload is
    read through match binding), so evalSelector still only reads STRUCT fields.
  - interp deps stay clean for the US-022 gate (go list -deps ./internal/interp:
    no go/types, internal/backend, internal/typecheck — reading sema.Info is fine).

## [2026-06-27T23:45:00Z] - US-011
- Added the host-function bridge: internal/interp now resolves a curated set of
  imported stdlib calls to native Go, and an unresolved imported call is a
  LOCATED, NAMED refusal rather than a silent nil.
- internal/interp/host.go (new): `hostFuncs` registry keyed "<import-path>.<Sym>"
  (fmt.Sprintf, fmt.Sprint, fmt.Println, fmt.Errorf, errors.New). `evalHostCall`
  resolves the package path + symbol, evaluates args, and either invokes the
  shim or returns `interp: <line:col>: unresolved imported call <pkg.Sym> (no
  host function registered)` using sel.Pos().String(). `goArg`/`goArgs` convert
  runtime Values to Go fmt args (primitives pass through; an error struct becomes
  a real Go error so %w/%v render the message; other composites render via
  Value.String()). Errors are represented as StructVal("error",{"message":...})
  via errVal — a lightweight encoding distinct from Result/Option (US-015/016).

  package name -> import path), populated in New via registerImports (alias when
  present, else last path element; skips _/. imports). Added strconv+strings.
- internal/interp/eval.go: evalCallMulti intercepts a selector call whose X
  names an imported package AND is NOT shadowed (scope.Lookup fails) and routes
  it to evalHostCall, BEFORE tryMethodCall. A local binding shadowing a package
  name therefore falls through to ordinary method/function dispatch.

  TestHostErrorsNew, TestHostErrorfWrapsError ("ctx: inner" — proves the %w

    *ast.SelectorExpr whose X is an *ast.Ident in ip.imports and not shadowed in

## [2026-06-27T23:00:00Z] - US-010
- Added the len/append/make/panic builtins and value- + pointer-receiver method
  dispatch to the goscript interpreter.
- evalCallMulti (eval.go) is the single interception point: an *ast.Ident callee
  whose name isBuiltin AND is not shadowed in scope routes to evalBuiltin; an
  *ast.SelectorExpr callee routes to tryMethodCall (struct receiver + a method on
  its type) BEFORE the generic function-value path, so a struct field holding a
  func and a deferred package call (fmt.Println, US-011) still fall through
  unchanged. builtinLen (slice/string/map), builtinAppend (returns a NEW slice;
  no backing-array aliasing, no variadic spread), builtinMake (arg[0] is a TYPE
  expr: *ast.MapType -> empty map, *ast.ArrayType -> slice of n element-zeros via
  zeroValue), builtinPanic (raises panicSignal).
- panic uses the established error-sentinel control pattern: panicSignal{value}
  (interp.go) rides the (… error) channel like returnSignal/break/continue, but
  NO boundary (execFor/execSwitch/callFunc/callMethod) recovers it — it
  propagates to Run and the host, which is the "recovered panic" (a test
  errors.As-es it at the Go boundary and reads .value).
- Method registry: registerMethods (called from New) indexes every method decl
  by star-stripped receiver type name -> method name -> *ast.FuncDecl
  (recvTypeName/recvName/recvIsPointer helpers off ast.FuncDecl.Recv: a
  *ast.StarExpr receiver type is a pointer receiver). callMethod binds the
  receiver in a fresh child of root (package scope), then params, runs the body,
  recovers returnSignal like callFunc. A POINTER receiver shares the caller's
  pointer-backed StructValue (mutations visible to caller); a VALUE receiver
  binds a shallow copyStructValue (mutations do NOT leak — Go value semantics).
- execStmt's ExprStmt case now routes a CallExpr through evalCallMulti and
  discards results, so a VOID call statement (a void method/function call) is
  valid — previously evalExpr->evalCall forced a single-value context and errored
  on a 0-value call.
- Files changed:
  - internal/interp/interp.go (panicSignal; methods registry field;
    registerMethods + recvTypeName/recvName/recvIsPointer; callMethod;
    ExprStmt-call routing through evalCallMulti)
  - internal/interp/eval.go (evalCallMulti builtin/method interception;
    evalBuiltin + builtinLen/Append/Make/Panic; isBuiltin; tryMethodCall;
    copyStructValue)
  - internal/interp/builtins_test.go (new: TestBuiltinLen, TestBuiltinAppendValue,
    TestBuiltinMakeMapReadBack, TestBuiltinPanicRecovered,
    TestBuiltinLenUndefinedOperand, TestPointerReceiverMethodMutates,
    TestValueReceiverMethodReads, TestValueReceiverMethodDoesNotLeak — stdlib
    testing, no testify)
  - prd.json (US-010 passes:true), progress.txt
  - history/20260627-feature-us-010-eval-builtins-and-methods/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Builtins are intercepted in evalCallMulti by NAME, guarded by a failed
    scope.Lookup so a user binding of the same name shadows the builtin. Add a
    new builtin by extending isBuiltin + evalBuiltin's switch.
  - Method dispatch is struct-receiver only for now (tryMethodCall returns
    handled=false on a non-struct/no-method receiver, so the generic path
    surfaces the right error). US-018 (implements dispatch) builds on this
    registry; an interface value dispatched to a concrete method reuses
    callMethod. The value-vs-pointer copy distinction (copyStructValue) is the
    seam that makes pointer-receiver mutation observable — keep it.
  - panicSignal is the loud-not-silent panic seam US-019 (assert) reuses: assert
    on a false condition should raise a panic the same error-sentinel way.
  - A void call as a statement now works (ExprStmt routes CallExpr through
    evalCallMulti); single-value contexts still go through evalExpr->evalCall.
  - interp deps stay clean for US-022 (go list -deps: no go/types,
    internal/backend, internal/typecheck).
