## [2026-06-27T22:10:00Z] - US-009
- Added composite-type evaluation to the goscript interpreter: struct composite
  literals + field access, slice literals + indexing, map literals + indexing +
  key assignment, and range-for over slices and maps. No value-model change was
  needed — value.go already carried StructValue (pointer, Fields map), []Value
  slices, and MapValue (pointer, string-keyed Entries) with constructors.
- eval.go: evalExpr gained *ast.CompositeLit / *ast.SelectorExpr / *ast.IndexExpr
  cases. evalCompositeLit dispatches on c.Type: *ast.ArrayType -> SliceVal
  (positional elements; arrays fold into slices for v1), *ast.MapType -> MapVal
  (KeyValueExpr elements, string keys via mapKeyString), *ast.Ident -> StructVal
  (KEYED field: value elements only — positional struct literals are a
  descriptive refusal). evalSelector reads a struct field (non-struct/absent ->
  error; package/variant selectors stay later stories). evalIndex bounds-checks
  slice int indices and reads map string keys (absent key -> NilVal, the defined
  absent-read). mapKeyString enforces the string-keyed v1 model.
- interp.go: execStmt gained *ast.RangeStmt -> execRange (slice: ascending
  IntVal index + element; map: SORTED string keys for determinism; honors :=/=
  and the blank identifier via rangeBind; recovers break/continue exactly like
  execFor). bindTargets was refactored to delegate per-target to a new
  assignTarget, which now handles *ast.IndexExpr (slice element / map entry
  write) and *ast.SelectorExpr (struct field write) in ADDITION to the existing
  *ast.Ident :=/=/compound behavior. compoundApply factors the compound-operator
  read-modify-write so index/field targets support += etc. too.
- Files changed:
  - internal/interp/eval.go (CompositeLit/Selector/Index cases + helpers +
    mapKeyString)
  - internal/interp/interp.go (RangeStmt case; execRange, rangeBind; bindTargets
    -> assignTarget/assignIndex/assignField/compoundApply; sort import)
  - internal/interp/composite_test.go (new: TestCompositeProgram [9 int cases +
    sorted map-key string], TestAcceptanceCombined [AC: structs+slices+maps +
    range], TestCompositeErrors — stdlib testing, no testify)
  - prd.json (US-009 passes:true), progress.txt
  - history/20260627-feature-us-009-eval-composite-types/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Reference semantics come FREE from the value model: StructValue/MapValue are
    pointers and a []Value shares its backing array, so an index/field/entry
    write through a looked-up binding is visible everywhere it's shared — no
    addressable-lvalue machinery needed. assignTarget evaluates the target's X
    to get that shared identity, then mutates in place.
  - assignTarget is now the SINGLE assignment-target seam (Ident/Index/Selector);
    later stories extend it rather than touching bindTargets. compoundApply is
    the shared compound-operator helper.
  - Maps stay STRING-KEYED (v1 value model): a map literal/index/assign with a
    non-string key is a located refusal (mapKeyString). Non-string keys are still
    deferred. Map-range visits keys in SORTED order so any string/golden
    assertion over a map range is deterministic.
  - Struct literals are KEYED only (field: value) — the goal idiom; positional
    struct literals are a descriptive refusal. evalSelector handles only struct
    field reads; a SelectorExpr whose X is a package name (fmt.Println) or an
    enum (Status.Pending) still routes elsewhere (US-011/US-012).
  - RangeStmt was deliberately deferred from US-008 to here; execRange mirrors
    execFor's break/continue recovery (errors.As over breakSignal/continueSignal,
    returnSignal/real errors propagate). interp deps stay clean for US-022.

## [2026-06-27T17:10:00Z] - US-008
- Added control-flow evaluation to the goscript interpreter: three-clause and
  condition-only (and infinite) for loops, expression switch (tagged + tagless,
  with default), bare nested block scoping, and break/continue. if/else already
  existed (US-004/US-006). execStmt (interp.go) now dispatches *ast.ForStmt,
  *ast.SwitchStmt, *ast.BranchStmt, *ast.IncDecStmt, and *ast.BlockStmt (the
  last runs its List in scope.NewChild() so inner decls don't leak).
- break/continue use the ESTABLISHED error-sentinel control pattern (like
  returnSignal): breakSignal{} and continueSignal{} are error types raised by
  execBranch and recovered via errors.As. execFor recovers BOTH (continue ->
  run Post + next iteration; break -> stop); execSwitch recovers ONLY break, so
  a continue inside a switch propagates to the enclosing loop. returnSignal and
  real errors always propagate past loop/switch to the call boundary.
- execFor opens loopScope := scope.NewChild() (Init binds there, persists across
  iterations); each body iteration runs in loopScope.NewChild(). Post runs after
  every iteration including a continue. nil Cond == always true; non-bool Cond is
  a located refusal. execSwitch: Init+Tag in swScope; a List==nil CaseClause is
  the default (run only if nothing matched); tagged match = any case expr
  .Equal(tag); tagless match = any case expr is bool true; selected body runs in
  swScope.NewChild() with NO fallthrough. A switch clause body is a flat
  []ast.Stmt (NOT a *ast.BlockStmt) so it runs via execClauseBody, not execBlock.
  execIncDec reads an *ast.Ident binding, applies applyBinary(ADD/SUB, cur, one)
  with one = IntVal(1)/FloatVal(1) by kind, Assigns back.
- Files changed:
  - internal/interp/interp.go (breakSignal/continueSignal; execStmt cases;
    execFor, execSwitch, caseMatches, execClauseBody, execBranch, execIncDec)
  - internal/interp/control_test.go (new: ForThreeClauseSummation,
    ForConditionOnly, ForInfiniteWithBreak, ContinueSkipsRemainder,
    TaggedSwitchDispatch, TaglessSwitchFirstTrue, BreakInSwitchExitsOnlySwitch,
    NestedBlockScoping, IfElseChain, NonBoolForConditionErrors,
    BreakOutsideLoopErrors — stdlib testing, no testify)
  - prd.json (US-008 passes:true), progress.txt
  - history/20260627-feature-us-008-eval-control-flow/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - The control-signal seam is now complete: returnSignal (call boundary),
    breakSignal + continueSignal (loop/switch boundary), all error sentinels
    recovered via errors.As. US-013 (statement-position match) panics
    'unreachable' on a proven-exhaustive default — model it the same loud way.
  - A switch CaseClause.Body is a flat []ast.Stmt, not a BlockStmt — don't reach
    for execBlock there (execClauseBody loops execStmt instead). RangeStmt
    (for-range) is deliberately NOT handled here; it lands in US-009 (composite
    types) since it needs slice/map iteration.
  - Tests drive real parsed programs (newInterp from call_test.go) through
    evalExpr(call("fn"), ip.root); a control-flow function that returns a value
    is the cleanest observable. For statement-only forms (bare block scoping,
    error refusals) build the AST node directly and call ip.execStmt against a
    child scope.
  - interp deps stay clean for the US-022 gate: no new imports beyond the
    already-present ast/token; no go/types, backend, or typecheck.

## [2026-06-27T16:20:00Z] - US-007
- Added function declarations as values + calls + recursion to the goscript
  interpreter. New now registers every top-level plain func (Recv==nil, named,
  bodied) into root as a FuncDeclVal closing over root, so a function is visible
  to its own body (recursion) and to forward refs. A call (*ast.CallExpr in
  evalExpr) resolves the callee via the scope chain, evaluates args, and dispatches
  to callFunc: flatten params (grouped `a, b int` -> two names), arity-check, bind
  in a FRESH child of the func's defining scope, run the body, recover the return.
  Return is a non-local control signal (returnSignal{vals []Value}, an error
  sentinel) threaded UP through execBlock/execStmt and recovered at the call
  boundary with errors.As — never escapes as a real error. Added the minimum
  if/return needed for recursive base cases (full control flow is US-008).
- Multi-return: callFunc/evalCallMulti return []Value (no tuple Kind added).
  evalExpr's CallExpr requires exactly 1 result (single-value context);
  execAssign gained a multi-result branch (len(Lhs)>1 && len(Rhs)==1 && sole RHS
  is a CallExpr -> spread positionally), and `return f()` spreads a multi-call.
- Files changed:
  - internal/interp/value.go (FuncValue grows Decl *ast.FuncDecl + Env *Env;
    new FuncDeclVal ctor; ast import; old name-only FuncVal kept)
  - internal/interp/interp.go (returnSignal; registerFuncs in New; Run via
    callFunc; callFunc + flattenParams; execStmt ReturnStmt/IfStmt cases;
    execReturn/execIf; execAssign multi-result branch; bindTargets extracted)
  - internal/interp/eval.go (evalExpr CallExpr case; evalCall + evalCallMulti)
  - internal/interp/call_test.go (new: RecursiveFactorial, RecursiveFibonacci,
    MultiReturnAssignment, MultiValueCallInSingleValueContext, ArgCountMismatch,
    CallNonFunction, UndefinedCall, FunctionDeclIsAValue — stdlib testing,
    no testify)
  - prd.json (US-007 passes:true), progress.txt
  - history/20260627-feature-us-007-eval-functions-and-calls/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - The return/control-flow seam is set: returnSignal is an error sentinel that
    execBlock/execStmt propagate and callFunc recovers. US-008 (for/switch/
    break/continue) adds break/continue the SAME way (their own sentinel signal
    types caught by the loop/switch boundary), and execIf already opens child
    scopes the way US-008's blocks should.
  - Functions are registered in New (load-time), so a `package interp` test can
    `New(...)` then `ip.evalExpr(call("fn", args...), ip.root)` to observe a
    return value — the direct-evalExpr seam from US-005/US-006 extends to calls.
    Build call/assign AST nodes by hand (ast.CallExpr/AssignStmt) in tests; no
    new parser entry point is needed.
  - Multi-value calls are modelled as []Value end-to-end (callFunc/evalCallMulti),
    NOT a tuple Value — avoids ambiguity with a genuine slice. A call is single-
    value everywhere except the sole RHS of a multi-assign / sole `return` operand.
  - value.go now imports goal/internal/ast; interp deps stay clean for the US-022
    gate (go list -deps: no go/types, internal/backend, internal/typecheck).

## [2026-06-27T15:54:00Z] - US-006
- Added variable declaration + assignment to the goscript interpreter. execStmt
  (interp.go) now dispatches *ast.DeclStmt (var/const) via execDecl and
  *ast.AssignStmt (:=, =, += -= *= /= %=) via execAssign, reading/writing the
  lexical Env. evalExpr's *ast.Ident case now resolves any non-true/false name

  never a silent zero). Compound assigns reuse applyBinary via a token->op map;

  - internal/interp/env.go (new Assign: chain-walking write that mutates the
    binding in its OWNING scope vs Define which always binds in this scope;

  - Env now has the full triad: Define (bind here), Lookup (read up the chain),

## [2026-06-27T15:47:00Z] - US-005
- Added internal/interp/eval.go, expression evaluation for the goscript
  interpreter: evalExpr(expr, scope)(Value,error) walks the SHARED AST directly
  (*ast.BasicLit, *ast.BinaryExpr, *ast.UnaryExpr, *ast.ParenExpr, and the
  predeclared true/false *ast.Ident) and produces the universal Value with Go
  semantics — int division truncates, `+` concatenates strings, `&&`/`||`
  SHORT-CIRCUIT (evaluate left, only touch right when undecided). Divide/rem by
  zero and operator/operand-kind mismatch are descriptive named errors, never
  panics or silent nils. interp.go execBlock now dispatches statements via a new
  execStmt (ExprStmt -> evalExpr; EmptyStmt no-op; everything else a loud
  "unsupported statement %T" refusal) — the seam US-006+ extend.
- Files changed:
  - internal/interp/eval.go (new: evalExpr, evalBasicLit, evalBinary/applyBinary,
    intBinary/floatBinary/stringBinary, evalUnary)
  - internal/interp/interp.go (execBlock loops via new execStmt; fmt import)
  - internal/interp/eval_test.go (new: TestEvalExpressions [27 rows, AC],
    TestShortCircuit, TestShortCircuitDoesEvaluateRightWhenNeeded, TestEvalErrors,
    TestExecBlockEvaluatesExprStmt — stdlib testing, no testify)
  - prd.json (US-005 passes:true), progress.txt
  - history/20260627-feature-us-005-eval-literals-and-operators/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - A bare expression in a function body parses to *ast.ExprStmt{X: expr}
    (parser parseSimpleStmt default case). A test reaches it via
    findMain().Body.List[0].(*ast.ExprStmt).X and calls evalExpr directly — no
    new parser entry point needed. This is the standard way the eval stories
    (US-006+) can unit-test expression/statement evaluation in `package interp`.
  - == / != are dispatched BEFORE the same-kind guard in applyBinary and delegate
    to Value.Equal (which compares Kind first), so cross-kind == is a clean false,
    not an error; all other binary ops require matching operand kinds.
  - Short-circuit is implemented by evaluating b.X first and returning early for
    `&& false` / `|| true` before b.Y is ever evaluated — proven by guarding the
    right operand with `1/0` in TestShortCircuit.
  - internal/interp still depends only on errors/fmt/strconv + goal/internal/{ast,
    sema,token} — no internal/backend, internal/typecheck, or go/types (verified
    via go list -deps). Keep it that way for the US-022 dependency gate.

## [2026-06-27T21:30:00Z] - US-004
- Added internal/interp/interp.go, the interpreter ENTRY seam: goscript is a
  back-end over the SHARED front-end (REWRITE-ARCHITECTURE.md §3.1). New(file
  *ast.File, info *sema.Info) *Interp constructs the interpreter from the exact
  artifacts the Go transpiler back-end consumes (parsed AST + resolved sema),
  NOT the Go backend's lowered form. Run() error locates the top-level `func
  main` (findMain: *ast.FuncDecl with Recv==nil && Name.Name=="main"; methods
  and a nil Name are skipped), opens a child Env scope, and walks the body via
  execBlock. An empty main body is a successful no-op; an absent main returns the
  named sentinel ErrNoMain ("interp: no func main declared"). execBlock is the
  statement-dispatch seam US-005+ extend (Run already returns error, so no API
  break later).
- Files changed:
  - internal/interp/interp.go (new: Interp, New, Run, findMain, execBlock,
    ErrNoMain)
  - internal/interp/interp_test.go (new: TestRunTrivialMain [AC],
    TestRunMissingMainErrors, TestConstructFromSharedFrontEnd — stdlib testing,
    no testify; parses+resolves via parser.ParseFile + sema.Resolve)
  - prd.json (US-004 passes:true), progress.txt
  - history/20260627-feature-us-004-interpreter-entry-over-ast-and-sema/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Use sema.Resolve(file) (NOT sema.New(), which is empty) to exercise the real
    front-end — same discipline backend.Transpile follows. The interpreter
    retains the *ast.File + *sema.Info pointers for later eval stories.
  - interp.go imports ONLY errors + goal/internal/ast + goal/internal/sema — no
    internal/backend, no go/types. This keeps the §3.1 native-front-end seam
    clean ahead of US-022's stricter dependency gate; keep it that way as eval
    stories grow.
  - The eval stories (US-005 literals/operators onward) hang off execBlock's
    per-statement loop; Run's child-scope + error return are the fixed seam.

## [2026-06-27T15:27:00Z] - US-003
- Added internal/interp/env.go, the interpreter's lexical environment: a
  parent-linked scope chain of name -> Value bindings. NewEnv() makes a root
  scope; (*Env).NewChild() opens an inner scope (parent = receiver);
  (*Env).Define(name, v) binds in THIS scope (overwrites a same-scope binding,
  never writes to a parent); (*Env).Lookup(name) walks this scope then parents,
  first hit wins, and on a miss returns the zero Value + a *NotFoundError naming
  the missing symbol (Error() == "undefined: <name>"). Inner scopes shadow outer
  ones non-destructively.
- Files changed:
  - internal/interp/env.go (new: NotFoundError, Env, NewEnv, NewChild, Define,
    Lookup)
  - internal/interp/env_test.go (new: TestDefineAndLookupSameScope,
    TestParentFallThrough, TestShadowing, TestLookupUndefinedReturnsNotFound,
    TestDefineOverwriteSameScope — stdlib testing, no testify)
  - prd.json (US-003 passes:true), progress.txt
  - history/20260627-feature-us-003-define-environment-and-scopes/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Value (value.go) holds a []Value slice, so it is NOT comparable with == /
    != — `got != Value{}` is a vet error. Compare runtime values with
    v.Equal(other) everywhere (tests included); two zero Values are Equal via the
    KindNil case.
  - Lookup returns (Value, error) not (Value, bool) so the missing name rides in
    *NotFoundError (errors.As-detectable). The eval stories (US-004+) read/write
    program state through this Env; assignment-through-chain semantics (write to
    an existing outer binding vs. define-in-place) are deferred to US-006.
---

## [2026-06-27T20:30:00Z] - US-002

  Variant{TypeID, Tag, Fields} used uniformly for enum / Result / Option — NOT the
  Go backend's (T,error)/*T optimizations (REWRITE-ARCHITECTURE.md §4). Provides
  constructors (IntVal/FloatVal/StrVal/BoolVal/NilVal/StructVal/SliceVal/MapVal/

    US-015 (Result), and US-016 (Option) build on: Result is TypeID="Result"

## [2026-06-27T17:30:00Z] - US-048
- Added textDocument/definition to the goal LSP, resolved from the AST symbol
  graph of the open document. A function/method call, an enum-variant reference
  (construction value, match pattern, or Enum.Variant selector), and a
  type/enum/sealed name reference each resolve to the range of their declaration;

  yields a null result (best-effort, like documentSymbol/semanticTokens).

  the AST recording each reference identifier's byte span -> declaration Range
  (refVisitor keyed by structural parent, mirroring the semantic-token role
  visitor). The index is built before references so a forward call resolves. The

  of check.OffsetToPosition); the ref whose [start,end) covers the offset wins.

  mirroring the US-046 parse+walk pattern. Best-effort: unknown URI or unparseable
  source yields an empty (non-nil) token set, no panic.

- Learnings for future iterations:

    roleVisitor's offset->role map is a seed for the symbol graph, and astRoles is the

  - Diagnostic findings are still analyze/scan-based; semantic tokens do NOT touch the
    checker, so the dead-scan cleanup still waits on the checker migrating off analyze.

## [2026-06-27T15:00:00Z] - US-046
- Switched the LSP document model to the AST. internal/lsp/symbols.go collectSymbols
  now parses with parser.ParseFile and walks ast.File.Decls, mapping each top-level
  declaration to a DocumentSymbol (EnumDecl->enum, SealedInterfaceDecl->interface,
  GenDecl TYPE TypeSpec->struct/interface/alias-class, FuncDecl->method when Recv!=nil

  ranges are taken directly off node Pos()/End() offsets; single-spec `type` decls
  keep the `type` keyword in range (start = GenDecl.Pos()), grouped specs use their
  own Pos() to avoid overlap. The scanDecls/skipLine/declEnd token walk + decl struct
  + internal/scan import are deleted. Best-effort preserved: parse error / nil File /

  (token end = Pos.Offset + len(Lit)), removing internal/scan from internal/lsp

## [2026-06-27T11:00:00Z] - US-045
- Added `goal fmt`, the canonical comment-preserving source formatter (internal/goalfmt).
  Source(src) parses as a validity gate then reindents raw source lines by delimiter
  nesting computed over lexer.Tokens (so braces inside comments/strings never miscount),
  trims trailing whitespace, collapses blank-line runs, and ends with one newline —
  preserving comments, string contents, operator spacing, and field alignment verbatim.
  Idempotent by construction (Source(Source(s))==Source(s)); proven over every corpus
  .goal input. Added `goal fmt [-w] [path]` to cmd/goal (mirrors `goal fix`).
- Files changed:
  - internal/goalfmt/format.go (new: Source + reindent + collapseBlanks + isOpener/isCloser)
  - internal/goalfmt/format_test.go (new: TestIdempotentOverCorpus, TestPreservesComments,
    TestReindentsAndIsStable, TestRejectsUnparseable)
  - cmd/goal/main.go (guideCommands fmt entry; run "fmt" dispatch; parseFmtFlags; cmdFmt)
  - AI-KNOWLEDGE-BOOTSTRAP.md (regenerated for the new subcommand, +2 lines)
  - prd.json (US-045 passes:true), progress.txt
  - history/20260627-feature-us-045-goal-fmt-source-printer/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - The corpus has NO /* */ block comments, NO raw (backtick) string literals (every
    backtick is inside a // comment), and NO switch — so multi-line-token protection and
    switch-case dedent are guarded defensively but not corpus-exercised. Switch bodies
    would indent by pure delimiter nesting (case not dedented); revisit only if a switch
    case ever lands in the corpus and the flat look matters.
  - Idempotency hinges on lexer Pos.Line agreeing with strings.Split("\n") indexing
    (line == split-index+1); confirmed and held across all 108 inputs. Output text comes
    from raw lines, not token Lit, so comment/string/alignment fidelity is automatic.
  - US-046 (LSP onto AST) is next; goalfmt does not touch scan/analyze, so the dead-scan
    cleanup still waits on US-046.

## [2026-06-27T08:05:00Z] - US-035
- Lowered postfix `?` propagation on the AST backend with a real, scope-aware
  gensym, retiring the magic `__goal_` prefix the US-034 seed lowering carried.
  `?` (ast.UnwrapExpr) is now lowered at statement position: stmt()'s AssignStmt
  case intercepts a single UnwrapExpr RHS (`name := expr?` / `_ := expr?`) and the
  ExprStmt case a bare `expr?`, dispatching to unwrap/unwrapResult/unwrapOption. A
  Result `?` destructures the callee's lowered arity (calleeSig off
  sema.FuncSignatures: plain-error callee -> 1 value, Result callee -> 2) and on
  failure returns the function's own (ok, err); an Option `?` mints a fresh pointer
  temp per site and returns nil.
- The whole __goal_ name family (ok/err/v/some/o) is gone. emitFile seeds
  emitter.fileIdents via fileIdentSet(f); funcDecl opens a per-function scope
  (newScope copy) and mints the open-E Result named returns up front (gensym
  "ok"/"err") so the signature and body agree; match/Option-box/`?` temps are local
  gensyms. gensym(want) appends the least integer suffix avoiding any in-scope name,
  so result_int's source `err` forces the named error return to `err1` — the
  scope-aware witness. Output is build+vet-clean (not byte-identical to the splice
  goldens — US-042 regenerates those).
- Files changed:
  - internal/backend/emit.go (emitter.fileIdents/taken/okName/errName; gensym +
    newScope; funcDecl scope setup; funcSig fallback names; stmt() `?` dispatch;
    unwrap/unwrapResult/unwrapOption/calleeSig; resultMatch/optionMatch/
    emitResultReturn/emitOptionReturn now use scoped names; doc refresh)
  - internal/backend/lower.go (removed the __goal_ const block; added fileIdentSet)
  - internal/backend/backend_test.go (US-035 tests: QuestionBehavioralTier,
    QuestionNoMagicPrefix, QuestionScopeAware, QuestionEncoding; updated US-034's
    ResultOptionEncoding pins to the new gensym names)
  - prd.json (US-035 passes:true), progress.txt
  - history/20260627-feature-us-035-lower-emit-question-real-gensym/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - A statement-position match can sit in a NON-Result function (03-result
    result_match's `handle` returns nothing), so its destructure value/error names
    MUST be fresh local gensyms — NOT the enclosing function's named returns. Only
    `?` propagation uses the function's okName/errName (it early-returns them).
  - The named-return names must be minted in funcDecl BEFORE funcSig runs, because
    funcSig emits them in the signature and the body references the same; keep them
    on the emitter (okName/errName), save+restore around the function.
  - `?` is lowered at statement position only; a nested `?` inside an expression
    still has no expr() case (not in the corpus). US-037 (closed-E `?`) plugs into
    the same unwrap dispatch — a closed-E Result function is roNone today, so its
    `?` currently hits the descriptive refusal rather than being mis-lowered.

## [2026-06-27T12:30:00Z] - US-034
- The AST backend lowers a function's enclosing Result/Option mode via an
  `emitter.fnKind` (roNone/roResultOpen/roOption from resultOptionKind off the
  *ast.FuncType result), set+restored around the body in funcDecl. A `return
  Result.Ok/Err(...)` / `return Option.Some/None` constructor is lowered ONLY when
  fnKind matches — so a bare `return` or a non-Result return is untouched. This is
  the AST analogue of the splice passes' funcSpans/sigAt scoping (internal/pass/
  result.go, option.go), but read off the parse tree.
- Statement-position match is intercepted in the stmt() *ast.ExprStmt case (a
  statement-position match parses to ExprStmt{X: *MatchExpr}); matchQualifier(m)
  (first VariantPattern's Enum Ident name) picks Result vs Option lowering. Enum
  and value-position match still error (US-036). Value-position match lives in
  assign/return, reaches expr() not stmt(), and still hits expr's default fail.
- Match-arm binding rename is done with an `emitter.renames map[string]string`
  consulted in the Ident emission, set for the duration of one arm body
  (armBodyRenamed, defer delete). Result renames Ok binding->__goal_v (or `_` if
  usesIdent says unused) and Err binding->__goal_err; Option does NOT rename (it
  declares `bind := *__goal_o` keeping the original name). usesIdent walks the arm
  body via an identFinder ast.Visitor adapter.
- A match-arm Body is a generic ast.Node: armBody() type-switches ast.Stmt
  (block/return) -> e.stmt, ast.Expr -> e.expr (expression statement). Assert
  ast.Stmt BEFORE ast.Expr (disjoint interfaces, but order documents intent).
- Output is BYTE-IDENTICAL to the checked-in 03-result/04-option goldens (reusing
  the __goal_ names from internal/pass/pass.go) — a good omen for US-042's golden
  regen, though US-035 will retire the __goal_ prefix for `?` propagation.
- Closed-E Result match is refused (not mis-lowered) by the open-E path via
  emitter.calleeMode (sema.Info.FuncSignatures[callee].Mode == ModeResultClosed
  -> e.fail); the open-E path is correct for all of feature 03. Closed-E is US-037.
- Files changed:
  - internal/backend/lower.go (name consts; roKind/resultOptionKind; isErrorIdent;
    matchQualifier; usesIdent + identFinder visitor)
  - internal/backend/emit.go (emitter.fnKind/renames; funcDecl fnKind scope;
    funcSig open-E named returns; indexExpr Option->*T; Ident rename; returnStmt +
    emitResultReturn/emitOptionReturn; matchStmt/resultMatch/optionMatch + armBody/
    armBodyRenamed/armByVariant/bindingName/calleeMode)
  - internal/backend/backend_test.go (TestASTEngineResultOptionBehavioralTier over
    all 8 03/04 cases; TestASTEngineResultOptionEncoding pins the shapes)
  - prd.json (US-034 passes:true), progress.txt
  - history/20260627-feature-us-034-lower-emit-result-and-option/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - US-035 (? with real gensym), US-036 (value-position match), US-037 (closed-E
    Result) extend the same seam: an encoder/helper in lower.go + a dispatch case
    in emit.go. The fnKind/renames/calleeMode machinery is reusable — US-037's
    closed-E match can branch off matchStmt where resultMatch currently guards.
  - resultOptionKind keys on the result TYPE EXPRESSION (IndexListExpr Result[T,
    error] with isErrorIdent on the 2nd arg; IndexExpr Option[T]); it does NOT read
    sema, so it is correct even where sema is unpopulated. sema is consulted only
    for the closed-E match guard (calleeMode).
  - Option[T] -> *T is lowered in the expr() IndexExpr case (indexExpr), so it
    fires wherever the type appears, not just return position; the Result open-E
    NAMED-return form is funcSig-only (named returns only make sense in return
    position).

## [2026-06-27T04:10:00Z] - US-004

  interface{ Check(src string)([]check.Diagnostic,error) } plus a CheckerFunc
  adapter so the free check.Analyze satisfies it without changing the check
  package. RunCheck(root, Case, Checker) reads each KindCheck case's .goal input,
  runs the checker, and matches diagnostics against inline `// want "substr"`

## [2026-06-27T05:30:00Z] - US-005

## [2026-06-27T11:30:00Z] - US-032
- Phase 2 emitter completion: internal/backend/emit.go now emits the FULL
  ordinary-Go subset the parser produces, not just the US-026 seed set. Added
  expression-switch emission (*ast.SwitchStmt + *ast.CaseClause via switchStmt/
  caseClause) — the seed emitter failed on any plain-Go `switch`. Also fixed a
  latent US-026 bug surfaced by the first struct-bearing fixture: fieldList
  COMMA-joined struct fields / interface methods (`struct { A int, B int }` is a
  Go SYNTAX error gofmt cannot repair). Replaced the StructType/InterfaceType
  expr cases with newline-separating structType/interfaceType emitters; interface
  methods now render `Name(params) results` (no `func` keyword). The struct
  `implements` guard moved into structType (still fails — goal-specific, US-033).
- AC2 (behavioral tier) proven by corpus.RunCompile over a new full-subset
  fixture (switch, struct type + composite literal, interface type, map literal +
  range, slice, defer, multi-return, const/var) — generated Go builds + vets in a
  temp module. AC1 (switch -> valid Go) proven by a focused transpile+format test.
- Files changed:
  - internal/backend/emit.go (switchStmt/caseClause; structType/interfaceType;
    doc refresh; fieldList doc clarified to params/results/recv only)
  - internal/backend/testdata/plain_full.goal (new full-subset fixture)
  - internal/backend/backend_test.go (TestASTEngineEmitsSwitch,
    TestASTEngineBehavioralTierFull)
  - prd.json (US-032 passes:true), progress.txt
  - history/20260627-feature-us-032-emit-go-subset-from-ast/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - STRUCT FIELDS and INTERFACE METHODS are newline/semicolon-separated in Go, NOT
    comma-separated; the emitter must not route them through the comma-joining
    fieldList (which is correct ONLY for param/result/receiver lists). A bad
    separator here is a parse error, so the format-once GoFormatter pass surfaces
    it as "generated Go did not parse" — not a layout nit. Any future field-list
    emission must pick the right separator by context.
  - Interface method form is `Name(params) results`, distinct from a struct field
    `name Type`: render the method's *ast.FuncType via funcSig WITHOUT the `func`
    keyword; embedded interfaces emit just the type name.
  - goal's parser does NOT accept func-literal IIFEs (`func(){}()` — parseOperand
    has no FUNC case; token.FUNC there is the func-TYPE) nor trailing variadic
    call spread (`f(xs...)` — CallExpr has no Ellipsis field). Keep them out of
    plain-Go fixtures; they are not part of goal's Go subset.
  - The behavioral-tier seam for ANY ad-hoc plain-Go fixture is unchanged from
    US-026: corpus.Case{Kind:KindTranspile, Mode:ModeFile, Input:<repo-rel path>}
    + corpus.RunCompile(repoRoot, c, corpus.TranspilerFunc(backend.Transpile)),
    -short-skipped (spawns the go toolchain). US-033+ reuse it per goal construct.

## [2026-06-27T03:17:00Z] - US-011
- Added internal/token (Phase 1.1), the first stone of the AST front-end: a Kind
  for every goal lexeme + a first-class Pos{Offset,Line,Col}. Modeled on go/token
  (iota-backed Kind, *_beg/*_end range markers, kindNames table, String()), but
  zero-import (a tiny local itoa keeps the package import-free). The goal-specific
  lexemes the splice passes faked are first-class kinds: QUESTION(?), FAT_ARROW(=>)
  as ONE token (asserted distinct from ASSIGN/GTR), ELLIPSIS(...), DOC_COMMENT(///).
  Contextual keywords implements/sealed/from/derive are deliberately NOT kinds —
  they lex as IDENT; tests pin IsKeyword==false and Lookup==(ILLEGAL,false) for them.
- Lookup(name)(Kind,bool) is the inverse of String over the operator+keyword ranges
  (keyword map then operator map; unknown -> (ILLEGAL,false)). Pos.Less orders by
  byte Offset (Offset is the canonical total order; Line/Col carried for diagnostics).
- Files changed:
  - internal/token/token.go (Kind + constants + String/Lookup/IsKeyword + range
    predicates + Pos + Less + Token{Kind,Lit,Pos})
  - internal/token/token_test.go (round-trip over both ranges, goal lexemes,
    contextual-keyword exclusion, unknown lookup, class predicates, Pos ordering)
  - history/20260627-feature-us-011-token-package-with-positions/ (initiative)
- Commit: 73bcb02
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - US-012 (lexer) emits []token.Token; the kinds/positions it needs already exist
    here. '///' (DOC_COMMENT) must be matched BEFORE '//' (COMMENT) and '=>'
    (FAT_ARROW) BEFORE '=' in the lexer's longest-match logic.
  - Only true reserved words are keyword kinds (Go reserved + match/enum/assert).
    Adding a contextual keyword as a Kind here would break the parser's positional
    disambiguation design — keep them IDENT.
  - The package is intentionally import-free (local itoa) so it sits at the very
    bottom of the dependency graph; do not add imports lightly.
---

## [2026-06-27T03:26:00Z] - US-012
- Added internal/lexer (Phase 1.2), the second stone of the AST front-end: a
  hand-written scanner that turns goal source into []token.Token for the core Go
  subset — identifiers, reserved keywords, int/float/imag/char/string literals,
  the full operator+delimiter set, and // and /* */ comments — each carrying an
  accurate token.Pos{Offset, Line, Col}. Modeled on go/scanner but smaller and
  emitting our token.Token directly.
- API: New(src)*Lexer + (*Lexer).Next() token.Token (incremental, for the future
  parser) and Tokens(src)[]token.Token (whole-slice, for tests). Cursor tracks
  offset/rdOffset/ch plus line + lineStart; Col = offset-lineStart+1, Line bumps
  after each '\n'. Multi-char operators are longest-matched via nested switches;
  unrecognized bytes become ILLEGAL tokens (carrying the byte + Pos) without
  panicking and still advance, guaranteeing progress; the stream ends in EOF.
- SCOPE: goal-specific lexemes are deliberately deferred to US-013 — '?' lexes as
  ILLEGAL, '=>' as ASSIGN then GTR, '.' always as PERIOD (no ELLIPSIS), and '///'
  scans as an ordinary '//' line COMMENT. Do NOT emit QUESTION/FAT_ARROW/ELLIPSIS/
  DOC_COMMENT or attach trivia here; that is US-013's job.
- Files changed:
  - internal/lexer/lexer.go (Lexer + New/Next/Tokens + scan methods)
  - internal/lexer/lexer_test.go (multi-line position test = the AC; plus
    keyword/ident, literals, longest-match operators, ILLEGAL, comments)
  - history/20260627-feature-us-012-lex-core-go-tokens-with-positions/ (initiative)
- Commit: 799f761
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - The multi-line acceptance test pins exact Offset/Line/Col per token by hand;
    when editing the sample, recompute byte offsets carefully (blank lines and
    leading tabs each advance offset by 1; tab is one byte column).
  - next() applies the pending newline's line/col bump at the START of the call
    (when the just-consumed ch was '\n'), so a token's Pos is captured before any
    newline is crossed — keep that ordering if you touch the cursor.
  - US-013 extends THIS lexer: fold '=>'→FAT_ARROW and '...'→ELLIPSIS into
    scanOperator, emit '?'→QUESTION (currently ILLEGAL), and special-case '///'
    in the comment path to DOC_COMMENT, retaining comment text as trivia.
---

## [2026-06-27T04:30:00Z] - US-013
- Wired the goal-specific lexemes into internal/lexer (Phase 1.3). The token
  kinds already existed (US-011); this story makes the US-012 lexer emit them as
  single tokens instead of the deferred fallbacks: '?'→QUESTION (was ILLEGAL),
  '=>'→FAT_ARROW one token (was ASSIGN then GTR), '...'→ELLIPSIS one token (was
  three PERIODs), and '///<line>'→DOC_COMMENT retained as trivia (was an
  ordinary '//' COMMENT). The contextual keywords implements/sealed/from/derive
  already lexed as IDENT via token.Lookup (token.keywords omits them) — no code
  change, just a pinned assertion (TestKeywordVsIdent already covered it).
- Added a peek2() two-rune lookahead so '///' and '...' can be longest-matched
  past peek(); the '/' case checks the third '/' before committing to '//', the
  '=' case checks for '>' before '='/'==', and the '.' case checks for two more
  dots before a single PERIOD. The '.'-then-digit FLOAT path in Next() is
  unaffected ('...' has no digit after the first dot). scanDocComment mirrors
  scanLineComment but tags DOC_COMMENT and keeps the full '/// ...' text.
- Files changed:
  - internal/lexer/lexer.go (peek2, scanDocComment, '?'/'='/'.'/'/' cases,
    refreshed package + case doc comments)
  - internal/lexer/lexer_test.go (TestGoalLexemes, TestGoalLexemesInContext,
    TestDocCommentTrivia; freshened TestComments doc)
  - history/20260627-feature-us-013-lex-goal-specific-lexemes-and-trivia/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Longest-match ordering is load-bearing: check '///' before '//', '=>' before
    '='/'==', '...' before '.'. peek2() is the seam for the three-char forms; the
    two-char '=>' uses the existing l.next()+switch idiom.
  - A '///'-prefixed line is ALWAYS a DOC_COMMENT (even '////...'), consumed to
    end of line; the parser (later story) decides attachment. Lexer-level
    "trivia" here just means "emitted as a distinct DOC_COMMENT token".
  - US-014+ (AST nodes / parser) consume token.QUESTION/FAT_ARROW/ELLIPSIS/
    DOC_COMMENT directly; the lexer now never fakes them.

## [2026-06-27T03:43:00Z] - US-014
- Added internal/ast (Phase 1.4), the one structural model the whole rewrite is
  built around. ast.go declares the position-carrying Node interface
  (Pos()/End()), the closed category markers Decl/Stmt/Expr/Spec (each embeds
  Node + a private marker method, so membership stays package-closed), and the
  Go-subset node set: File, GenDecl/FuncDecl, ImportSpec/ValueSpec/TypeSpec,
  Field/FieldList, the Go exprs (Ident, BasicLit, Paren/Unary/Binary/Selector/
  Index/Slice/Call/Star/CompositeLit/KeyValue/FuncLit), the type exprs
  (Array/Map/Struct/Interface/Func/Chan/Ellipsis), and the Go stmts (Block/Expr/
  Assign/IncDec/Return/If/For/Range/Switch/CaseClause/Defer/Go/Branch/Decl/Empty).
- walk.go adds Visitor{ Visit(Node) Visitor } and Walk(v, node): pre-order,
  go/ast convention — visit node, recurse into children only when Visit returns
  non-nil, then Visit(nil) to mark end-of-children. Walk(v, nil) and nil child
  fields are no-ops (guarded). Helpers walkExpr/walkExprList/walkIdentList/
  walkStmtList keep the nil-skipping in one place.
- ast_test.go (package ast, stdlib testing only) builds a representative *File
  tree by hand, registering every constructed node via an `add` helper, then a
  collector Visitor records each non-nil Visit. Asserts: visited count ==
  constructed count, every node visited exactly once (visit-count map), and no
  unexpected node visited. Plus TestWalkNilNodeIsNoop.
- Files changed:
  - internal/ast/ast.go (Node/Decl/Stmt/Expr/Spec + all Go-subset nodes)
  - internal/ast/walk.go (Visitor + Walk + walk* helpers)
  - internal/ast/ast_test.go (Walk-visits-every-node-once + nil no-op)
  - history/20260627-feature-us-014-core-ast-nodes-and-walk/ (initiative)
- Commit: c42a8ad
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Modeled on go/ast trimmed to goal's subset, but nodes carry our own
    token.Pos (Offset/Line/Col) — positions live on the tree, not re-derived.
  - US-015 (enum/sealed/implements/from-derive decls) and US-016 (match/pattern/
    construction exprs) ADD nodes here and ADD cases to Walk's type switch; the
    switch is intentionally open. Keep marker methods (declNode/stmtNode/
    exprNode/specNode) on every new node so it joins the right category.
  - The "visited exactly once" property is the go/ast Walk invariant: a node is
    counted on the single non-nil Visit(node) call; the trailing Visit(nil)
    end-markers carry nil and are not counted. The test's collector ignores nil.
  - token.Pos zero value is token.Pos{} (all-zero); FieldList/FuncType guard
    "Opening/Func is set" by comparing against token.Pos{}.

## [2026-06-27T08:30:00Z] - US-015

  StructType via a new optional Implements field (no separate StructDecl) —

- Learnings for future iterations:

    because every construction is a KEYED struct literal (ast_test.go is the sole
    consumer); a positional literal would break. Keep ast literals keyed.
  - New support nodes (Node, not Decl/Stmt/Expr) walk fine — Walk takes Node, so
    Variant/PayloadField/ImplementsClause need no category marker; only the two
    top-level decls carry declNode().
  - US-016 ADDS the goal EXPRESSION/pattern nodes (MatchExpr/MatchArm,
    VariantPattern/RestPattern, UnwrapExpr, VariantLit/LabeledArg, SpreadElement)
    the same way: define in a new file, add Walk cases, assert Walk descent.
  - The Walk-descent test pattern: collect(root) -> map[Node]int via the existing
    collector, then assert parent + each declared child == 1 visit. Reuse it.
---

## [2026-06-27T04:05:00Z] - US-016
- Added goal's expression/pattern surface to internal/ast (Phase 1.5 exprs): the
  match/postfix-?/construction/spread nodes that make the three meanings of
  Enum.Variant(x) distinct node types (the structural fix for the
  Match-before-Enums ordering hack). New file internal/ast/goal_expr.go declares
  MatchExpr/MatchArm, VariantPattern/RestPattern, UnwrapExpr,
  VariantLit/LabeledArg, and SpreadElement.
- Design: MatchExpr is an Expr (so value-position `var x = match ...`, refused by
  the splice approach today, is representable); statement-position match is the
  same node used where a statement is expected (no separate MatchStmt). MatchArm
  is a support node (Node only, like Variant); its Body is a generic Node so an
  expression body (value position) or a statement/block body both fit — walked
  via Walk(v, n.Body) guarded by nil, NOT walkExpr (walkExpr takes Expr).
  VariantLit (construct) and VariantPattern (destructure) are deliberately
  separate types of the same surface syntax. RestPattern is its own node (not a
  `_` Ident) so exhaustiveness can spot the wildcard arm.
- Walk gained a "Goal expressions and patterns" case block; nodes carry token.Pos
  with nil/zero-Pos guards mirroring goal_decl.go. TestWalkGoalExprChildren
  (package ast, stdlib testing + fmt only) asserts Walk descends into each child
  exactly once AND that fmt.Sprintf("%T") of the VariantLit != that of the
  VariantPattern (== *ast.VariantLit / *ast.VariantPattern), satisfying AC 2.
- Files changed:
  - internal/ast/goal_expr.go (new: 8 nodes)
  - internal/ast/walk.go (new case block)
  - internal/ast/ast_test.go (+fmt import, TestWalkGoalExprChildren)
  - history/20260627-feature-us-016-goal-expression-and-pattern-ast-nodes/ (initiative)
- Commit: efa31ad
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Adding goal nodes is a 3-file move: declare in a new goal_*.go file, add a
    Walk case per node, add a Walk-descent test reusing collector/assertChildren
    from TestWalkGoalDeclChildren. Keep ast literals KEYED (ast_test is the sole
    constructor) so field additions stay safe.
  - For a child typed as `Node` (not Expr/Stmt), Walk it with Walk(v, child)
    guarded by `!= nil`; walkExpr/walkExprList only accept Expr. MatchArm.Body is
    the one such field here.
  - The "distinct node types" assertion idiom is dependency-free %T string
    comparison — no reflect, no testify.
  - US-017+ (parser) construct these nodes; US-033+/US-035/US-036 lower them
    (enum match, ? gensym, value-position match). The node set is now complete
    for the parser stories.

## [2026-06-27T05:10:00Z] - US-017
- Added internal/parser (Phase 1.4, declaration tier): a hand-written, Go-grammar-
  shaped recursive-descent parser turning the lexer's token stream into an
  *ast.File. ParseFile(src)(*ast.File,error) parses the package clause, single and
  grouped imports (incl. named `m "math"`, blank `_ "x"`, dot `. "x"`), and single
  and grouped func/type/var/const declarations of the Go subset, plus the full
  Go-subset type expressions (qualified/indexed names, pointer, array/slice, map,
  struct w/ field list, interface w/ method list, func, chan). It collects every
  ImportSpec onto File.Imports as well as File.Decls.
- Scope deferrals (matched to later stories): function bodies are captured as a
  balanced-brace *ast.BlockStmt with NO statement list (US-018); initializer values
  use a minimal operand+postfix expr parser — literals/ident/paren/selector/call/
  index/composite-lit, NO binary/unary/postfix-? (US-019); goal-specific decls
  (enum/sealed/implements/from/derive) are NOT parsed here (US-020+).
- Files changed:
  - internal/parser/parser.go (new: parser + ParseFile + decl/type/expr methods)
  - internal/parser/parser_test.go (new: declaration-shape test over a 12-decl
    Go-subset sample + struct/alias/interface + composite-initializer + error-path
    + well-formed-no-error tests)
  - prd.json (US-017 passes:true)
  - history/20260627-feature-us-017-parse-package-imports-declarations/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - NO SEMICOLON INSERTION: the lexer emits no newline/`;` terminators, so the
    parser delimits structurally — top-level decls dispatch on the leading keyword
    (PACKAGE/IMPORT/CONST/VAR/TYPE/FUNC); grouped specs / field lists / param lists
    run until their closing delimiter; minimal value parsing stops at the first
    token it can't extend. Consequence: a valueless, untyped, multi-spec grouped
    const/var (`const ( A \n B )`) is ambiguous and unsupported — give specs a
    value or a type. US-018 (statements) must adopt the same no-`;` discipline.
  - expect() ALWAYS advances (recording an error on mismatch) so every loop makes
    progress on malformed input; top-level + spec/field/param loops also guard EOF.
    ParseFile returns errors.Join(errs...) (nil for well-formed Go-subset input).
  - Parameter/field name-vs-type disambiguation uses ONE-token lookahead
    (nameThenType / peekKind): after an IDENT, COMMA/RPAREN/PERIOD ⇒ unnamed or
    qualified type; a type-start token ⇒ the IDENT was a name. Generic-instantiated
    *param* types (`x Foo[T]`) are intentionally not disambiguated (IDENT `[` reads
    as an array-typed named param); avoid them until later type-arg-list support.
  - internal/parser imports lexer+token+ast only; none import parser, so its tests
    are package parser (INTERNAL) — no external-_test dance needed (unlike corpus).
  - Function bodies: parseBlockSkip records Lbrace/Rbrace and balances braces; US-018
    fills in BlockStmt.List by parsing the token span between them.

## [2026-06-26T21:40:00Z] - US-018
- Implemented statement parsing in internal/parser (Phase 1.4, statement tier).
  parseBlockSkip (balanced-brace skip) is replaced by parseBlock, which fills
  ast.BlockStmt.List by parsing statements; parseFuncDecl now calls it. Added
  parseStmt (leading-token dispatch) and the statement parsers: parseSimpleStmt
  (expr stmt / assignment / short-var / inc-dec, with range detection),
  parseIfStmt (init/cond + else-if chain + else block), parseForStmt (infinite,
  condition-only, three-clause init;cond;post, and range forms), parseSwitchStmt
  + parseCaseClause (expression switch with case/default), parseReturnStmt,
  parseCallStmt (defer/go), parseBranchStmt (break/continue/goto/fallthrough),
  DeclStmt-wrapped const/var/type, and EmptyStmt for a stray ';'.
- Files changed:
  - internal/parser/parser.go (parseBlock + all statement methods; exprLev field
    + composite-literal suppression in control headers; package doc refreshed)
  - internal/parser/parser_test.go (TestParseFunctionBodyStatements: a 13-stmt
    body exercising every required form; asserts list shape + per-stmt details)
  - prd.json (US-018 passes:true)
  - history/20260627-feature-us-018-parse-statements/ (initiative + spec)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - NO SEMICOLON INSERTION (carried from US-017): statement lists are delimited
    structurally. parseBlock loops until RBRACE; each statement parser consumes
    exactly its tokens and stops. Explicit ';' (three-clause for header) is lexed
    as token.SEMICOLON and consumed where the grammar expects it; a stray one is
    an EmptyStmt.
  - COMPOSITE-LITERAL vs BLOCK ambiguity is the load-bearing gotcha: with no
    semicolons, `ident {` at statement level is read as a composite literal. The
    fix is go/parser's exprLev: parser.exprLev < 0 while parsing a control-clause
    header suppresses the brace-composite in parsePostfix, so a trailing body `{`
    is taken as the block. Bracketed contexts (parens/index/call/composite elts)
    do exprLev++ so composites are re-enabled inside them (`if check(T{})`). A
    statement whose final expression is a bare Ident/Selector/Index that is then
    immediately followed by a standalone block `{...}` is STILL ambiguous at
    exprLev 0 — order test inputs so a block follows a literal/call-terminated
    statement, not a bare-ident one. This is inherent to the tokenization until
    newline-aware lexing or `?`/full-expr work changes it.
  - for/if/switch headers share a pattern: set exprLev=-1, parse a simple stmt;
    if a ';' follows it was the Init (cond/tag parsed next), else the simple stmt
    WAS the cond/tag (extract via stmtExpr, which pulls X out of an ExprStmt);
    restore exprLev before parsing the body block.
  - Range detection lives in parseSimpleStmt(allowRange): after the assign token
    (:= or =), a `range` keyword yields *ast.RangeStmt (Key/Value from the lhs
    list) instead of an AssignStmt. parseForStmt passes allowRange=true.
  - internal/parser still imports only lexer+token+ast; tests stay package parser
    (internal). US-019 layers full Pratt expressions + postfix ? onto the same
    expression parser (parseExpr/parseOperand/parsePostfix) used here.
---

## [2026-06-27T04:40:00Z] - US-019
- Upgraded internal/parser from a flat operand+postfix expression grammar to
  precedence-correct parsing (Phase 1.4, expression tier). parseExpr now does
  precedence climbing over Go's five binary levels via parseBinary(minPrec)
  (left-assoc: the recursive call uses opPrec+1), layered on parseUnary for the
  prefix operators (+ - ! ^ & <- as ast.UnaryExpr; *x as ast.StarExpr). goal's
  postfix `?` joins the existing selector/call/index chain in parsePostfix as a
  dedicated ast.UnwrapExpr, so it binds tightest and "falls out of the grammar":
  f(x)? unwraps the call, a.b? unwraps the selector. startsExpr broadened to
  include unary-operator starts so a unary-led expression is recognized after
  `return`.
- A precedence() helper maps token kinds to 1..5 (0 = non-binary); ARROW (`<-`)
  is deliberately 0 (unary-only, matching Go — channel send is a statement).
- Files changed:
  - internal/parser/parser.go (precedence + parseBinary + parseUnary; parseExpr
    rewired; QUESTION case in parsePostfix; startsExpr broadened; doc refresh)
  - internal/parser/parser_test.go (TestParseExpressionPrecedence: f(x)?, a.b?,
    a+b*c==d, a-b-c, -a*b, via a parseExprInBody helper)
  - history/20260627-feature-us-019-parse-expressions-pratt-postfix-question/
- Commit: 9fb591b
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Every expression caller (parseExprList, parseValueSpec, parseSimpleStmt,
    control headers, return, array length, index, composite elts) routes through
    the single parseExpr entry point, so they ALL gained full precedence with no
    call-site change. When extending expressions (US-021 match, US-022 variant
    construction/spread), hook into parseUnary/parseOperand/parsePostfix, not the
    callers.
  - exprLev composite-literal suppression is preserved — parseUnary/parseBinary
    don't touch exprLev; the LBRACE guard in parsePostfix still governs composite
    literals in control headers. Keep that invariant when adding expr forms.
  - The new-test idiom for a bare expression: wrap it as
    `package p\nfunc f() { _ = <expr> }`, ParseFile, then read
    FuncDecl.Body.List[0].(*ast.AssignStmt).Rhs[0]. Reuse parseExprInBody.
  - Postfix `?` lives in the postfix chain (tightest), so `-x?` is `-(x?)`.

## [2026-06-27T05:55:00Z] - US-025
- Added deterministic AST snapshot tests (Phase 1, parser structural gate;
  replaces the tree-sitter differential). New internal/ast/dump.go exports
  ast.Sexpr(Node) string: a reflection-driven, position-free s-expression
  renderer. It walks each node's EXPORTED struct fields, SKIPS token.Pos fields
  (so a snapshot pins structure, not byte offsets that shift with whitespace),
  renders token.Kind via String() and names FuncMod/ChanDir, elides zero/empty
  fields, and recurses pointers/interfaces/slices. Output is deterministic
  (fixed struct field order, no map iteration) and stdlib-only
  (reflect/strings/fmt) so the zero-dependency rule holds.
- New internal/parser/snapshot_test.go: TestASTSnapshots parses one
  representative .goal per goal construct, renders via ast.Sexpr, and diffs
  against a committed golden under internal/parser/testdata/snapshots/<name>.sexpr.
  A `-update-snapshots` flag regenerates the goldens; a plain `go test ./...`
  (no flag) compares. The test also asserts ast.Sexpr is deterministic (two
  renders equal) and t.Fatal's if no cases are declared.
- 9 representative inputs / goldens cover every goal-specific node:
  enum (EnumDecl/Variant/PayloadField, VariantLit/LabeledArg, data-less
  SelectorExpr), match (MatchExpr/MatchArm/VariantPattern/RestPattern), question
  -prop (UnwrapExpr + IndexListExpr Result[int,error]), error-e (closed Result
  match + IndexListExpr), implements (StructType.Implements/ImplementsClause +
  method Recv), defaults (SpreadElement ...defaults), assert (AssertStmt printf
  form), doctests (DocComment/Doctest), derive-convert (FuncFrom/FuncDerive
  bodyless modifiers).

  - ast.Sexpr is the reusable structural-rendering seam: US-045 (goal fmt) and

## [2026-06-27T06:30:00Z] - US-027
- Phase 2 symbol resolution: internal/sema now derives the name-keyed semantic
  facts (enums, structs, function signatures, the from-registry, methods) by
  WALKING the parsed goal AST instead of re-scanning a flat token stream like
  internal/analyze. Because the facts come off the parse tree they are correct by
  construction where analyze is not — most visibly a struct field whose type
  carries a top-level comma (analyze.parseStructBody whitespace-splits and mangles
  it; the AST walk renders the field type from its type node, so the comma never
  confuses resolution).
- sema.go: Info grew from a placeholder into the fact tables (FuncSignatures,
  Enums, Sealed, Structs, FromRegistry, Methods) plus the supporting types
  (Mode/FuncSig/Field/Variant/Enum/ConvEntry/Method). Mode uses the SAME iota
  order as analyze.Mode so the two resolvers' modes compare equal as ints. New()
  still returns an EMPTY (nil-map) *Info for the plain-Go back-end seam.
- resolve.go: Resolve(*ast.File) *Info walks File.Decls — EnumDecl -> Enums (+
  VSet/FieldSet); GenDecl(TYPE)+StructType -> Structs; SealedInterfaceDecl ->
  Sealed; FuncDecl routed by Mod/Recv (from|derive -> FromRegistry keyed by
  (firstParamType, resultTarget); receiver -> Methods star-stripped; else ->
  FuncSignatures). Result/Option mode is detected off the single unnamed result's
  IndexExpr/IndexListExpr head Ident, then the lowered arity/ends-in-error is
  applied exactly like analyze.analyzeSig (Result -> 2/true, Option & closed-E ->
  1/false). typeString is a small position-free AST type printer (Ident/Selector/
  Star/Paren/Array/Map/Index(+List)/Ellipsis/Chan/Func/Interface/Struct) that is
  comma-safe by construction.
- resolve_test.go (package sema, stdlib testing): TestResolveMatchesAnalyze diffs
  sema vs analyze.Build over a representative source (enum w/ payload + data-less
  variant, struct, plain func, open-E Result/Option/closed-E Result funcs, from
  func, derive func, value+pointer methods, sealed interface) — type strings
  compared modulo whitespace. TestResolveStructCommaFieldType resolves a
  generic-typed field Result[int, error] to one correct field AND asserts
  analyze.Build mishandles the same comma-bearing type (the documented bug).
- Files changed:
  - internal/sema/sema.go (placeholder Info -> populated fact tables + types)
  - internal/sema/resolve.go (new: Resolve + walk + typeString)
  - internal/sema/resolve_test.go (new: parity + comma-bug tests)
  - prd.json (US-027 passes:true), progress.txt
  - history/20260627-feature-us-027-resolve-symbols-by-ast-walk/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - sema does NOT import analyze (it is the replacement); the parity test lives in
    package sema and imports parser+analyze (neither imports sema, so no cycle).
  - The comma-bug exemplar must be a BRACKET-delimited comma type (a generic
    instance like Result[int, error]), NOT a func-typed struct field: with no
    semicolon insertion the lexer makes `cb func(int, string)\n name string` parse
    as ONE field whose result type is `name` — a parser ambiguity, not a sema bug.
    Bracket-delimited generic args parse unambiguously while still defeating
    analyze's whitespace split.
  - sema.New() stays the empty seam; backend.Transpile still calls it. Wiring
    Resolve into the emit path is US-032+. Adding Resolve here is inert to the
    back-end (Emit does not read Info yet), so blast radius is internal/sema only.
  - Method Arity/EndsInError use RAW result counts (no Result/Option override),
    matching analyze.methodFrom; plain FuncSignatures DO apply the override.
  - typeString renders types modulo whitespace; any future exact-spelling consumer
    (e.g. a comparison against verbatim source) must normalize whitespace or use a
    position-carrying printer instead.

  no-zero-value must eventually come from a native checker; this story is purely

    not produce a go/types view, so the stable contract is the findings, not the
    typed internals. Returns an error only for a transpile/parse failure (a
    goal-compiler bug), exactly like Load.

    Load then CheckImplements + CheckMustUse + CheckNoZeroValue in that order.

  - The interface-seam pattern in this repo is uniform: define the interface +
    a concrete impl in the same package, route the single caller through an
    interface-typed value, add a parity test. Backend/Formatter/Transpiler/Checker
    all follow it; TypeChecker matches.

    typecheck.Load return an error (the lowered Go fails to parse) — a stable,

## [2026-06-27T06:46:00Z] - US-030
- Reimplemented feature-08 (no-zero-value, spec §8) field-completeness checking
  over the AST in internal/sema, the structural replacement for the lexical
  internal/check/fields.go. CheckFields walks the parse tree and flags struct
  literals / enum-variant constructions that omit a declared field without a
  completing spread, deferring on unresolved types — wired into sema.Check so the
  existing corpus.SemaCheck adapter forwards it unchanged.
- Files changed:
  - internal/sema/fields.go (new: CheckFields + helpers identName/litKeys/
    litHasSpread/labeledArgNames/variantFields/missingFieldNames/quoteJoin)

    testdata/check/08-no-zero-value cases)
  - history/20260627-feature-us-030-field-completeness-check-on-ast/ (initiative)
- Commit: 7431503
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - The three meanings of `Enum.Variant(x)` are now SEPARATE node types, so the
    08 check is correct by construction where the lexical check needs heuristics:
    a struct literal is *ast.CompositeLit (Type an *ast.Ident), a construction is
    *ast.VariantLit (the parser builds it ONLY when a call carries >=1 labeled
    arg — a data-less `Enum.Dot` stays a *ast.SelectorExpr, trivially complete),
    and a match-arm binding is *ast.VariantPattern. Walking VariantLit alone never
    sees a pattern, so the legacy match_binding_arm false positive is impossible —
    no span/skip-list machinery needed (cf. internal/check/fields.go
    matchPatternSpans, which exists solely to dodge that).
  - Present keys come off *ast.KeyValueExpr.Key (an *ast.Ident) for structs and
    *ast.LabeledArg.Label for variants; a `...defaults`/`...derive(s)` is an
    *ast.SpreadElement element => complete-by-construction (skip). Non-Ident
    composite types (slice/map/array, generic, pkg-qualified) are skipped, so
    struct tags (on the AST field) and element-type literals never false-positive.
  - Diagnostic MESSAGES + severities mirror internal/check/fields.go verbatim so
    the inline // want markers pass through corpus.RunCheck unchanged; codes are
    `missing-field` (Error) and `unresolved-literal-type` (Warning), Feature
    `08-no-zero-value`. Reused exprName/plural/pronoun from sema/check.go; added
    quoteJoin (backtick names, no enum prefix — distinct from check.go's
    quoteVariants which prefixes the enum).
  - The corpus check-runner pattern is now uniform across sema stories: a per-
    feature test (TestSemaExhaustiveRunner / TestSemaFieldsRunner) filters
    manifest KindCheck cases by Input prefix, drives each through
    CheckerFunc(SemaCheck) + RunCheck, t.Fatalf on zero. US-031 (must-use/
    implements/question) adds its check to sema.Check and a sibling runner test
    the same way.

## [2026-06-27T00:00:00Z] - US-031
- Reimplemented the remaining lexical static checks over the AST in internal/sema,
  wired into sema.Check (so the corpus SemaCheck adapter carries them automatically):
  must-use (feature 03), implements (feature 07), and the `?`-propagation checks —
  CheckQuestion (open-E feature 05 arity/refusal) and CheckClosed (closed-E feature
  06 From-totality + Result.Err closedness).
- Correct by construction off the parse tree, where the token scanner had to
  reconstruct shape:
  - A dropped Result is `*ast.ExprStmt{X: *ast.CallExpr{Fun: *ast.Ident}}` to a
    ModeResult/ModeResultClosed func. A consumed `f()?` is `ExprStmt{X: *UnwrapExpr}`
    (X is the UnwrapExpr, not the CallExpr) — so the drop walk never misreads a
    propagation, and match/return/bind/argument positions are never an ExprStmt's
    top-level CallExpr. No interface-brace-span skip needed (an interface method is a
    *FuncType, never an ExprStmt).
  - A match-arm `Result.Err(b)` is a `*ast.VariantPattern`; a constructed
    `Result.Err(E.V)` is `*ast.CallExpr{Fun: *SelectorExpr}` — distinct nodes, so the
    closedness walk never misreads a binding as a construction (legacy false positive
    structurally impossible).
- Files changed:
  - internal/sema/sema.go (Info += Interfaces, EmbeddedIfaces)
  - internal/sema/resolve.go (init the two maps; resolveInterface records in-file
    interface method sets + embeddings; resolveTypeDecl now switches struct/interface)
  - internal/sema/mustuse.go + _test.go (CheckMustUse)
  - internal/sema/implements.go + _test.go (CheckImplements + requiredMethods)
  - internal/sema/question.go + _test.go (CheckQuestion + CheckClosed)
  - internal/sema/check.go (wire the four checks into Check)
  - internal/corpus/sema_question_test.go (TestSemaQuestionImplementsRunner over
    03-result/06-error-e/07-implements — 21 cases, all pass)
  - history/20260627-feature-us-031-mustuse-implements-question-checks-on-ast/
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - sema had NO interface model — only structs. resolveInterface adds Interfaces
    (own methods) + EmbeddedIfaces (embedded names). Build interface Method.Sig with
    the SAME paramTypeListFL/joinTypes normalization resolveMethod uses, or the
    implements signature compare won't match. Leave interface Method.Raw EMPTY so
    sigForMsg falls back to sigText and the missing-method suggestion renders
    `Name() results` (matching the legacy // want markers).
  - sema.Check now runs ALL checks for EVERY SemaCheck caller, so the 02-match and
    08-no-zero-value runners exercise the new checks too. Before adding a check,
    confirm it cannot false-Error on those fixtures (it can't: no 02/08 fixture has a
    dropped Result statement, a struct `implements`, or a `?` in a Result function).
  - `?` sites are read only at well-formed statement positions (UnwrapExpr as an
    AssignStmt RHS or a bare ExprStmt X) via collectQuestionSites — this matches 100%
    of the corpus and avoids a `question-not-statement`-style Error on grammar the
    parser never produces.
  - The closed-E Err passthrough (a bare-ident Err arg like `Result.Err(e)`) is
    simplified to "non-`E.Variant` arg => defer Warning unresolved-err-value" rather
    than porting the lexical checker's param/var/match-binding passthrough analysis;
    it produces no false Error and satisfies the fixture.

## [2026-06-27T08:30:00Z] - US-033
- Phase 2 lowering: the AST Go backend now lowers goal's closed types — enums,
  sealed interfaces, the struct `implements` clause, and variant construction —
  so the 01-enums and 07-implements transpile cases pass the behavioral tier
  (corpus.RunCompile: temp-module go build + go vet) through `--engine=ast`.

  the arch doc marks lower/ir optional and emit.go already does direct emission).
  New internal/backend/lower.go holds the encoders mirrored from internal/pass
  (genEnum/genSealedInterface/genMarkerMethod/exported/pointerReceiverSet, plus
  nil-safe enumOf/isSealed over *sema.Info). backend.Transpile now resolves real
  semantics via sema.Resolve(file) (was sema.New(), which is empty), and
  goBackend.Emit threads info into emitFile(file, info). The emitter gained
  `info *sema.Info` + a `pointerRecv` set (computed locally because sema.Methods
  is star-stripped and can't say pointer-vs-value).
- emit.go lowering: decl() dispatches *ast.EnumDecl -> genEnum (marker interface +
  per-variant structs + per-variant marker methods) and *ast.SealedInterfaceDecl
  -> genSealedInterface; structType drops the implements clause (plain struct);
  implementsMarkers (called from decl after genDecl) emits the §8.5 marker AFTER
  the type decl — sealed -> `func (T) isI() {}`, else pointerRecv -> `var _ I =
  (*T)(nil)`, else `var _ I = T{}` (iface name via typeExprName, Ident/Selector);
  selectorExpr lowers a DATA-LESS variant (`Status.Pending` ->
  `Status(Status_Pending{})`, guarded by info.Enums + VSet so ordinary/qualified
  selectors are untouched); variantLit lowers payload construction
  (`Status.Active(since: now())` -> `Status(Status_Active{Since: now()})`, labels
  exported, values recursive so nested payloads lower for free).

## [2026-06-27T08:15:00Z] - US-036
- AST backend now lowers a goal `match` over an ENUM to a Go type-switch over the
  §8.1 sum encoding, in BOTH statement position and value position (`return match`
  and `var name T = match`). This completes match lowering on the new front-end:
  value-position match (refused by the splice engine's untyped form) now works for
  the typed forms.
- internal/backend/emit.go: new `enumMatch(m, pos, name)` + `matchPos`
  (posStmt/posReturn/posVar). `usesBinding` mints a scope-aware guard gensym `v`
  only when some arm references its payload binding (an unused-but-declared guard
  would not compile); `emitEnumArm` renames the binding to the guard (the existing
  `renames` map) and sets `armBinding`/`armFields` so a field access on the binding
  exports (`a.since` -> `v.Since`) through a new `selectorExpr` branch. A `_` rest
  arm becomes a real `default:`; otherwise the default panics with the §8.2
  non-exhaustive message. `armWrap` wraps each arm per position (bare /
  `return <body>` / `name = <body>`).
- Dispatch sites: `matchStmt` default branch (statement, guarded by
  `enumOf(info, q) != nil`); `returnStmt` (`return match` over an enum);
  new `tryVarMatch` off the `*ast.DeclStmt` case (`var name T = match`: emits
  `var name T` then the switch). Result/Option matches keep their dedicated
  lowering; matchStmt routes by `matchQualifier`.
- New corpus case features/02-match/examples/shape_value.goal (+ .go.expected,
  golden produced by the canonical splice engine so the legacy transpile runner
  stays green). Manifest regenerated 107->108; generate_test transpile count
  51->52.
- Files changed:
  - internal/backend/emit.go (emitter.armBinding/armFields; selectorExpr field
    export; matchStmt enum dispatch; matchPos + enumMatch/emitEnumArm/armWrap;
    returnStmt `return match`; stmt DeclStmt -> tryVarMatch)

    TestASTEngineEnumMatchBehavioralTier; TestASTEngineEnumMatchEncoding)

  - prd.json (US-036 passes:true), progress.txt
  - history/20260627-feature-us-036-lower-emit-match-value-position/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Enum match needs NO pass-ordering hack: the three meanings of `Enum.Variant`
    are distinct AST nodes, so a destructuring VariantPattern (match arm) is never
    confused with a construction. `matchQualifier` picks Result/Option vs enum off
    the first variant-pattern arm.
  - Value-position match reaches the emitter at STATEMENT level after all (a
    `return match`/`var = match` is a ReturnStmt/DeclStmt whose value is a
    MatchExpr) — so it is intercepted in returnStmt/stmt, NOT in expr(). MatchExpr
    still has no expr() case (a match nested mid-expression is not in the corpus).
  - Field export on a payload binding is keyed on the active arm's binding name +
    `sema.Enum.FieldSet[variant]`; the binding ident itself is rewritten by the
    `renames` map, the field by exported() in selectorExpr. Both armBinding/
    armFields are saved+restored per arm so nested matches stay clean.
  - When a value-position-match fixture is added, its .go.expected golden MUST be
    generated by the SPLICE engine (the default), because the US-003 transpile
    runner compares against it; the AST engine is judged only by build+vet
    (US-036) until US-042 regenerates exact goldens. Adding a file-mode transpile
    pair requires bumping internal/corpus/generate_test.go's count assertion.

## [2026-06-27T10:30:00Z] - US-040
- The AST backend now extracts `///` doctests and emits the `_test.go` sidecar,
  lowered through the SAME emit path as function bodies, so the 11-doctests cases
  pass the doctest tier through the new (AST) engine.
- Extraction is AST-native: emitDoctests reads the structured doctest nodes the
  parser attached in US-023 (ast.FuncDecl.Doc.Doctests, []*ast.Doctest{Input,
  Expected}) — NOT a re-lex of the source. renderDoctests rebuilds the same
  goal-shaped `TestDoctest_<fn>_<n>` sidecar shape as internal/pass.RenderDoctests
  (package clause + `import "testing"` + got/want/inequality per example), then
  emitDoctests parses that rendered source back to an *ast.File and runs it
  through emitFile with the ORIGINAL file's *sema.Info. Passing the source's info
  (not sema.Resolve(testFile), which would be empty of the source's enums) is the
  hinge: the emitter's variantLit/selectorExpr lower a construction by info.Enums
  membership keyed on name, so a doctest body's `Rejection.MountNotGranted(path:)`
  lowers to `Rejection(Rejection_MountNotGranted{Path:})` exactly as the body does.
- goBackend.Emit now also calls emitDoctests and sets pipeline.Output.Test;
  backend.Transpile already gofmt-formats a non-empty Output.Test.
- Files changed:
  - internal/backend/doctest.go (new: renderDoctests + emitDoctests)
  - internal/backend/backend.go (goBackend.Emit sets Output.Test)
  - internal/backend/backend_test.go (doctestCases; TestASTEngineDoctestTier;
    TestASTEngineDoctestExecTier; TestASTEngineDoctestEnumLowering)
  - prd.json (US-040 passes:true), progress.txt
  - history/20260627-feature-us-040-emit-doctest-sidecars-ast-backend/ (initiative)
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Doctest bodies lower for FREE through the existing emit path once you feed the
    rendered sidecar the ORIGINAL file's sema.Info — there is no separate doctest
    lowering. The splice path (pipeline.doctestFile) does the same thing by running
    the rendered goal test through the same passes + tables; the AST analogue is
    "parse rendered sidecar, emitFile with source info".
  - Output is byte-identical to the checked-in 11-doctests goldens (unlike most
    AST-engine stories, which diverge by gensym name): doctest bodies declare no
    generated temporaries, so the US-035 `v` vs `__goal_v` divergence never arises.
    So both corpus.RunDoctest (text-vs-golden) AND corpus.RunDoctestExec
    (behavioral) pass against the existing goldens — no golden regen needed here.
  - The AST already carries doctests structurally (US-023), so any future doctest
    consumer (US-045 goal fmt, LSP) should read ast.FuncDecl.Doc.Doctests rather
    than re-scanning `///` lines.

## [2026-06-27] - US-044
- Moved internal/fix (goal fix / idiomatize) off token re-lexing onto the parsed AST.
  fix.File now parses each fixed-point pass with parser.ParseFile and resolves facts
  with sema.Resolve, replacing scan.Lex + analyze.Build + analyze.FuncSpans/SigAt +
  scan.ScanFuncs. All four rules (result-sig, propagate, switch->match, call-site)
  detect candidates structurally over AST nodes; edits remain minimal scan.Replacement
  byte splices applied with scan.Splice, so untouched code/comments are byte-preserved.
- Files changed: internal/fix/{fix,resultsig,propagate,match,callsite}.go (rewritten);
  prd.json (US-044 passes:true); history/20260627-refactor-us-044-move-fix-onto-ast/*.
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - The parser strips // and /* comments, so any fix/fmt rule that must NOT drop a
    comment has to scan the raw source byte range (spanHasComment over token.Pos.Offset),
    not the AST. The AST cannot see comments. This is the key constraint for US-045 (goal
    fmt) too — comment fidelity needs raw-source / position-anchored handling.
  - To emit minimal, format-preserving edits from the AST, compute byte ranges from node
    Pos()/End() offsets and splice with scan.Replacement/scan.Splice (pure string utils,
    NOT lexing). Printing the AST would reflow everything; fix/fmt-idempotence tests
    compare exact bytes, so reflow would break them.
  - FuncType.Results is a *ast.FieldList with Opening/Closing paren positions: zero
    Opening == unparenthesized single result; >=2 all-unnamed fields ending in `error`
    == the (T,error) tuple. sema.FuncSig.Mode (ModeNone/ModeResult/ModeResultClosed/
    ModeOption) + .T give the propagation shape without any token scan.
  - The three meanings of Enum.Variant(x) are already distinct nodes, and a statement
    `return Result.Err(err)` is one CallExpr over a SelectorExpr — so propagation-vs-
    construction is told apart structurally (no skip-lists). `*o` deref is a StarExpr{X:Ident}.
  - To skip returns inside nested function literals, walk statements only and never
    descend into expressions (FuncLit is an expr) — closure returns become unreachable.
  - analyze.ZeroLit is a pure type->zero-literal helper (no lexing); reuse it with a
    typeDecls map built by walking File.Decls TypeSpecs instead of analyze.Build.

## [2026-06-29] - US-001 (self-host-phase-4 PRD)
- Fixed the gating iota const-block miscompile. `const ( Red Color = iota;
  Green; Blue )` silently transpiled (exit 0) to `Green Blue` — Green's spec
  greedily absorbed the bare `Blue` as its type, dropping Blue's iota value.
- Root cause: internal/parser/parser.go parseValueSpec consumed the next IDENT
  as the spec's type whenever startsType() held, with no spec-boundary signal
  (the lexer drops newlines). Fix: new onNewLine() helper (compares
  cur().Pos.Line to the previous token's line); parseValueSpec only takes an
  optional type when NOT onNewLine, so a bare continuation name on the next line
  parses as its own ValueSpec. Matches Go's newline=semicolon rule.
- Backend needed NO change: spec/genDecl emitters already render bare-name
  ValueSpecs correctly; the parser was producing 2 specs instead of 3.
- Files: internal/parser/parser.go (onNewLine + parseValueSpec guard);
  internal/parser/parser_test.go (TestParseIotaConstBlockBoundaries);
  internal/backend/backend_test.go (TestASTEngineEmitsIotaConstBlock);
  prd.json (US-001 passes:true); progress.txt. Initiative artifacts under
  history/20260629-bug-fix-iota-const-block-miscompile/.
- Verify: task check + task build green; transpiled iota enum compiles via
  go build; both new regression tests fail on the old collapse, pass after.
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Boundary reconstruction is the recurring parser hazard now that the lexer
    is newline-free. When a construct's meaning in Go depends on newline=
    semicolon, reach for token line numbers (onNewLine), not more lookahead.
  - This unblocks US-005 (port token): token kinds are an iota enum that hit
    exactly this bug.
---

## [2026-06-29] - US-002 (self-host-phase-4 PRD)
- Stood up the self-host transpile-and-build smoke gate: a new package
  internal/selfhost transpiles each in-scope compiler package through the goal
  front-end and `go build`s the generated Go in a throwaway temp module. This is
  the verification harness every later port story (US-005+) reuses.
- New: internal/selfhost/selfhost.go (InScope list; ReadPackage(dir) ->
  *project.Package from non-test *.go; BuildTranspiled(layout) transpiles +
  writes into a `module goal` temp module under each module-relative dir + runs
  `go build ./...`) and internal/selfhost/selfhost_test.go (positive gate over all
  8 packages + negative test proving a non-compiling transpile fails the gate).
- DEFECT FOUND BY THE GATE (the whole point): the PRD premise "the compiler
  source is already valid goal" was FALSE. goal reserves `match`, `enum`, `assert`
  beyond Go's keywords (implements/sealed/from/derive are contextual, NOT
  reserved). Four files used `enum` as a plain local identifier (valid Go, rejected
  by the goal parser): internal/sema/check.go, internal/sema/fields.go,
  internal/sema/question.go, internal/backend/emit.go. Renamed to enumDecl /
  enumIdent (behavior-preserving; error-message strings left untouched). After the
  renames all 8 packages transpile and build clean.
- Files: new internal/selfhost/{selfhost.go,selfhost_test.go}; edited
  internal/sema/{check,fields,question}.go, internal/backend/emit.go; prd.json
  (US-002 passes:true); progress.txt. Initiative artifacts under
  history/20260629-feature-us-002-per-package-transpile-build-smoke-gate/.
- Verify: `task check` and `task build` green; gate test ok.
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Only the EXACT words match/enum/assert are reserved; enumOf, enumName, Enums,
    .Enum are fine (the lexer takes the longest identifier). When porting/feeding a
    package through the front-end, grep for bare `\benum\b`/`\bmatch\b`/`\bassert\b`
    used as identifiers and rename them first.
  - backend.TranspilePackage stops at the FIRST file that fails to parse, so a
    package with several offending files surfaces them one build at a time. The
    gate's per-package error names the file; fix, re-run, repeat (or scan all files
    up front).
  - The 8 covered packages' non-test internal dependency closure is fully within
    the covered set, so a single temp module holding all transpiled output builds
    with no extra wiring (stdlib imports pass through). Reuse BuildTranspiled for
    US-005+; key the layout map by the module-relative dir (e.g. "internal/token").

  then `diff -r`). `task fixpoint` exits 0 (byte-identical) on the skeleton.
