  clean now also rms _bootstrap); .gitignore (/_bootstrap/). Initiative artifacts
  under history/20260629-feature-us-004-bootstrap-and-fixpoint-harness/.
- Verify: task bootstrap exit 0; task fixpoint exit 0 (FIXPOINT OK); task check
  and task build green; git status clean of bootstrap artifacts.
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - KEEP BOOTSTRAP ARTIFACTS UNDER A `_`-PREFIXED DIR. The Go toolchain ignores
    dirs whose names begin with `_` (or `.`) when expanding `./...`, so emitting
    to `_bootstrap/` keeps `go build ./...`/`go vet ./...`/`go test ./...` (i.e.
    `task check`/`task build`) green — but an explicit path like
    `go build ./_bootstrap/s1/selfhost` still builds. Verified empirically.
  - selfhost/ holds only .goal files, so it is invisible to the Go toolchain;
    only the goal front-end (project.Discover) sees it. No conflict with the Go
    package internal/selfhost (the US-002 smoke gate) despite the shared name.
  - The skeleton transpiles cleanly as plain Go-superset goal: strings.HasPrefix/
    TrimPrefix flag parsing and octal 0o755/0o644 literals all round-trip. No
    reserved-word (match/enum/assert) collisions.
  - Fixpoint reuse: as each US-005+ package is ported into selfhost/, `task
    fixpoint` already covers it (Discover walks the whole tree); no harness change
    needed per port.

  go.mod (`module goal`, `go 1.26`) into each emit dir (_bootstrap/s1, s2) and

  package-under-test (else the test's token != the package's token -> type error).

## [2026-06-29T05:30:00Z] - US-004 (self-host idiomatic PRD)
- Step 2 of 3 (autofix). Ran `goal fix --inplace` across all selfhost/*.goal to
  mechanically idiomatize (T,error)+manual `if err!=nil` propagation into
  Result/?. The run DOGFOODED `goal fix` on the goal-written compiler and exposed
  a real fixer miscompile: result-sig was converting functions whose call sites
  it could not (per-file) rewrite, producing non-compiling output. Three concrete
  cases in selfhost: `Discover` (exported; caller selfhost/main.goal:64
  `pkgs, err := project.Discover(root)` in another file), `Analyze` (exported),
  and `goListResolve` (unexported but tail-returned by DefaultResolver, which is
  exported + non-propagating so it stayed (string,error) while its body returned
  a Result).
- Fix landed in internal/fix/resultsig.go (the story's "fix the fixer here"
  clause). result-sig is now conservative about call-site safety, matching the
  package's stated philosophy (never emit incorrect code):
  - Split per-decl structural analysis into classifyResultSig (returns a
    *sigCand candidate or a near-miss *Report), keeping the exact bare-error /
    multi-value / non-propagating Skip messages.
  - fixResultSig now: collect candidates -> compute willResult + the safe
    call-site offset set (safeLocalPropagationCalls, mirroring fixPropagate's
    match: `v,err:=f(); if err!=nil{<propagation>}` adjacency inside a
    will-be-Result fn, recording the local-call Fun ident offset) -> for each
    candidate refuse if exported (Skip "exported `X` has callers fix cannot see")
    or if unsafeRefOffset finds any reference not in the safe set (Skip "`X` is
    called where `?` cannot apply"); else convert. Removed the old
    exported-Warn-and-convert branch.
- RESULT: zero selfhost source changes (every candidate is an unsafe
  cross-boundary conversion, now correctly refused). goal fix is idempotent on
  selfhost (second run writes nothing). The Result/? idiomatization of selfhost's
  exported APIs is deferred to the per-package audits US-005+, which coordinate
  cross-file callers.
- Files: internal/fix/resultsig.go; prd.json (US-004 passes:true); progress.txt.
  Initiative artifacts under history/20260629-refactor-us-004-autofix-selfhost/.
- Verify: go test ./internal/fix ./cmd/goal green (TestConvertTupleToResult,
  TestFixExportedWarning et al. preserved — the exported test still sees an
  "exported"+name report, now a Skip). task check (incl. corpus 15s + selfhost
  port gate 16s), task build, task fixpoint (FIXPOINT OK) all green.
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - `goal fix` will report a result-sig Skip for every fallible exported API and
    every function with a non-propagating caller. US-005..US-012 should treat
    those Skips as the worklist: convert the signature AND hand-edit the
    cross-file callers (`x, err := F()` -> `x := F()?` inside a Result fn, or
    `F().Unwrap()`/match at a non-Result boundary), then confirm `goal fix`
    reports none for the package.
  - When dogfooding a code-mod tool on its own compiler, run it on a SCRATCH COPY
    first (cp -r + fix --inplace + diff) to scope the blast radius before
    touching the tree — that is how the three miscompiles were found here.

## [2026-06-29T06:30:00Z] - US-005 (self-host idiomatic PRD)
- Step 3 of 3 (idiomatic audit), first package: selfhost/token. Audit outcome is
  a recorded DECISION, not a source change — selfhost/token/token.goal already
  satisfies every behavioral AC and has no idiom that fits a rewrite.
- enum decision (AC-1): refused rewriting `type Kind int` + iota const block into
  a goal `enum`. A goal enum lowers to a sealed interface + per-variant struct +
  marker (boxed, unordered) — it cannot serve Kind's three load-bearing integer
  uses: array indexing (kindNames[k]), range predicates (literalBeg < k &&
  k < literalEnd via the *_beg/*_end sentinels), and numeric iteration in init().
  Forcing an enum would also change Kind's representation off `int`, breaking the
  public API (type Kind int; Lookup(...)(Kind,bool)) that the US-003 verbatim
  oracle tests run against unchanged. Recorded in DECISIONS.md under "self-host
  idiomatic audit — US-005 (token)".
- No switch->match (token.goal has no switch, only the "switch" spelling string).
  No Result/? conversions: package is import-free with no (T,error) function;
  the lone multi-value helper Lookup is comma-ok (Kind,bool), pinned by the
  oracle test, and refused for Option conversion (not a goal-fix site; would
  break the test). `goal fix selfhost/token/token.goal` => no diff, no report
  (AC-2 already held).
- Files: DECISIONS.md (new audit section), prd.json (US-005 passes:true),
  progress.txt. Initiative artifacts under
  history/20260629-refactor-us-005-idiomatic-audit-token/. No .goal source edit.
- Verify: goal fix (no diff/report); task check (incl. internal/selfhost port
  gate + internal/token) green; task build green; task fixpoint FIXPOINT OK
  (selfhost/token/token.go byte-identical across goal-c-1/goal-c-2).
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Establishes the per-package audit pattern (see new Codebase Patterns bullet):
    classify each Go-ism (const-iota / switch / fallible helper) against the goal
    idiom it could become, convert where it FITS, and record refusals in
    DECISIONS.md. A go/token-style ordered integer enum is the canonical "keep as
    iota" case.
  - For a package the US-003 oracle pins, never change a public signature even to
    a nicer idiom (Option/Result) unless the cross-file callers AND the reused
    test are updated together — token's reused test forbids touching Lookup.

## [2026-06-29T07:30:00Z] - US-006 (self-host idiomatic PRD)
- Step 3 of 3 (idiomatic audit), second package: selfhost/lexer. Audit outcome
  is a recorded DECISION, not a source change — selfhost/lexer/lexer.goal
  already satisfies every behavioral AC and has no idiom that fits a rewrite.
  Mirrors US-005 (token).
- switch->match (AC-1): refused. The lexer declares NO in-file enum, and AC-1
  scopes the conversion to "switch over an in-file enum". Every switch in the
  lexer is over a non-enum value: Next() is an expression-less switch over
  boolean predicates (ch==eof / isLetter / isDigit / quote...); scanOperator
  and its nested switches (+ - & | < > = and op2) switch over l.ch/ch, a `rune`
  (primitive int) with individual char-literal arms. Per DECISIONS §02-match
  §228 plain switch is legal on non-enum types and match is reserved for closed
  enums — so these stay switch. (token.Kind is `type Kind int`, not an enum per
  US-005, so even a Kind switch would not be an enum switch.)
- Result/Option/? (AC-1): none apply. The lexer is a TOTAL tokenizer — no
  function returns error; it signals lexical problems in-band by emitting
  token.ILLEGAL (scanOperator default), so there is no `if err!=nil`
  propagation for goal fix to idiomatize. Multi-value uses are not error sites:
  token.Lookup is comma-ok (Kind,bool), pinned by the oracle (kept comma-ok per
  US-005); utf8.DecodeRuneInString returns (rune,int) size not error.
- Machine check (AC-2): `goal fix selfhost/lexer/lexer.goal` => no stdout diff
  vs source, empty stderr (no remaining auto-convertible propagation sites).
- Files: DECISIONS.md (new "US-006 (lexer)" audit section), prd.json (US-006
  passes:true), progress.txt. Initiative artifacts under
  history/20260629-refactor-us-006-idiomatic-audit-lexer/. No .goal source edit.
- Verify: goal fix (no diff/report); task check green (incl. internal/selfhost
  port gate + internal/lexer); task build green; task fixpoint FIXPOINT OK
  (byte-identical across goal-c-1/goal-c-2).
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - A pure-producer/consumer package with NO error-returning function (signals
    via an in-band sentinel like ILLEGAL) has zero Result/? audit surface — the
    audit is a documented decision, same shape as token. Expect this for other
    infallible leaf packages.
  - "switch over an enum" means an in-file goal `enum`; switches over `rune`,
    `int`, or boolean conditions are NOT match candidates (§02-match §228).
    Confirm there is an actual enum declaration before planning switch->match.
---

## [2026-06-29T08:30:00Z] - US-007 (self-host idiomatic PRD)
- Step 3 of 3 (idiomatic audit), third and highest-opportunity package:
  selfhost/ast (ast.goal, goal_decl/expr/stmt.goal, walk.goal). Outcome is a
  recorded DECISION, not a source change — every idiomatic candidate's only
  behavior-preserving form lies OUTSIDE selfhost/ast, so converting would break
  the US-003 verbatim self-host oracle and/or ripple beyond this story's scope.
  Mirrors US-005 (token) / US-006 (lexer).
- Category interfaces Node/Decl/Stmt/Expr/Spec -> sealed interface: REFUSED.
  (a) A goal sealed interface lowers via §8.1 (synthesized isNAME() marker +
  per-type `implements NAME for T`), changing the go/ast-mirrored public API the
  oracle pins. (b) Per §9 switch-coexistence, a plain switch on a closed
  enum/sealed value is a sema COMPILE ERROR — and selfhost/{sema,backend,parser}
  dispatch on these interfaces with dozens of plain `switch x.(type)`
  type-switches, so sealing them would force a tree-wide switch->match
  conversion that is explicitly OUTSIDE US-007 (scoped to selfhost/ast only).
- Walk's `switch node.(type)` -> match: REFUSED. match needs a closed
  enum/sealed scrutinee (§228); since Node must stay a plain interface (above),
  its match form has no legal scrutinee. The traversal is behavior-identical as
  a plain switch.
- FuncMod / ChanDir (`type X int` + iota) -> enum: REFUSED. Both public,
  oracle-pinned, ORDERED integer enums consumed cross-package by ==/!= (sema:
  question/convert/resolve) and plain switch (backend/emit; sema/resolve for
  Dir). A goal enum is a boxed sealed interface, not an int, so == breaks and
  the plain switches become §9 compile errors — all out of scope. Same canonical
  "ordered/comparable iota int, keep as-is" case as token.Kind (US-005).
- No Result/Option/?: NONE APPLY. selfhost/ast is pure AST data + the total Walk
  traversal; it declares no error-returning function (the lone "error" is a word
  in a doc comment). `goal fix selfhost/ast/*.goal` => no diff, no report across
  all five files (AC-2 already holds).
- Files: DECISIONS.md (new "US-007 (ast)" section), prd.json (US-007
  passes:true), progress.txt. Initiative artifacts under
  history/20260629-refactor-us-007-idiomatic-audit-ast/. No .goal source edit.
- Verify: goal fix (no diff/report); task check green (incl. internal/selfhost
  port gate + internal/ast); task build green; task fixpoint FIXPOINT OK
  (byte-identical goal-c-1/goal-c-2).
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - The §9 switch-coexistence rule is the dominant blocker for sealing AST
    category interfaces: any package whose closed-type values are consumed by
    plain `switch`/type-switch in OTHER packages cannot be sealed without a
    coordinated cross-package switch->match conversion. A single-package audit
    story (US-008..US-012) should NOT seal a type whose consumers it may not
    edit. The whole-tree US-013 sweep is where such cross-package conversions,
    if ever wanted, would belong.
  - go/ast-style ordered iota ints used as modifiers/directions (FuncMod,
    ChanDir) are the same "keep as iota" case as token.Kind: equality/plain-
    switch consumption + int representation make the boxed enum encoding a
    behavior break, independent of array-indexing/range-predicate uses.

## [2026-06-29T09:30:00Z] - US-008 (self-host idiomatic PRD)
- Step 3 of 3 (idiomatic audit), fourth package: selfhost/parser (parser.goal,
  goal_construct/decl/match/stmt.goal). The story names Result/? as the headline
  idiom; this audit went looking specifically for that intra-package surface and
  it genuinely does NOT exist, so the outcome is a recorded DECISION with no
  .goal source change. Mirrors US-005 (token) / US-006 (lexer) / US-007 (ast).
- Result/? (AC-1): REFUSED with reason. The parser uses an error-ACCUMULATOR
  design, not (T,error) propagation: `parser.errs []error` appended by the void
  recorder `errorf`; every internal helper returns a bare ast node/nil and never
  error; the lone (T,error) function is the exported, oracle-pinned
  ParseFile(src)(*ast.File,error) which joins p.errs at the end. Grep of all 5
  files for `func .*error` => only ParseFile + errorf; grep `err != nil`/`, err`
  => only ParseFile's errors.Join. So there is NO `if err!=nil` propagation site
  to convert, and ParseFile is forbidden to change (US-003 oracle pins its
  signature; parser_test.go calls it). goal fix result-sig SKIPs ParseFile, i.e.
  it is not an auto-convertible site -> AC-2 holds (zero auto-convertible sites).
- switch->match (AC-1): REFUSED. selfhost/parser declares no in-file `enum`. All
  switches are over non-enum scrutinees: token.Kind (`type Kind int`, not an enum
  per US-005), type-switches over ast category interfaces (can't seal per US-007
  §9), and boolean `switch {}`. No closed-enum scrutinee => no match candidate.
- Option (predicates): N/A. The bool helpers (at/onNewLine/startsType/
  atTypeParams/nameThenType/isTypeSwitchGuard/startsExpr/...) are pure predicates,
  not comma-ok fallible lookups.
- Machine check (AC-2): `goal fix selfhost/parser/*.goal` => no content diff on
  any file; only stderr is the ParseFile result-sig SKIP (non-auto-convertible).
- Files: DECISIONS.md (new "US-008 (parser)" section), prd.json (US-008
  passes:true), progress.txt. Initiative artifacts under
  history/20260629-refactor-us-008-idiomatic-audit-parser/. No .goal source edit.
- Verify: goal fix (no diff; only the deliberate ParseFile skip); task check green
  (incl. internal/selfhost port gate + internal/parser); task build green; task
  fixpoint FIXPOINT OK (selfhost/parser/*.go byte-identical goal-c-1/goal-c-2).
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - See the new Codebase Patterns bullet: an error-accumulator parser has zero
    intra-package Result/? surface. The "Result/? is the headline idiom" note in
    a story is an EXPECTATION to test against the source, not a guarantee the
    surface exists — verify the package's error strategy first.
  - sema (US-009) is the next audit: it DOES have real (T,error)/Result surface
    per the US-004 result-sig skips; expect genuine conversions there, unlike the
    leaf packages token/lexer/ast/parser which all bottomed out at documented
    refusals.

## [2026-06-29T10:30:00Z] - US-009 (self-host idiomatic PRD)
- Step 3 of 3 (idiomatic audit), fifth package: selfhost/sema (12 files). sema is
  the FIRST ported package with a genuine fallible (T,error)/Result surface (per
  the US-004 result-sig skips + the US-008 carry-forward note). Unlike the leaf
  packages (token/lexer/ast/parser, all pure refusals), this audit makes ONE
  genuine behavior-preserving Result/? conversion and refuses the rest with reason.
- CONVERTED sema.Analyze: `([]Diagnostic, error)` -> `Result[[]Diagnostic, error]`,
  propagating the parse step with `parser.ParseFile(src)?` and returning success
  via `return Result.Ok(Check(file, info))`. This is the ONLY fitting site: Analyze
  has a real (T,error) propagation site AND zero consumers anywhere in selfhost AND
  zero oracle tests (no analyze_test in the sema behavioral gate), so the
  conversion needs no caller/test edits. Open-E Result lowers to native (T,error),
  so the emitted Go is byte-identical (`func Analyze(src string) (ok []Diagnostic,
  err error) { file, err := parser.ParseFile(src); if err != nil { return ok, err }
  ...; return Check(file, info), nil }`) — same public signature, fixpoint stays
  byte-identical. This is the first Result/? in selfhost EXECUTABLE source.
- REFUSED (recorded in DECISIONS.md "US-009 (sema)"): EnrichForeign ([]error
  accumulator), DefaultResolver (DirResolver-type + oracle-pinned), foreignDecls
  (4-value + accumulator caller), goListResolve (tail-return at exported boundary),
  AnalyzePackageInDir/With (exported + oracle-pinned + 3-value); constIntLit/
  moduleResolve/readModulePath (comma-ok control-flow bool, err swallowed);
  Mode/Severity (exported ordered iota ints, consumed cross-package by == and
  sema.Mode/sema.Severity(x) conversions in backend/typecheck/lsp); no switch->match
  (no in-file enum; Diagnostic.Code/Feature are strings).
- Machine check (AC-2): `goal fix selfhost/sema/*.goal` -> no source diff on any
  file (Analyze no longer appears in the report now that it is Result-returning);
  remaining stderr is only the documented non-auto-convertible skips + advisory
  call-site suggestions. Zero auto-convertible sites remain.
- Files: selfhost/sema/analyze.goal (Analyze -> Result/?), DECISIONS.md (US-009
  section), prd.json (US-009 passes:true), progress.txt. Initiative artifacts under
  history/20260629-refactor-us-009-idiomatic-audit-sema/.

  green (incl. selfhost port gate + internal/sema); task build green; task fixpoint
  FIXPOINT OK (selfhost/sema/*.go byte-identical across goal-c-1/goal-c-2).
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - See the two new Codebase Patterns bullets: (1) an open-E (T,error)->Result/?
    conversion is byte-identical at the emit boundary, so it is SAFE even on an
    exported selfhost function with no in-tree callers and no oracle test; (2) a
    comma-ok (T,bool) helper that swallows err to a control-flow bool is NOT a
    Result/Option/? site, and a `goal fix` `suggestion` (vs `skipped`) does not

## [2026-06-29T13:30:00Z] - US-012 (self-host idiomatic PRD)
- Step 3 of 3 (idiomatic audit), EIGHTH and FINAL package: selfhost/typecheck
  (772 LOC: checker/typecheck/implements/mustuse/nozero.goal). Outcome: a
  DOCUMENTED REFUSAL (no .goal source change), mirroring the pure-refusal packages
  (token/lexer/ast/parser US-005..US-008, project/pipeline US-010) rather than the
  conversion audits (sema US-009, backend US-011).
- Package survey: the ONLY two error-returning functions are (1) exported `Load`
  (typecheck.goal) and (2) the `TypeChecker`-interface method `GoTypesChecker.Check`
  (checker.goal). EVERY depth check (CheckImplements/CheckMustUse/CheckNoZeroValue)
  returns []Diagnostic with NO error — zero fallible surface. Helper predicates are
  bool / comma-ok (mustUseFieldKind, litClassOf, litFieldKeys) — not `?` sites.
- REFUSALS (all recorded in DECISIONS.md "US-012 (typecheck)"):
  - `Load` stays (*Package, error): all internal propagation WRAPS context
    (fmt.Errorf "%w") so `?` (propagates UNCHANGED) is a behavior change; its
    callees (backend.TranspilePackage, parser.ParseFile) are Go-tuples not Result
    so nothing to `?`; exported + oracle-pinned (6 `p,err:=Load(...)` test sites) +
    in-tree caller Check, so the US-009 byte-identical-emit trick (no callers AND no
    oracle test) does NOT apply. goal fix agrees: `skipped: [result-sig]`.
  - `Check` stays ([]Diagnostic, error): TypeChecker interface method (pinned by
    `var _ TypeChecker = GoTypesChecker{}` + tc.Check two-value calls); its lone
    `return nil, err` is PURE but the emitter requires a `?`-host to be Result, and
    making Check Result breaks the interface contract. goal fix emits only an
    advisory `suggestion` (not a skip, not a diff).
  - `litClass` stays type int + iota: no switch over it (the only switch is a TYPE
    switch over go/ast nodes); consumed via `== classGeneric` + numeric `return 0` —
    enum lowers to a sealed interface with no int identity, breaking both.
- Files changed: DECISIONS.md (refusal section), prd.json (passes:true),
  progress.txt. NO selfhost/typecheck/*.goal change.
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - A go/types-style depth-checker harness concentrates ALL fallibility in its
    exported Load entry + the swappable checker interface method; the actual checks
    are pure []Diagnostic producers. So such a package has ~zero intra-package `?`
    surface by construction — expect a refusal, like the parser accumulator (US-008).
  - Machine check for a refusal package: `goal fix <pkg>/*.goal` must produce no
    diff; a `skipped: [result-sig]` (refused) and a `suggestion: [call-site]`
    (advisory) both satisfy AC-2 because neither is an auto-conversion.
  - US-012 done leaves only US-013 (final whole-tree sweep + self-host proof).

## 2026-06-29T14:31:30Z - SEAM-001
- Established the seam methodology + equivalence oracle for the SEAM PRD: added a
  "## Seam methodology" section to DECISIONS.md defining the RELAXED gate for
  cross-package idiom changes (SEAM-002..006) that may alter emitted Go.
- Documentation + procedure only; no source idiom change.
- Files changed: DECISIONS.md (new section), prd.json (SEAM-001 passes:true;
  note: prd.json was already swapped from the per-package US-001..013 PRD to the
  SEAM PRD in the working tree), progress.txt, and the morse-code initiative dir
  history/20260629-feature-seam-001-seam-methodology-and-equivalence-oracle/.
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - The relaxed gate's keystone: `task fixpoint` proves goal-c-1==goal-c-2
    (stage1==stage2 self-consistency), NOT output==before — so a seam edit may
    change emitted Go and still be FIXPOINT OK. The per-package audits leaned on
    fixpoint as if it pinned output; it only ever pinned self-consistency.
  - Golden regen mechanisms for later seams: corpus exact goldens via
    `go test ./internal/corpus -run TestUpdateGoldens -update-goldens`; parser AST
    snapshots via `go test ./internal/parser -update-snapshots`; go/ast-mirror
    unit tests in internal/ast are hand-updated (no flag) and are the US-003 oracle
    tension SEAM-004 must confront.
  - EXPECTED-to-change tests under a seam: go/ast-mirror units + golden
    transpile-shape fixtures. MUST-stay-green: task fixpoint, corpus behavioral
    tier, full task check after golden regen.
  - morse-code automode: human-review gates ("user-approval") pause on the first
    `workflow next`; running `workflow next` again clears the gate and advances.
    Each `next` also pre-fetches the NEXT step's skill, so write a step's artifact
    BEFORE advancing (it transitions you into the following step's audit).

  self-host mirror in selfhost/):
  1. matchQualifier (lower.go / lower.goal): handle a package-qualified variant
     pattern whose `vp.Enum` is an *ast.SelectorExpr (`pkg.Enum`), returning the
     qualified string `"pkg.Enum"`. The existing case-label builder
     (`enumName + "_" + Variant`) then yields the correct `pkg.Enum_Variant`
     reference to the imported variant struct — no emit.go change needed.
  2. EnrichForeign (foreign.go / foreign.goal): reconstruct foreign enums from an
     imported package's generated §8.1 encoding (a marker interface
     `type X interface{ isX() }` + variant structs `X_<V>`) and fold them into
     info.Enums keyed `alias.Enum`. enumOf then resolves imported enums from the
     merged cross-package sema.Info, generalizing beyond the Result/Option
     special-casing. New helpers: markerEnumName, reconstructForeignEnums;

  - internal/ is the LIVE transpiler (corpus + unit tier); selfhost/ is the .goal
    mirror for `task fixpoint`. A backend capability must be implemented in BOTH:
    internal so the corpus behavioral fixture exercises it, selfhost so the
    self-hosted compiler has it and fixpoint stays green (selfhost source need not
    yet USE it — it only must remain valid goal that both stages emit identically).
  - Cross-package enum resolution lives in PACKAGE mode only: single-file
    backend.Transpile uses sema.Resolve (no foreign enrichment), so a cross-package

  identity: kindNames[k] indexing, literalBeg<k<literalEnd range arithmetic,

  selfhost/parser/parser.goal (qualified construction `ast.FuncMod.FuncFrom`/
  `ast.ChanDir.SendRecv` + zero-value fix `&ast.FuncDecl{Mod: ast.FuncMod.FuncPlain}`),
  selfhost/sema/{question.goal,resolve.goal,convert.goal} (==/!=/switch -> match),
  selfhost/backend/emit.goal (funcDecl control switch -> isDerive bool match; chanType

  behavioral gate), task build clean, task fixpoint = FIXPOINT OK (stage1==stage2 on
  the new enum/match source). Verified the bootstrap output lowers to the real forms:
  `type FuncMod interface{ isFuncMod() }` + `FuncMod_*` structs; matches -> cross-pkg
  Go type-switches (`case ast.ChanDir_RecvOnly:`); construction ->
  `ast.ChanDir(ast.ChanDir_SendRecv{})`.
- Learnings for future iterations (carry into SEAM-003/004):
  - ENUM ZERO VALUE IS nil, not the first variant. iota silently gave a meaningful
    zero (FuncPlain=0, SendRecv=0); an enum does not. Audit every constructor of a
    struct holding the (soon-to-be) enum field and set it explicitly, or a later
    `match` faults at run time on nil. Here: parseFuncDecl needed `Mod:
    ast.FuncMod.FuncPlain`; ChanType already set Dir. fixpoint + behavioral port
    gates catch a missed one, but find them up front by grepping `&ast.<Type>{`.
  - == / != / plain-switch over the enum all become `match`. For a `!=`/`==` used
    inside a boolean (`!ok || x.Mod != V || ...`), bind a bool via value-position
    `match` and SPLIT the `!ok` type-assert guard out FIRST — hoisting the match
    above `!ok` nil-derefs the failed assertion.
  - A control-flow switch with a no-op/grouped arm (e.g. `case FuncPlain, FuncFrom:`
    no-op; `case FuncDerive: …; return`) is cleanest as `isX := match {…}` + `if isX`
    rather than a statement `match` with an empty `{}` arm.
  - internal/ast (the bootstrap Go compiler's own AST) stays Go-iota; it need not
    mirror selfhost's enum repr and is not in the fixpoint diff. Only the SHARED
    oracle test conflicts: a port-gated internal test that references the iota
    constants won't compile against the enum-transpiled selfhost pkg. Resolution =
    relocate those assertions to a NEW internal-only `_test.go` (kept OUT of
    internal/selfhost/port_test.go's BuildAndTest slice) so the port-gated file is
    symbol-free. collect/assertChildren in ast_test.go are function-LOCAL closures —
    re-create them in the new file, don't reference them.
  - No golden regeneration was needed: corpus exact-tier goldens + parser snapshots
    test the UNCHANGED internal/ Go compiler, not selfhost/. The selfhost tree is
    proven only by the port gates + fixpoint. (A SEAM that edits internal/ too would
    move goldens; a selfhost-only idiom conversion does not.)

## 2026-06-29T20:30:00Z - SEAM-003
- Converted selfhost/sema Mode (ModeNone/ModeResult/ModeResultClosed/ModeOption) and
  Severity (Error/Warning) from `type X int` + iota to goal `enum`s, and converted every
  cross- and same-package consumer to `match` in one atomic change. Total conversion — no
  member kept as iota (neither type has numeric identity; the US-011-claimed
  `sema.Severity(x)` numeric conversions DID NOT actually exist in the tree).
- Files: selfhost/sema/{sema,check}.goal (enum defs; Severity.String() method -> free
  `SeverityLabel` func), selfhost/sema/{resolve,question,mustuse,analyze,foreign}.goal
  (Mode match + Severity == match + zero-value fixes), selfhost/sema/{implements,convert,
  fields,assert}.goal (Severity literal requalification), selfhost/backend/{lower,emit}.goal
  (needsResultPrelude/closedResultTE/unwrapClosed/resultMatch guards + calleeMode + FuncSig
  construction), selfhost/typecheck/{mustuse,implements,nozero}.goal. internal/sema/check.go
  (mirrored SeverityLabel) + internal/sema/mode_test.go (new) + rewritten shared tests +
  DECISIONS.md + prd.json + progress.txt.
- Gates: task check green, task build clean, task fixpoint = FIXPOINT OK (stage1==stage2 on
  the new enum/match source). No golden regen needed (goldens test internal/ Go compiler).
- Learnings for future iterations (carry into SEAM-004/005):
  - A goal enum cannot carry a METHOD: `enum X` lowers to a sealed interface `type X
    interface{ isX() }`, and Go forbids declaring a method on an interface type
    (`invalid receiver type X (pointer or interface type)`). Convert any `(x X) String()`
    (or other method) to a FREE function `XLabel(x X)`; update `%s`/Stringer call sites to
    call it explicitly. This bites Severity (rendered via %s in analyze.Render and
    typecheck Diagnostic.String).
  - Value-position `match` rules in the bootstrap backend: it lowers `:=`/`var x T = match`
    and `return match`, but NOT a bare `field = match`/`x = match` assignment
    (`unsupported expression *ast.MatchExpr`). And `:=` inference only fires when ALL arms
    are one enum, string, or bool LITERAL; an arm whose value is a variable (e.g.
    `=> sig.Arity`) forces `var name T = match ...`. So: assign matches to a NEW `:=` temp
    (or annotate `var`), then assign the temp to the field.
  - Empty match arms are still the anti-pattern: a control switch with a no-op variant arm
    (ModeNone) can't be `=> {}`. Either precompute bools and keep a switch-true with an
    empty `case` body (legal in Go), or split into per-output value matches where the no-op
    variant maps to the already-computed value (`Mode.ModeNone => sig.Arity`).
  - nil-safe matching: when a value may be the enum ZERO (nil) — a `csig`/`sig` returned
    with `!known`/`!ok`, or a map miss — match with an explicit `_` rest-arm (lowers to a
    real Go `default`, no panic) instead of full enumeration (lowers to a panicking
    default). Keep the `!ok`/`!known` short-circuit in the surrounding `if`. For
    always-set values use full enumeration (exhaustiveness).
  - Enum zero is nil: audit EVERY constructor whose struct holds the enum field. The
    silent killer here was sema/foreign.goal building foreign FuncSigs without Mode (they
    land in info.FuncSignatures, which backend needsResultPrelude matches over) and
    backend calleeMode returning a map-miss zero FuncSig's nil Mode. Set Mode.ModeNone
    explicitly at both.
  - Port-gate shared-test conflict (bigger than SEAM-002's): internal/{sema,typecheck}
    white-box tests reference the bare iota constants AND are reused by the self-host port
    gate against the enum-transpiled selfhost pkgs (no bare constants there). Two fixes by
    whether the type has a production string form: (a) Severity — add a mirrored
    `SeverityLabel` to internal/sema and rewrite shared `x.Severity != Error` to
    `SeverityLabel(x.Severity) != "error"` (compiles against BOTH, full coverage, no
    relocation); (b) Mode (no string form) — relocate the assertions to a new internal-only
    `_test.go` kept OUT of port_test.go's BuildAndTest slice (reuse the same-package
    `mustResolve`/`repr` helpers), leaving the shared file symbol-free.

## 2026-06-29T22:30:00Z - SEAM-005
- Lifted the scope-blocked half of the fallible exported/interface API to goal
  Result/? in selfhost/, and honestly KEPT the semantics-blocked half (documented).
- CONVERTED (selfhost/ only; reverses US-008..US-012 SCOPE refusals):
  - typecheck.Load (*Package,error) -> Result[*Package,error]. Wrapping guards
    (fmt.Errorf %w) can't `?` (would drop the wrap), so each stays statement-form
    `return Result.Err(fmt.Errorf(...))`; final `return Result.Ok(p)`.
  - typecheck TypeChecker.Check interface + GoTypesChecker.Check ->
    Result[[]Diagnostic,error]; body `p := Load(pkg)?` (the real idiom gain) +
    `return Result.Ok(diags)`. Interface method + impl lifted in LOCKSTEP.
  - sema.AnalyzePackageInDir ([][]Diagnostic,error) -> Result[[][]Diagnostic,error];
    explicit unpack of the 3-value ...With, then Result.Ok/Result.Err.
- KEPT as documented SEMANTIC non-fits (not scope): parser.ParseFile (partial-AST-
  on-error value+error, load-bearing for project.PackageClause + pipeline.declSites),
  EnrichForeign ([]error accumulator), AnalyzePackageInDirWith (3-value),
  foreignDecls/goalForeignDecls (4-value), moduleResolve/readModulePath/constIntLit
  (comma-ok). See DECISIONS.md "SEAM-005".
- Files: selfhost/sema/package.goal, selfhost/typecheck/{typecheck,checker}.goal,
  DECISIONS.md, prd.json, progress.txt, history/20260629-refactor-seam-005-*.
- Gates: task check green (incl. internal/selfhost port gate transpiling
  selfhost/{typecheck,sema} + running the UNCHANGED oracle tests against the lowered
  Go, plus corpus behavioral tier), task build clean, task fixpoint = FIXPOINT OK.
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Open-E Result lowers to native (T,error); an INTERFACE METHOD returning Result
    lowers to a (T,error) method (verified: `Check(pkg) (ok []Diagnostic, err error)`).
    So a SEAM Result conversion of an exported/interface fn is BYTE-IDENTICAL at the
    emit boundary -> the Go bootstrap mirror (internal/*.go) needs NO edit (Go can't
    express Result and already IS the lowered form), and the port-gated Go oracle
    tests (two-value `v,err:=`, `var _ I = T{}`) stay green against BOTH compilers
    unchanged. The seam stays swappable with zero test churn. This dissolves the
    US-012 "oracle-pinned, out of scope" objection entirely.
  - Converting a callee to Result is the ENABLER for `?` in its caller: Check's pure
    propagation `p,err:=Load(pkg); if err!=nil {return nil,err}` only becomes the
    idiomatic `Load(pkg)?` once Load returns Result AND Check returns Result. Lift
    callee+caller (and the interface contract) together in one atomic change.
  - WRAPPING propagation stays statement-form even inside a Result host: `?`
    propagates the error UNCHANGED, so a `fmt.Errorf("ctx: %w", err)` guard must be
    `if err != nil { return Result.Err(fmt.Errorf(...)) }`, not `?`. A Result host
    happily contains plain `v, err := goCallee()` 2-value assignments + Result.Err
    returns; the callee need not be Result.
  - HONESTY: a function that returns a value AND an error SIMULTANEOUSLY meaningfully
    (parser.ParseFile: a non-nil PARTIAL AST + joined errors, consumed partial-on-
    error by tolerant callers) is a genuine SEMANTIC non-fit for Result (Err carries
    no value) -- same class as multi-value/comma-ok, NOT a cross-package scope block.
    Carve it out and document; do not fake the conversion. Grep callers for
    `f, _ := Fn(` / partial-use-after-error before assuming a (T,error) fn is pure.

## 2026-06-29T18:28:00Z - SEAM-CAP-3a
- Sealed interfaces now preserve their declared method signatures in emitted Go.
  Previously sealedInterfaceDecl discarded the parsed body and emitted only the
  marker (`type Name interface{ isName() }`), so a method-bearing sealed interface
  (e.g. ast.Node with Pos()/End()) lost its methods — blocking sealing Node.
- Fix: sealedInterfaceDecl emits declared methods + the isName() marker when the
  body is non-empty; keeps the compact marker-only form (via genSealedInterface)
  when empty so emitted Go stays byte-identical (fixpoint-safe). Interface-method
  rendering extracted into a shared emitter helper `interfaceMethod(*ast.Field)`
  reused by both interfaceType and sealedInterfaceDecl.
- Files: internal/backend/emit.go, selfhost/backend/emit.goal (line-for-line
  mirror), internal/backend/sealed_methods_test.go (new regression test).
  lower.go/lower.goal genSealedInterface kept unchanged (empty-body path).
- Gates: task check, task build, task fixpoint (FIXPOINT OK) all green; corpus
  behavioral tier unchanged. Commit d79ebee.
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - selfhost/backend/emit.goal mirrors internal/backend/emit.go line-for-line
    (interfaceType/funcSig/identList/field are identical) — when extracting a new
    emitter helper in one, add the SAME helper to the other or the selfhost port
    test fails with "e.<helper> undefined" (the .goal is real Go compiled by the
    port gate). The PostToolUse task-check hook catches this immediately.
  - Keeping the pre-existing compact output for the no-op/empty case is the
    cheapest way to protect `task fixpoint` byte-identity when touching emit/lower.
  - To prove an interface method is "callable through the interface", transpile to
    a temp `module goal` and `go test` a file that assigns the implementor to an
    interface-typed var and calls the method — if the signature were dropped the
    test fails to COMPILE, not silently pass (pattern from crosspkg_goal_enum_test).

## 2026-06-29T19:30:00Z - SEAM-CAP-3b
- Implemented type-pattern `match` over a same-package SEALED INTERFACE (CAP-3 part
  2 of 3): `match n { *Lit(l) => …; *Neg(g) => … }` now lowers to a Go type-switch
  with concrete `case *T:` labels — the feature that lets `switch x := n.(type)`
  become an exhaustive `match`. Same-package only; cross-package is CAP-3c.
- Four gaps closed, mirrored line-for-line in BOTH internal/ (Go) and selfhost/
  (.goal, compiled by the port gate):
  1. Implementor registry: sema.Info gains `SealedImpls map[string][]string`
     (iface → implementor `*T` set), built in resolve.go resolveTypeDecl from
     `StructType.Implements`, unioned+deduped in Info.Merge. KEPT `Sealed
     map[string]bool` separate (NOT folded into the registry) — `implements` also
     targets ordinary interfaces verified by CheckImplements via `Sealed[iface]`;
     conflating would skip that feature-07 check (corpus regression). SealedImpls is
     consulted only for keys also in Sealed.
  2. Parser: new `ast.TypePattern` node (distinct from Variant/RestPattern);
     parsePattern routes `*`-leading arms to parseTypePattern (`*T`/`*T(x)`). New
     parser field `armBody` stops a value-position arm body's binary expr at a
     newline-leading operator (Go ASI never starts a continuation with an infix op),
     so `body \n *T` is the next arm, not `body * T`.
  3. Backend: new sealedMatch/emitSealedArm (lower.go isSealedMatch; emit.go),
     DISTINCT from enumMatch — emits `switch [v :=] subj.(type)` + `case *T:` per
     arm, `_`→default else panicking default; binding renamed to the guard.
     Dispatched from matchStmt/returnStmt/tryVarMatch/tryAssignMatch/matchValue.
  4. Sema: checkOneSealedMatch enforces full-implementor coverage or `_`, else
     `non-exhaustive-match` Error; unresolvable sealed type defers with a new
     `unresolved-match-sealed` Warning (added to guide catalog + AI-KNOWLEDGE golden).
- Files: internal/{ast/goal_expr.go,ast/walk.go,ast/ast_test.go,parser/goal_match.go,
  parser/parser.go,sema/sema.go,sema/resolve.go,sema/check.go,backend/lower.go,
  backend/emit.go,guide/catalog.go} + selfhost mirrors (ast/{goal_expr,walk}.goal,
  parser/{goal_match,parser}.goal, sema/{sema,resolve,check}.goal,
  backend/{lower,emit}.goal); new tests internal/backend/sealed_match_test.go +
  internal/sema/sealed_match_test.go; AI-KNOWLEDGE-BOOTSTRAP.md, DECISIONS.md,
  prd.json. Initiative: history/20260629-feature-seam-cap-3b-sealed-interface-match/.
- Gates: task check green; task build green; task fixpoint FIXPOINT OK (stage1==stage2
  on the new parser/sema/backend source); corpus behavioral tier unchanged (additive).
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Type patterns introduce ONE grammar ambiguity: a value-position arm body
    followed by a newline-leading `*T` parses as multiplication. The general fix is
    Go ASI (a binary operator never begins a line); gating parseBinary on
    `armBody && onNewLine()` is the targeted, fixpoint-safe form. Any new pattern
    whose lead token is also a binary operator (`*`,`-`,`+`,`&`,`<-`) hits this.
  - Sealedness (`Sealed`) and the implementor registry (`SealedImpls`) are SEPARATE
    facts: `implements` clauses also bind ordinary interfaces, and CheckImplements
    short-circuits sealed ones — do not unify the two maps.
  - Implementors are stored as `*T` so the registry value equals both the type-switch
    `case` label render and the type-pattern type string — exhaustiveness compares
    rendered strings directly, no extra normalization.
  - CAP-3c is now unblocked: same-package sealed match works; the remaining gap is
    propagating SealedImpls across .goal packages (extend the SEAM-CAP-2 foreign
    goal-source reading path, which today projects enums only). SEAM-004 (seal AST +
    convert ~43 type-switches) depends on 3c.

  - Cross-package sealed match ALREADY lowered before this story: the backend sealedMatch
    path is dispatched by isSealedMatch(m) (pattern-SHAPE only — any TypePattern arm) and
    renders `case *pkg.T:` directly from the pattern type, so it never consulted the
    registry. CAP-3c is therefore PURELY a sema resolution/exhaustiveness fix (project the
    foreign implementor set); no emitter change was needed.
  - The foreign-enrichment registry key must match typeString of the consumer's pattern:
    qualifyForeignType("*Lit","shape") == "*shape.Lit" == typeString(*shape.Lit pattern), so
    sealedInterfaceOf compares rendered strings with no extra normalization. Same precedent
    SEAM-CAP-2 used for enum field types — reuse qualifyForeignType, don't hand-qualify.
  - foreignDecls/goalForeignDecls now return 6 values (structs,funcs,methods,enums,sealed,err);
    the .go path returns nil for `sealed` by design (the real bootstrap resolves siblings to
    .goal SOURCE, so the goal-source path is the one exercised) — mirror BOTH copies or the
    selfhost port gate fails to compile (it caught every transient signature drift here).
---

## 2026-06-29T23:59:00Z - SEAM-CAP-3d
- Implemented NESTED sealed-interface hierarchies (CAP-3 part 4 of 4, the FINAL SEAM-004
  prerequisite): a concrete type declared `implements B` where sealed B embeds sealed A now
  registers as an implementor of BOTH A and B and emits BOTH markers (isB() and isA()). This
  is the 2-level AST topology SEAM-004 needs (ast.Expr/Stmt/Decl/Spec embed ast.Node);
  CAP-3a/b/c only proved FLAT single-level sealed interfaces.
- Design choice: EMBEDDING CASCADE (option b), NOT a multi-interface `implements B, A`
  clause. Cascade mirrors Go's own interface embedding and needs NO parser change; the
  multi-clause form would require new grammar + restate by hand what embedding expresses.
- Fix (mirrored line-for-line internal/ + selfhost/):
  1. sema (resolve.go/.goal): cascadeSealedImpls propagates a sealed iface's implementors to
     every sealed interface it TRANSITIVELY embeds (via the already-populated
     info.EmbeddedIfaces — a sealed interface body shares resolveInterfaceMethods with an
     ordinary interface, so `sealed interface B { A }` yields EmbeddedIfaces[B]=[A]), gated
     on info.Sealed. Run at tail of Resolve(f) (single-file backend.Transpile path) AND tail
     of ResolvePackage after the merge loop (cross-file hierarchies). Idempotent
     (addImplementor dedups). Helpers sealedEmbedClosure/collectSealedEmbeds use plain
     recursion (NO closure — selfhost has no recursive-closure precedent).
  2. backend (lower.go+emit.go / .goal): sealedEmbeds (transitive embedded-sealed set,
     source order, deduped) + implementsMarker emits a marker per embedded sealed iface.
- Cross-package needed NO change: goalForeignDecls (CAP-3c) projects info.Sealed +
  info.SealedImpls from the defining package's ResolvePackage, which now cascades BEFORE
  projection. SEAM-004's AST is one package anyway.
- Files: internal/sema/resolve.go, internal/backend/{lower,emit}.go, selfhost/sema/resolve.goal,
  selfhost/backend/{lower,emit}.goal, internal/sema/nested_sealed_test.go (new),
  internal/backend/nested_sealed_test.go (new), DECISIONS.md, prd.json, progress.txt,
  history/20260629-feature-seam-cap-3d-nested-sealed-hierarchies/.
- Gates: task check green (incl. selfhost port gate + corpus), task build clean, task
  fixpoint = FIXPOINT OK (stage1==stage2). Corpus behavioral unchanged (additive tests).
- Learnings for future iterations (carry into SEAM-004):
  - EmbeddedIfaces is ALREADY populated for sealed interfaces (shared resolveInterfaceMethods),
    so a nested-hierarchy cascade needs no new tracking — just walk it gated on Sealed.
  - A concrete type carries ONE `implements` clause -> the cascade is the ONLY thing making
    it satisfy an embedded sealed interface. Without the backend marker cascade, emitted Go
    fails `go build` "missing method isA"; without the sema registry cascade, a match over
    the EMBEDDED interface (A) silently drops the cascaded implementors (broken exhaustiveness).
  - Fixpoint stayed byte-identical because selfhost has NO nested sealed hierarchy yet
    (SEAM-004 introduces it); cascade adds nothing + sealedEmbeds is empty for flat cases.
    Map-iteration order in the cascade never reaches emitted Go (SealedImpls order is sema
    metadata; marker order follows source-ordered EmbeddedIfaces).
  - selfhost mirror discipline: avoid recursive closures (`var walk func(...)`); use a
    plain recursive helper threading (seen, accumulator). The port gate compiles .goal as Go
    and the PostToolUse task-check hook catches any signature/helper drift immediately.
  - SEAM-004 is now FULLY unblocked: CAP-3a (sealed method sigs) + CAP-3b (same-pkg match) +
    CAP-3c (cross-pkg match) + CAP-3d (nested hierarchy) cover every capability the AST seal
    needs.

## 2026-06-29T23:59:59Z - SEAM-004
- Sealed the AST: selfhost/ast Node/Expr/Stmt/Decl/Spec are now `sealed interface`s
  (Node carries Pos()/End(); Expr/Stmt/Decl/Spec each `{ Node }`). Every concrete node
  type declares `implements <Category>` (CAP-3d cascade emits both isCat()+isNode());
  Node-only support types (Field, FieldList, File, DocComment, Variant, PayloadField,
  MatchArm, ImplementsClause) declare `implements Node`. Old marker methods deleted.
- Converted ~25 type-switches over a single sealed AST interface to goal `match` with
  exhaustiveness across selfhost/sema (check, resolve, question, fields, mustuse,
  assert), selfhost/backend (lower, emit), selfhost/parser (parser, goal_construct).
- KEPT PLAIN (documented in DECISIONS.md + inline): ast/walk.goal Walk (60-arm, grouped
  multi-type + no-op clauses; AC-permitted exclusion); backend/emit.goal armBody (cases
  over SIBLING interfaces ast.Stmt/ast.Expr, not variants of one); sema/foreign.goal ×3
  (over go/ast stdlib, unsealable). go/ast-mirror oracle RESOLVED by retaining the
  mirror unchanged — internal/ast tests reference no marker methods, so they pass
  against both open internal/ast and the sealed selfhost transpile.
- PREREQUISITE BUG FIXED (was a ~50%/run flake the real nested AST exposed):
  sema.sealedInterfaceOf resolved a sealed match's interface by first-map-hit over one
  arm type, nondeterministic when a type is in several sealed sets via the cascade
  (every *ast.Expr is also under ast.Node). Now resolves to the MOST SPECIFIC sealed
  interface (smallest implementor set, ties by name) containing ALL covered arm types.
  Mirrored internal/sema/check.go + selfhost/sema/check.goal. Call site passes `covered`.
- Files: selfhost/ast/{ast,goal_decl,goal_expr,goal_stmt,walk}.goal,
  selfhost/sema/{check,resolve,question,fields,mustuse,assert}.goal,
  selfhost/backend/{lower,emit}.goal, selfhost/parser/{parser,goal_construct}.goal,
  internal/sema/check.go, DECISIONS.md, prd.json (passes via orchestrator), progress.txt.
- Gates: task check, task build, task fixpoint (FIXPOINT OK) all green; full go test ./...
  run twice clean; corpus behavioral + interp tiers unchanged; no golden regen needed
  (goldens test the internal/ Go compiler, not selfhost/).
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - A plain type-switch over a sealed interface is NOT rejected by sema, so the seal and
    the switch->match conversions can land incrementally; every committed state still
    built. (The §9 rule is enforced only against `match` exhaustiveness, not switches.)
  - sealed match arm lowering only ALIASES a USED binding to the type-switch guard (no
    `b := v.(*T)` is emitted), so an unused arm binding never causes declared-and-not-used
    — and a no-binding type pattern (`*RestPattern =>`) is valid.
  - A value-returning type-switch becomes a STATEMENT-position match with `return` inside
    each arm block (avoids value-position match constraints). A `case nil:` is hoisted to
    an `if x == nil` guard before the match (no nil type pattern exists).
  - A switch over SIBLING category interfaces (`case ast.Stmt:`/`case ast.Expr:`) cannot
    be a `match` (match patterns are concrete *T) — keep it a plain type-switch.
  - Nested sealed hierarchies make a type belong to multiple sealed sets; any
    arm-type->interface resolver MUST disambiguate by the covered set (smallest superset),
    or it is nondeterministic under map iteration.

  each file vs its fix output): 12 result-sig skips (refusals) + 14 call-site
  suggestions (advisory), every one mapping to a SEAM-005 documented non-fit or the
  command boundary. The autofixer agrees the propagating API is idiomatic.
- META-finding (the central result): the deep idioms were blocked not just by
  per-package scope but by MISSING compiler features. Reaching this end state
  required FOUR new capabilities built in this PRD — SEAM-CAP (cross-package
  enum-match lowering), SEAM-CAP-2 (cross-.goal-package enum/sema-fact propagation),
  SEAM-CAP-3a-d (sealed-interface type-pattern match: method-sig preservation,
  same-package, cross-.goal-package, nested hierarchies). Before this work a
  cross-package enum match errored and sealed-interface match did not exist.
- Files: DECISIONS.md (new "SEAM-006" section: per-seam tally, honest end state,

  measured end state), prd.json (SEAM-006 passes:true), progress.txt,
  history/20260629-feature-seam-006-cross-cutting-proof/.
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - The seam proof is measurable with grep: `^\s*\*Type(x)? =>` counts type-pattern
    arms (sealed matches); `enum ` counts enum decls; `Result[` in func sigs counts
    lifted APIs; diff each file vs `goal fix <file>` stdout to prove zero auto-fixes.
  - `goal fix <dir>` reports only the entry file's reports cleanly; iterate per-file
    over `find selfhost -name '*.goal'` to get the full residual list. Reports are
    "skipped" (refused, no change) or "suggestion" (advisory) — neither is an
    auto-applied conversion, so a tree with only those = autofixer-idiomatic.
  - ./bin/goal is the full CLI (build|run|check|fix|fmt|ai|lsp); ./bin/goal-c-1/-c-2
    are the bootstrap selfhost binaries with only `build --emit`.

## 2026-06-30T17:09:00Z - US-004
- Added `task verify-generated`, a drift gate that re-emits the goal compiler
  source to a scratch tree (_bootstrap/verify), prepends the SAME fixed
  generated header `task generate` uses, then two-way `diff -r -x '*.goal'`
  against the committed internal/compiler tree. Wired it into `task check`
  (between vet and test) so the universal pre-commit gate fails on any drift
  between committed generated Go and the .goal source.
- Files changed: Taskfile.yml (new verify-generated target + check wiring),
  prd.json (US-004 passes:true), progress.txt. Committed 94808d6.
- Verification: verify-generated EXIT 0 on the clean tree ("generated Go is up
  to date"); appended a marker to internal/compiler/token/token.go -> EXIT
  non-zero with diff printed, then reverted; `task check` EXIT 0 and its log
  shows verify-generated ran inside it; `task fixpoint` "FIXPOINT OK".
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - The drift gate works because emit is deterministic and the header is a fixed
    literal (US-003). `diff -r -x '*.goal'` is two-way: it catches changed,
    added, AND removed generated .go (not just edits), and the `-x '*.goal'`
    excludes the colocated source so the regenerated .go-only tree compares
    cleanly against the committed .goal+.go tree.
  - The PostToolUse `task check` hook now runs verify-generated on EVERY edit.
    Consequence for later port stories (US-006+): after editing a *.goal source
    you MUST run `task generate` to refresh the colocated .go before the next
    edit, or the hook's verify-generated will (correctly) fail on the stale .go.
    Order an in-flight refactor so generate runs before check sees it green.
  - `task clean` already removes _bootstrap, so the verify scratch dir
    (_bootstrap/verify) needs no separate cleanup target; the task rm -rf's it
    on success and clean covers a failed mid-run.

## [2026-06-30T19:08:00Z] - US-012 (self-host-flip PRD)
- Ported the interpreter's expression EVALUATOR (internal/interp/eval.go, 1177
  LOC) to goal source: internal/compiler/interp/eval.goal (the real evalExpr +
  evalMatch/evalUnwrap/evalCompositeLit/evalSelector/evalVariantLit/evalIndex/
  evalCall/evalBinary/evalUnary/builtins/...). `task generate` emits colocated
  eval.go; `go build ./internal/compiler/interp/...` and `go vet` are green.
- THREE behavior-preserving rewrites were needed (eval.go is NOT a clean
  plain-Go-superset, unlike the US-011 value/env/host/assert files):
  1. `enum` is a goal RESERVED word but eval.go uses it as a local var of type
     *sema.Enum (13 sites). Renamed the IDENTIFIER only -> `enumDecl`. CRITICAL:
     the word "enum" also appears inside error-message STRING literals ("unknown
     enum %s", "enum %s has no variant") and must NOT be renamed there. Use
     delimiter-anchored seds (`enum.` / `enum, ` / `enum *sema.Enum` / `enum ==`)
     that match the identifier's syntactic context but never the strings. Do NOT
     use `\b` in sed on macOS — BSD sed silently ignores `\b` (it no-ops, looks
     like success). Use the trailing-delimiter trick or `[[:<:]]`/`[[:>:]]`.
  2. sema.Mode comparisons: the ported internal/compiler/sema models Mode as a
     goal `enum`, which the backend lowers to a SEALED INTERFACE
     (sema.Mode_ModeResult, ...). So eval.go's `sig.Mode == sema.ModeResult`
     CONSTANT comparisons do not compile. Rewrote them to type-assertion
     predicates: `func isModeResult(m sema.Mode) bool { _, ok :=
     m.(sema.Mode_ModeResult); return ok }` (+ isModeResultClosed/isModeOption),
     EXACTLY the idiom internal/compiler/fix already uses. goal SOURCE accepts the
     emitted underscore variant name `sema.Mode_ModeResult` as a type-assertion
     target (proven by fix.goal). Same pattern is in progress.txt's Patterns block.
  3. eval.goal now imports sema (legacy interp's value/env/host/assert did NOT),
     so the interp package's transpile/build dep graph GREW: token, lexer, ast,
     parser, sema, cap (was just token/ast/cap in US-011). The selfhost port test
     layout/deps had to add lexer/parser/sema.
- SKELETON EXPANSION (interp.goal): deleted the US-011 placeholder evalExpr (the
  real one is now in eval.goal); grew the Interp struct from 3 fields to the full
  set (file/info/root/methods/imports/derives/fnStack/caps/stdout); added the real
  control-signal type returnSignal (eval.goal's propagateErr/propagateNone CONSTRUCT
  it) next to panicSignal; and added loud-refusal PLACEHOLDERS for the US-013
  driver symbols eval.goal calls but does not define: methods callFunc, callMethod,
  sigFor, curSig, evalDerive, and package funcs selectMatchArm, unreachableMatch,
  armScopeFor. US-013 MUST delete every placeholder and fold in (not re-declare)
  Interp/returnSignal/panicSignal/CapabilityError/emitStdout.
- AC-2 behavioral gate: new internal/interp/eval_subset_test.go — a DRIVER-FREE
  white-box test that builds a bare `&Interp{}` and a fresh `NewEnv()` scope and
  drives parsed expressions straight through the real evalExpr (the
  arithmetic/comparison/logical/short-circuit/unary/error matrix from eval_test.go).
  It deliberately avoids New/findMain/Run/ip.root (US-013 driver), so it runs at
  the US-012 checkpoint. It runs BOTH against the legacy package (under `task
  check`) AND against the goal-built package (internal/selfhost
  TestPortedInterpPackage, extended with sema/lexer/parser deps + this file). Use
  UNIQUE test/helper names (subsetExprOf/subsetEval/TestEvalSubset*) — eval_test.go
  already defines exprOf/evalProgram/TestEval* in the same package.
- Files changed: internal/compiler/interp/{eval.goal,eval.go (generated),
  interp.goal,interp.go (generated)} (eval.* new), internal/interp/
  eval_subset_test.go (new), internal/selfhost/port_test.go
  (TestPortedInterpPackage layout/deps/testFiles + doc), prd.json (US-012
  passes:true), progress.txt.
- Verification: `go build ./internal/compiler/interp/...` OK; go vet OK;
  TestPortedInterpPackage PASS (transpile-and-build gate + value/env/eval-subset
  behavioral gate); `task check` GREEN (vet + verify-generated drift gate + full
  test incl. legacy eval_subset_test.go parity); `task fixpoint` FIXPOINT OK.
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - US-013 (port interp.go -> interp.goal, derive.go -> derive.goal) DELETES all
    of interp.goal's US-013 placeholders and folds in the real driver. The eval
    package will then evaluate WHOLE programs, so US-013's gate can use the legacy
    eval_test.go / control_test.go / call_test.go etc. (which need New/Run).

    selfhost port_test layout AND deps maps both need the new dep and its

    goal/internal/compiler/<dep> is not in std".

## [2026-06-30T20:30:00Z] - US-014 (self-host-flip PRD)
- Spike: proved goal SOURCE can express the concurrency the lsp port (US-015..017)
  needs — goroutines + sync.Mutex — before committing to the ~2292 LOC port. The
  backend already EMITTED go/chan/select (token GO/CHAN/SELECT, ast.GoStmt,
  parser.parseCallStmt(token.GO)/parseChanType/parseSelectStmt), but no goal source
  had ever USED concurrency (the compiler is single-threaded).
- Probe: features/_spikes/lsp-concurrency/{main.goal,go.mod,README.md}. main.goal
  launches 8 goroutines (`go func(){...}()`), each doing 1000 sync.Mutex-guarded
  increments of a shared counter synchronized with sync.WaitGroup, prints the total.
  Built+run via the REAL toolchain (`go build -o bin/goal ./cmd/goal && ./bin/goal
  run features/_spikes/lsp-concurrency`) -> prints 8000, deterministic across runs.
  A supporting buffered-channel probe (make(chan int,4)+goroutine send+close+range)
  printed 10. Emitted Go is a VERBATIM lowering (go func(){}(), var mu sync.Mutex,
  mu.Lock()/Unlock(), wg.Add/Done/Wait) — no goal-specific rewriting; sync/fmt are
  ordinary foreign stdlib imports.
- Outcome recorded in DECISIONS.md ("US-014 — lsp concurrency spike"): NO blocking
  capability gap; US-015 may proceed. JSON-RPC-over-stdio framing is US-015 scope
  (ordinary io/bufio/encoding/json, not a language capability).
- Files changed: features/_spikes/lsp-concurrency/{main.goal,go.mod,README.md} (new),
  DECISIONS.md (new entry), prd.json (US-014 passes:true), progress.txt.
- Verification: `./bin/goal run features/_spikes/lsp-concurrency` -> 8000 (x3);
  `task check` exit 0; `task fixpoint` FIXPOINT OK (exit 0).
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - To run a one-off goal program through the toolchain, `goal run <dir>` needs a
    go.mod at <dir> or a parent (it overlays the transpiled Go onto that module and
    `go run`s the sole main pkg). Absent go.mod -> "go.mod file not found".
  - Park non-production goal programs under an UNDERSCORE-prefixed dir
    (features/_spikes/, like the existing features/_cut/): Go ignores `_`-prefixed
    and nested-module dirs for `go build/test/vet ./...`, and anything outside
    internal/compiler is invisible to generate/verify-generated/bootstrap/fixpoint
    (all scoped to ./internal/compiler), so such a probe touches NO gate.
  - Concurrency in goal source is FREE: go/chan/select/sync are plain-Go-superset
    constructs already handled by lexer/parser/ast/backend. The lsp port (US-015+)
    can use sync.Mutex + goroutines directly with no new compiler capability.
  - `morse-code workflow next` PAUSES at human-review gates ("paused: awaiting human
    review"); in automode advance past them with `morse-code workflow resume` (NOT
    --reject, which routes to on_fail). Status via `morse-code workflow status`.

  consts + legend), jsonrpc.goal (Content-Length framing readMessage/writeMessage

  AC-1 names; the rest of legacy internal/lsp (server/symbols/codeaction/hover/
  definition/references/diagnostics/semantictokens) is US-016/US-017.
- This subset is a LEAF package: NO in-module (goal/internal/*) imports, only
  foreign stdlib (bufio/encoding/json/fmt/io/strconv/strings/sync/net/url/
  path/filepath). Ported VERBATIM (Go superset = valid goal); no idiom rewrite.
  No goal reserved-word collisions — `match`/`enum`/`assert` appear ONLY inside a
  comment ("must match") and a string literal ("enum"), both harmless.
- `task generate` (scoped to ./internal/compiler) auto-discovered the new lsp
  package with NO Taskfile edit (same as interp in US-011..013) and emitted
  colocated internal/compiler/lsp/{protocol,jsonrpc,uri}.go with the generated
  header; `go build ./internal/compiler/lsp/...` + `go vet` clean.
- AC-2 parity oracle: added TestPortedLspPackage to internal/selfhost/port_test.go
  following the leaf-package shape of TestPortedCap/Textedit but with foreign
  stdlib imports. BuildTranspiled(layout={internal/compiler/lsp}) is the compile
  gate; BuildAndTest(... ,nil deps) feeds the legacy white-box ../lsp/jsonrpc_test.go
  (TestFramingRoundTrip = encode-then-decode preserves method+params;
  TestReadMessageMissingLength) and ../lsp/uri_test.go (TestURIToPath). The
  identical files run against the legacy package under `task check`, so they are
  the same-input same-output oracle.
- Files changed: internal/compiler/lsp/{protocol,jsonrpc,uri}.{goal,go} (new),
  internal/selfhost/port_test.go (+TestPortedLspPackage), prd.json (US-015
  passes:true), progress.txt.
- Verification: go build ./internal/compiler/lsp OK; go vet OK; TestPortedLspPackage
  PASS; `task check` exit 0 (vet + verify-generated drift gate + full test);
  `task fixpoint` FIXPOINT OK.
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - When an AC names a SPECIFIC file set ("ports protocol.go, jsonrpc.go, uri.go"),
    port exactly that subset even though the legacy package has many more files —
    the remaining files belong to later stories (US-016/017). A partial-package
    port compiles standalone as long as the ported files + their fed-in tests
    reference no symbol from the un-ported files (Go does NOT error on unused
    package-level type/const/var/func decls, only unused imports + locals). Verify
    by inspection before copying.
  - Concurrency carried over for FREE (jsonrpc.writeMessage takes *sync.Mutex):
    confirms the US-014 spike finding — sync.Mutex is plain foreign-stdlib
    passthrough, no compiler capability needed.
  - A ported leaf with FOREIGN stdlib imports (vs cap/textedit which had none)
    still uses the nil-deps BuildAndTest path; the foreign imports pass through the
    throwaway temp `module goal` unchanged.

## [2026-06-30T20:29:00Z] - US-016 (self-host-flip PRD)
- Ported the LSP server loop + lifecycle handlers to goal source under
  internal/compiler/lsp: server.goal (the readMessage loop, handle() dispatch,
  didOpen/didChange/didClose, reply/replyNull/replyError/notify/write, NewServer/
  NewServerWithIO/osDirReader), symbols.goal (documentSymbol outline), codeaction.goal
  (the source.fixAll.goal idiomatize action via fix.File). These are exactly the
  three files US-016 AC-1 names.
- KEY: server.goal's dispatch references 8 handlers + the openFile type that live in
  US-017 files (diagnostics: compile/publish/openFilesInDir/openFile; query features:
  definition/hover/references/rename/semanticTokens). Go requires every referenced
  symbol to be DEFINED for the package to compile, so a partial port that calls into
  un-ported files does NOT build standalone (unlike US-015's transport subset, which
  referenced nothing forward). Bridged with us017_stubs.goal: inert stubs with the
  exact legacy signatures returning zero values. They satisfy AC-1's `go build` gate
  without changing the handshake (which never reaches them). US-017 DELETES
  us017_stubs.goal when it lands the real diagnostics/definition/hover/references/
  semantictokens ports.
- enum-drift recurrence (3rd time, see Codebase Patterns): symbols.goal's legacy
  `switch decl.Mod { case ast.FuncFrom: ... case ast.FuncDerive: ... }` does NOT
  transpile — the ported internal/compiler/ast models FuncMod as a goal `enum` that
  lowers to a sealed interface (ast.FuncMod_FuncFrom/_FuncDerive structs). Rewrote to
  `switch decl.Mod.(type) { case ast.FuncMod_FuncFrom: ... }`. The build error surfaces
  at `go build` (undefined: ast.FuncFrom), NOT at transpile time — the goal backend
  emits the .go from .goal regardless, so always `go build ./internal/compiler/<pkg>/...`
  after `task generate`, never trust a clean generate alone.
- The lsp package is NO LONGER A LEAF after US-016: server imports project+sema,
  symbols imports ast/parser/token, codeaction imports fix. So BuildTranspiled (which
  compiles the WHOLE package dir) needs the full closure {token,lexer,ast,parser,sema,
  project,textedit,fix}. This BROKE the existing US-015 TestPortedLspPackage (layout was
  {lsp} alone) — adding source files to a ported package can break a sibling gate, so
  re-run the package's OTHER self-host gates after a port. Extracted an lspClosure(t)
  helper (discovers the closure once) and widened TestPortedLspPackage's layout+deps;
  added TestPortedLspServer using the same helper.
- AC-2 oracle: internal/lsp/server_handshake_test.go (new, package lsp) scripts
  initialize -> initialized -> shutdown -> exit through NewServer and pins the
  capability advertisement (textDocumentSync:1, documentSymbolProvider,
  source.fixAll.goal, semanticTokensProvider, definition/hover/references/rename
  providers, serverInfo goal-lsp/0.1.0) + the `"result":null` shutdown reply. Own
  `frameMsg` helper (server_test.go already defines `frame`, would clash in package
  lsp). It runs against the legacy package under `task check` AND is fed to
  TestPortedLspServer.BuildAndTest against the goal-built package — the same-input
  same-output handshake parity. The didOpen->publishDiagnostics path
  (TestServerPublishesDiagnosticsOnOpen) is NOT gated here: it needs the real
  compile/publish that US-017 (diagnostics) ports; stubbed compile would fail it.
- Files changed: internal/compiler/lsp/{server,symbols,codeaction,us017_stubs}.{goal,go}
  (new), internal/lsp/server_handshake_test.go (new), internal/selfhost/port_test.go
  (lspClosure helper + widened TestPortedLspPackage + new TestPortedLspServer),
  prd.json (US-016 passes:true), progress.txt.
- Verification: go build ./internal/compiler/lsp OK; TestServerHandshakeScript PASS
  (legacy); TestPortedLspPackage + TestPortedLspServer PASS (goal-built); `task check`
  green (vet + verify-generated drift gate + full test); `task fixpoint` FIXPOINT OK.
  Commit 323c3d4.
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - When a story ports the file that DISPATCHES to handlers ported in a LATER story,
    the package can't build standalone — stub the forward-deps (exact signatures, zero
    returns) in a clearly-named bridge file the later story deletes. This is the only
    way to honor an AC that says "ports <subset> AND generates .go that builds" when
    the subset isn't self-contained.
  - Adding source files to an already-ported package can break that package's OTHER
    self-host gates (a leaf becomes a non-leaf). After any port, run ALL of the
    package's self-host gates, not just the new one (`go test ./internal/selfhost
    -run 'TestPortedLsp'`).

## [2026-06-30T21:40:00Z] - US-017 (self-host-flip PRD)
- Ported the LSP query features (legacy internal/lsp hover.go, definition.go,
  references.go, diagnostics.go, semantictokens.go) verbatim to goal source under
  internal/compiler/lsp/*.goal and DELETED the US-016 forward-dep bridge
  us017_stubs.{goal,go}: the five ported files now SUPPLY the real openFile type +
  compile/publish/openFilesInDir/definition/hover/references/rename/semanticTokens
  symbols the stub file had inerted. This completes the lsp port and Phase 2.
- Port mechanics = the established recipe: cp legacy .go -> .goal, sed-repoint
  `goal/internal/` -> `goal/internal/compiler/`, `task generate`, then ALWAYS
  `go build ./internal/compiler/lsp/...` (enum-drift surfaces at build, not generate).
- TWO drift fixes were required (both predicted by grepping the 5 files first):
  - sema.Severity sealed-interface drift (4th occurrence, see Codebase Patterns):
    diagnostics.goal's `if d.Severity == sema.Warning` does not compile against the
    ported sema (Severity is an enum -> sealed interface Severity_Error/_Warning, no
    comparable consts). Rewrote to a comma-ok assertion:
    `if _, ok := d.Severity.(sema.Severity_Warning); ok`.
  - goal reserved word `enum` used as an IDENTIFIER: the refVariant PARAMETER
    `enum ast.Expr` (definition/hover/references) -> `enumExpr`; and in references.goal
    the symKey STRUCT FIELD `enum string` + its 3 struct-literal sites
    (`enum: en`/`enum: id.Name`) -> `enumName`. Comments/strings containing the word
    `enum` are harmless (only bare identifiers collide).
  - rangeOf was already ported in symbols.goal (US-016); definition/references just
    CALL it — do NOT redefine (would be a duplicate-decl build error).
- AC-2 parity oracle: internal/lsp/features_parity_test.go (package lsp, NEW). One
  self-contained file driving all five features via the public/white-box surface
  (resolveHover/resolveDefinition/computeSemanticTokens directly; references/rename
  via s.references/s.rename after feeding initialize+didOpen and letting EOF end Run;
  diagnostics via didOpen with an `untitled:` URI -> compileSingle -> publish, no
  filesystem). Every assertion is DERIVED from the fixture (offsets resolved at
  runtime, fp* helper prefix to avoid clashing with the other lsp test files), so the
  IDENTICAL file holds on BOTH the legacy package (`task check`) and the goal-built
  package (new TestPortedLspFeatures via BuildTranspiled+BuildAndTest) — that
  two-package agreement is the parity proof.
- WHY a fresh oracle instead of feeding the legacy feature *_test.go (US-016
  precedent): the legacy lsp test suite is a tightly-coupled white-box web AND two
  files touch drifted surface that cannot compile against the ported package:
  diagnostics_test.go uses sema.Error/sema.Warning value consts; references_test.go
  reads the renamed symKey.enum field; server_test.go depends on diagnostics_test's
  nonExhaustiveSrc; and hover/definition/references/semantictokens tests share
  helpers (offsetOfNth/cursorAt in definition_test, testServer/fakeResolver in
  package_test, frame in server_test). Untangling that web is far more fragile than
  one derived-assertion oracle. The legacy tests stay UNTOUCHED under `task check`.
- lspClosure (US-016) needed NO change: the ported query files import only
  ast/parser/sema/project/token/lexer, all already in the closure. Re-ran ALL three
  lsp gates (TestPortedLspPackage/Server/Features) — all green (a port can break a
  sibling gate, so never run only the new one).
- Files changed: internal/compiler/lsp/{diagnostics,definition,hover,references,
  semantictokens}.{goal,go} (new), internal/compiler/lsp/us017_stubs.{goal,go}
  (deleted), internal/lsp/features_parity_test.go (new), internal/selfhost/port_test.go
  (+TestPortedLspFeatures), prd.json (US-017 passes:true), progress.txt.
- Verification: `task generate` + `go build ./internal/compiler/lsp/...` OK;
  go test ./internal/lsp -run Parity (7 PASS, legacy); go test ./internal/selfhost
  -run TestPortedLsp (Package/Server/Features all PASS, goal-built); `task check`
  EXIT 0 (vet + verify-generated drift gate + full test); `task fixpoint` FIXPOINT OK.
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - When porting a package whose legacy white-box tests consume drifted surface
    (sealed-interface enums) or renamed reserved-word identifiers, do NOT try to feed
    them through BuildAndTest. Write ONE self-contained parity oracle with assertions
    DERIVED from the fixture (not pinned magic numbers) so the same file is valid
    against both the legacy and the goal-built package — the cross-package agreement
    IS the parity proof. Query a server handler directly by feeding initialize+didOpen
    and letting EOF return Run (docs persist; didClose not sent), then call the
    unexported handler with json.Marshal'd params.
  - Force the single-file diagnostics path (no filesystem) with a non-`file:` URI
    (e.g. `untitled:`): uriToPath fails -> compileSingle -> sema.Analyze -> publish.

## 2026-06-30T21:10:00Z - US-018
- Repointed every cmd/* import of a ported package from goal/internal/<pkg> to
  goal/internal/compiler/<pkg>, so the shipped goal & goalc binaries (and the
  dev tools) run on the goal-sourced compiler. Start of Phase 3 (the flip).
- Files changed:
  - cmd/goal/main.go: 11 imports (backend, fix, goalfmt, guide, interp, lsp,
    parser, pipeline, project, sema, typecheck) -> compiler/*; severity drift
    fixes at lines 532 and 631.
  - cmd/goalc/main.go: backend, sema -> compiler/*; severity drift fix at l.78.
  - cmd/goal-wasm/main_wasm.go: backend -> compiler/backend.
  - cmd/build-playground/main.go: backend -> compiler/backend (byexample stays).
  - prd.json (US-018 passes:true), progress.txt.
  - cmd/corpus-gen NOT touched (only Go-only internal/corpus).
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - sema.Severity drift bites the CONSUMERS too, not just ports: the legacy
    internal/sema.Severity is a comparable int (sema.Error/sema.Warning with a
    String() method); the compiler port internal/compiler/sema.Severity is a
    sealed interface (Severity_Error{}/Severity_Warning{}, no consts, no
    String()). When repointing any caller, (1) `x == sema.Error` ->
    `_, ok := x.(sema.Severity_Error); ok`, and (2) `%s`/fmt of a Severity ->
    `sema.SeverityLabel(x)` (returns the same "error"/"warning", so rendered
    output stays byte-identical — parity-safe). Grep callers for
    `sema\.(Error|Warning)\b` and `%[sv].*[Ss]everity` before repointing.
  - An identity type conversion survives the drift: cmd/goal:594
    `sema.Severity(d.Severity)` still compiles because compiler/typecheck
    .Diagnostic.Severity is ALREADY compiler/sema.Severity (T(x) where x is T is
    a valid no-op conversion). Don't "fix" these — they're inert.
  - Repoint ALL of a single binary's ported imports together so its type graph
    stays single-sourced (no legacy+compiler type mixing within one binary).
    Dev tools whose unported deps (byexample) don't share types with the ported
    dep (backend) are safe to repoint piecemeal.
  - Cheap, decisive parity oracle for a flip: build the pre-edit binary first
    (working tree is the baseline), then diff old-vs-new stdout+stderr+exit code
    over a corpus/feature sweep. goalc covers transpile+doctest+check; `goal
    check <dir>` additionally exercises AnalyzePackageInDir + the severity-render
    path. wasm cmd carries //go:build js && wasm so it's excluded from host
    ./... — verify it with `GOOS=js GOARCH=wasm go build ./cmd/goal-wasm`.

## 2026-06-30T22:10:00Z - US-020
- Promoted the goal compiler from its transition home internal/compiler/<pkg> to
  the final internal/<pkg> layout. git-mv'd all 16 package dirs (ast, backend,
  cap, fix, goalfmt, guide, interp, lexer, lsp, parser, pipeline, project, sema,
  textedit, token, typecheck) plus the root entrypoint main.go/main.goal (now at
  internal/main.{go,goal}). Rewrote every Go import + goal self-import
  goal/internal/compiler/<pkg> -> goal/internal/<pkg> across 136 source files,
  and the stale code/build comments, so no 'internal/compiler' path remains in
  code/Taskfile (only .md docs, which are US-021's scope).
- Updated Taskfile generate/verify-generated/bootstrap/fixpoint to ./internal.
  The compiler `main` package now lives at internal/ itself, so bootstrap builds
  `go build ./internal` and emit discovers the .goal packages under ./internal.
- Files changed: 138 git renames (internal/compiler/** -> internal/**) carrying
  both .goal + regenerated .go; Taskfile.yml; cmd/{goal,goalc,goal-wasm,
  build-playground,goal-gen}/main.go imports; internal/corpus/* + internal/
  selfhost/selfhost.go(+_test) imports; internal/selfhost/selfhost.go (dropped a
  now-no-op ReplaceAll of goal/internal/ test imports); prd.json (US-020
  passes:true); progress.txt.
- Verification: task generate; task check EXIT 0 (vet + verify-generated drift
  gate + full test incl. corpus behavioral tier + selfhost); task fixpoint
  FIXPOINT OK (goal-c-1 vs goal-c-2 byte-identical); go build ./... and
  GOOS=js GOARCH=wasm go build ./cmd/goal-wasm green.
- Learnings for future iterations:
  - Do NOT hand-sed the COMMITTED generated .go for an import-path rename: sed
    rewrites the path in place but does NOT re-sort the import block, and the
    backend emits imports gofmt-sorted, so a renamed path that changes sort
    position (US-020: goal/internal/compiler/backend -> goal/internal/backend now
    sorts BEFORE the unchanged goal/internal/byexample in guide.go) drifts the
    committed .go from the regenerated .go and fails `task verify-generated`. Fix:
    sed the .goal source (and any siblings), then run `task generate` to
    re-emit ALL .go deterministically — that is the only authority for the
    committed .go. (The .goal import block order is cosmetic; the emitter sorts.)
  - When the generated-from-goal packages share internal/ with Go-only infra
    (byexample/corpus/selfhost have no .goal), a blanket
    `diff -r internal _bootstrap/verify/internal` drift gate FALSE-FAILS: the
    emit produces only the compiler packages, so the infra dirs show as
    "Only in internal". Scope the diff to exactly the emitted entries:
    `for entry in _bootstrap/verify/internal/*; do diff -r -x '*.goal'
    "internal/$(basename $entry)" "$entry"; done`. This still catches changed/
    added/removed generated files within each compiler package + the root main.go.
  - The compiler's `package main` root entrypoint (main.goal/main.go) promotes to
    internal/ itself (a package main directory whose siblings are the lib
    packages + Go-only infra). `goal build ./internal` discovers all .goal
    packages under it (infra skipped, no .goal); `go build ./internal` builds
    only the main package in that dir. Both work without a dedicated subdir.
